## Consolidated Gap Register

> **Reorganized 2026-06-14.** Resolved/closed items are collected under **✅ Done / Resolved**; the remaining open items are grouped by **revenue impact** (Direct → Growth → Core → Internal). Revenue tiering is a first-pass heuristic — adjust freely. The thematic feature write-ups are preserved verbatim under **📓 Archived thematic context**. Full audit trail: `git log`.
>
> **Stats — 341 register items:** ✅ 53 resolved · 🔓 288 open. Open by revenue impact → 💰 Direct 15 · 🚀 Growth 10 · 🛠️ Core 190 · 🧹 Internal 73.

### 🧵 Isolation Tracks — parallel agent assignment

Dispatch **one agent per track**. Tracks are **file-disjoint by construction**, so agents run in parallel without stepping on each other. An agent assigned a track edits **only** files under that track's _Owns_ paths, works **only** the open gaps whose primary file lives there, and draws migration numbers **only** from its reserved band. Anything outside its paths belongs to another track — use the shared-hub rules below, never edit cross-track.

| Track | Owns (primary paths) | Gap focus | Mig band |
|---|---|---|---|
| **T1 · Marketing & SEO Web** | `frontend/src/app/{page.tsx,compare,integrations,marketplace/[slug],product,agents,blog,pricing,projects/[id],sitemap.ts}` · `frontend/src/lib/{seo,content,structured-data,og,marketplaceSeo,blogData,routeMarketing}.*` · `frontend/src/components/{PublicShell,MarketingHeader,AppFooter,PageContainer,RouteMarketing,QuickStart,blog/*}` · `frontend/public/{robots.txt,install.*}` · routes `pendingPromptRoutes.ts` | 🚀 Growth | — |
| **T2 · App UI & Brain** | all other `frontend/src/{app,components}/**` · `frontend/src/lib/brain/**` · `brain-embedded/**` · route `dashboardRoutes.ts` | 🛠️ Core (UI/UX) | 0180–0189 |
| **T3 · Gateway & LLM** | `api/src/application/llm/**` · `api/src/infrastructure/cache/**` · route `llmRoutes.ts` | 💰 Direct + LLM Core/Internal | 0130–0139 |
| **T4 · Cloud Runtime & PR loop** | `api/src/application/{runtime,repos}/**` · `api/src/infrastructure/relay/**` · routes `runtimeRoutes.ts`,`repoRoutes.ts`,`repoAnalysisRoutes.ts`,`taskRoutes.ts`,`agentRuntimeRoutes.ts` | 🛠️ Core (cloud agents) | 0140–0149 |
| **T5 · On-Prem Agent Runtime** | `agent-runtime/**` · `packages/**` | 🧹 Internal (engine/pi/tui) | — |
| **T6 · Studio & Voice** | `studio/**` · `studio-embedded/**` · `voice/**` · routes `studioVoiceCloneRoutes.ts`,`studioWeightRoutes.ts` · frontend `components/{LlmStudioPanel,VoiceClonePanel}`,`app/ide/voice` | 🛠️ Core (video/voice) | 0150–0159 |
| **T7 · Tenant · Embed · Governance** | `builderforce-embedded/**` · `frontend/src/{app,lib}/embed/**` · `api/src/application/seams/**` · `api/src/infrastructure/auth/segment*` · routes `tenant*`,`embedRoutes.ts`,`governanceRoutes.ts`,`segment*`,`seamRoutes.ts`,`webhookRoutes.ts`,`biRoutes.ts`,`mcpExtensionRoutes.ts`,`reportRoutes.ts` | 🛠️ Core + 🧹 Internal (multi-tenant) | 0160–0169 |
| **T8 · Workflows · Boards** | `api/src/application/{workflow,boardsync,swimlane}/**` · routes `workflow*`,`board*`,`integrationRoutes.ts`,`githubWebhookRoutes.ts` · frontend `components/workflow-builder/**`,`app/workflows/**` | 🛠️ Core (orchestration) | 0170–0179 |
| **T9 · Platform · DB · CI** _(steward)_ | `api/migrations/**` · `api/scripts/**` · `.github/workflows/**` · `frontend/eslint.config.js` · root tsconfig/lint · schema-drift allowlist | 🧹 Internal (migrations/drift/tests/lint) | 0190+ |
| **T10 · Docs & QA** | `docs-site/**` · `qa-e2e/**` · `api/src/application/qa/**` · route `qaRoutes.ts` · frontend `components/QaContent.tsx` | QA + docs | — |

**Shared hubs — append-only, never edit another track's block:**
- `api/src/infrastructure/database/schema.ts` — append new tables at the end; **T9 stewards** ordering + drift.
- `api/src/index.ts` — append route mounts only.
- `frontend/src/lib/builderforceApi.ts` — append API-client blocks only.
- `frontend/src/lib/content.ts` — **T1 owns**; other tracks request copy changes via T1.
- This **Consolidated Gap Register** — append entries; run the "organize + calculate gaps" pass only when no other agent is mid-edit (it rewrites section counts).

**Migration numbering is the one true serialization point** (duplicate numbers already bit us — see the `0109`/`0111` collision gap). Draw **only** from your band; **T9** issues any number outside a band. Next free single slot: **0129**.

**Run each track in its own git worktree + branch** (`git worktree add ../bf-T2 -b track/T2`). File-disjoint paths only prevent *merge* conflicts — pointing two agents at the **same working copy** still lets their edits interleave mid-run (and a shared `tsc`/`pnpm` build clobbers). One worktree per track = one branch per track = truly parallel; merge the branches back when each track lands. Track boundaries are **convention, not enforced** — an agent that ignores its _Owns_ scope can still stray (the durable fix is a CI/pre-commit guard that rejects a branch touching files outside its declared track — logged in the register).

**Dispatch example:** _"Agent A → T1 (Growth) · Agent B → T3 (Gateway/Direct) · Agent C → T9 (Internal/DB),"_ each in its own worktree/branch. Three agents, zero file overlap.


### 🔓 Newly logged (open)

- 🧹 **Internal (test isolation) — `getOrSetCached`'s module-global L1 `Map` is never reset between tests, making cache-backed tests order-dependent.** Surfaced by the CI failure in [cloudMemory.test.ts](api/src/application/runtime/cloudMemory.test.ts): the `recall clamps the limit` test populated L1 key `am:recall:1:0:5:q` with `[]`, and the later `degrades to {ok:false}` test reused the same tenant/query/limit, getting an L1 hit (`ok:true`) instead of running the failing loader. Fixed in this pass by giving the degrade test an isolated tenant (99) + unique query (cold cache). Durable fix unblocks safe co-location of any future cache-dependent tests: export a `__clearL1CacheForTests()` from [readThroughCache.ts](api/src/infrastructure/cache/readThroughCache.ts) (clears the module-level `l1` Map) and call it in a shared `beforeEach`, so tests don't have to hand-pick collision-free keys. Primary file: `api/src/infrastructure/cache/readThroughCache.ts`.
- ✅ **RESOLVED (2026-06-16) — Tenant Claude subscription (OAuth) now powers the `/v1/chat/completions` + cloud coding cascade, not just `/v1/messages`.** `VendorEnv` gained `CLAUDE_OAUTH_TOKEN`; [vendors/anthropic.ts](api/src/application/llm/vendors/anthropic.ts) `apiKeyFrom` prefers it (encoded with an `oauth:` sentinel) and `call()` switches to `Authorization: Bearer` + the `oauth-2025-04-20` beta + a prepended Claude Code identity system block (drops `x-api-key`). `LlmProxyService` threads a per-request `anthropicOAuthToken` option into `vendorEnv()`/`creditedVendorEnv()` and SUPPRESSES `paidOverflow` for subscription-funded Claude (free to us) via `isSubscriptionFunded`. Wired live at every completion consumer: the `/v1/chat/completions` route and both [cloudAgentEngine.ts](api/src/application/runtime/cloudAgentEngine.ts) sites (in-Worker/DO loop + container op), each resolving the token via `resolveAnthropicOAuthToken`. BYO-credential DB lookups are defensive (degrade to operator-key floor, never 500). Tests: `anthropicOAuthVendor.test.ts`. _Residual:_ the BYO `/v1/messages` our-models branch and the `setTenantProviderKey` (API-key) BYO path still meter on operator/our keys by design — a tenant's BYO **API key** (vs subscription) is NOT used by the chat cascade (it only serves the `/v1/messages` passthrough); wiring api-key BYO into the cascade would change overflow accounting and was intentionally left out of this pass.
- **PWA install prompt and update banner can render at the same bottom-center spot** (2026-06-16). Added [PwaInstallPrompt.tsx](frontend/src/components/PwaInstallPrompt.tsx) (captures `beforeinstallprompt` / iOS Add-to-Home-Screen fallback) and refactored both PWA toasts onto a shared [PwaToast.tsx](frontend/src/components/PwaToast.tsx) shell. Both toasts use identical `position:fixed; bottom:24; left:50%` placement, so in the rare window where a returning, not-yet-installed user also has a freshly-deployed waiting service worker, [PwaUpdateBanner](frontend/src/components/PwaUpdateBanner.tsx) and [PwaInstallPrompt](frontend/src/components/PwaInstallPrompt.tsx) overlap. Not broken (update banner auto-reloads within 60s and the overlap window is tiny) but visually messy. **Fixing** (a single `PwaToastStack` container that vertically stacks whichever toasts are live, or having the install prompt yield while an update is pending) unblocks: clean co-occurrence of the two PWA affordances. Owner: T2 (App UI).
- **Brain `list_tasks` returns the full untruncated task list (per-task `description` included) in one tool result** (2026-06-16). Surfaced while fixing the archived-backlog bug: the triage for chat #18 shows the `list_tasks` tool result at ~145k chars because [tasksApi.list](frontend/src/lib/builderforceApi.ts) → [GET /api/tasks](api/src/presentation/routes/taskRoutes.ts) returns every task's full body, and the brain action ([platformActions.ts](frontend/src/lib/brain/platformActions.ts) `tasks/list`) feeds it back to the model verbatim. Now that archived tasks are filtered the payload shrinks, but a large active backlog still blows the context window and token budget on a single list call. The same trace was also mis-marked `ERROR` — that is a *separate* false-positive in the triage report's broad `isFailedToolResult` regex (it matches the literal word "error" anywhere in legit data; see the note at [platformActions.ts:101](frontend/src/lib/brain/platformActions.ts#L101)), not a real tool failure. **Fixing** (give the brain `list_tasks` a slim projection — id/key/title/status/priority/archived only, with full bodies fetched on demand via `get`, and tighten the triage error-classifier to inspect the result shape rather than regex-scan the payload) unblocks: cheaper, context-safe backlog reads and accurate run-trace error reporting. Owner: T2 (brain).
- **Service worker `/sw.js` intermittently fails to fetch on update** (2026-06-15). Live console shows `Failed to update a ServiceWorker … sw.js: An unknown error occurred when fetching the script` on `/login`. Code-level fix already applied: `PwaUpdateBanner.checkForUpdate` now `.catch()`es the `registration.update()` rejection (it was a `void`-discarded promise firing on every poll + visibilitychange/focus/online → "Uncaught (in promise)" spam). **Residual (infra, not code):** the *underlying* transient sw.js fetch failure is unresolved — likely Cloudflare Pages / `@cloudflare/next-on-pages` occasionally routing `/sw.js` through the SSR worker (returning HTML, MIME mismatch) instead of the static asset, or an edge revalidation hiccup against the `no-cache` `/sw.js` header. Fixing it removes the warning entirely and guarantees the update toast always arrives. Needs prod repro (check the `content-type` + `cf-cache-status` actually returned for `/sw.js`) to confirm. Owner: T9 (platform/CI) + T2 (PwaUpdateBanner).
- **Cloudflare vendor moved to the OpenAI-compatible endpoint + one shared body builder + prompt caching on every call** (2026-06-15). The CF coders I added 400'd on tools (`[cloudflare] 400: tools[0].function: Field required`): the old `/ai/run/<model>` path with a hand-rolled `toCloudflareTools` flattener sent `{name,…}`, but the newer FC models (kimi/glm) want the OpenAI-nested `{type:'function',function:{…}}`. Fixed by switching CF to its **OpenAI-compatible** endpoint (`/ai/v1/chat/completions`) via the shared `executeChatCompletion` transport — standard tools in, standard response out, translation deleted. While there: extracted ONE `buildOpenAIChatBody` in `vendors/types.ts` (openrouter/nvidia/cerebras/googleai/cloudflare were five identical copies; Cerebras's `max_completion_tokens` + OpenRouter/Cerebras schema-sanitize ride small opts; Ollama stays native). **Prompt caching is now ON for every call**: `applyPromptCaching` is baked into the shared builder (no-op for non-Anthropic models) AND the direct-Anthropic floor (`anthropic.ts`) now marks `cache_control` on the system block + last tool — so the metered Claude path caches its large stable prefix at ~0.1x instead of full price every turn. All resolved this pass (991 api tests green); no residual.

- **Cloud coding runs 413'd on small-context models + a gateway error wrongly marked the run COMPLETE; context-aware model selection added, but true context COMPACTION is still a gap** (2026-06-15). A 97K-token coding context hit a 32K-window Cloudflare model (`@cf/qwen/qwen3-30b-a3b-fp8`) → HTTP **413** "exceeded this model context window limit", surfaced as a misleading "Gateway 429", and the **container** loop (`api/container/server.mjs`) then ran `finalize` (→ COMPLETED) instead of failing. Fixed: (a) **413 ∈ `CASCADE_STATUSES`** so a context overflow fails over to a bigger-window model (pool ordered big-window-first; a strict pin also drops + cascades on 413); (b) the container loop routes a gateway `turn.error` to the `fail` channel (self-heal/retry), never `finalize` — the in-Worker + durable surfaces already mapped `ok:false`→FAILED; (c) **context-aware first-pass selection** — `VendorModelEntry.contextWindow` (live values), `estimateRequestTokens` + `modelsFittingContext` filter the seed to models whose window fits BEFORE the SSM learned-routing ranks them (small-window models stay in the pool for small tasks, never seeded into an oversized one); (d) gateway errors now name the resolved model + candidate chain ("which model failed"); (e) **context COMPACTION** (`api/src/application/llm/compactMessages.ts`) — both cloud loops compress the conversation BEFORE each paid call when it exceeds a ~40K-token budget: the bulky middle (accumulated read_file/search tool results) is summarized into ONE "builder-memory" note via the free-pool gateway (`buildGatewaySummarizer`, same pattern as `BrainService.summarizeChat`), with lossy elision as the no-LLM fallback. Pinning the system prompt + the task + the recent tail, and the tail-never-starts-on-a-`tool`-message rule, keep tool-call pairing valid. The in-Worker/durable loop mutates `messages` in place (persists into CloudLoopState so the DO doesn't re-summarize the same prefix); the container `llm` op RETURNS `compactedMessages` and `server.mjs` adopts them as its loop state. A `context.compacted` timeline event reports before→after tokens. So a long run no longer re-sends a ballooning history — cheaper, and small/fast CF coders stay viable for longer.
- **Cloud coding runs drained the operator's metered Anthropic key ($10/mo cap hit 100%) — root-caused to the cascade reaching the funded direct-Anthropic floor too eagerly; FIXED in the gateway** (2026-06-15). **RESOLVED — Cloudflare binding + catalog:** `wrangler whoami`/`secret list` confirmed `CLOUDFLARE_AI_API_TOKEN` + `CLAUDE_API_KEY` were bound but **`CLOUDFLARE_ACCOUNT_ID` was NOT** (a misnamed `CLOUDFLARE_ACCOUNT_API_TOKEN` secret existed instead), so the vendor `apiKeyFrom` returned null and Cloudflare (`PAID_LEAD_VENDOR`, free neurons) was DEAD on every call → all overflow floored to the metered Anthropic key. Operator added `CLOUDFLARE_ACCOUNT_ID` as a secret (NOT committed — account id kept out of `wrangler.toml` for security). The stale `@cf/meta/llama-3-8b-instruct` (404s) was replaced with the live `@cf/meta/llama-3.1-8b-instruct-fp8`, and 3 live function-calling-verified CF coders were added to the pool (`@cf/zai-org/glm-4.7-flash` 128K, `@cf/moonshotai/kimi-k2.7-code` 256K, `@cf/meta/llama-3.3-70b-instruct-fp8-fast` 24K) so coding overflow burns free neurons before any metered coder. Fixes landed in `api/src/application/llm/**` + `api/src/infrastructure/auth/cooldownStore.ts`: (a) an Anthropic usage-cap **400** (`invalid_request_error` "reached your specified API usage limits") was classified as a fatal caller `request_error` → it short-circuited the cascade with no failover AND wrote no cooldown; now `throwClassified4xx`/`isCapacityLimitBody` map any capacity/credit-balance 4xx to a retryable 429 so it fails over to another provider; (b) coding runs were capped at `FREE_ATTEMPT_BUDGET=2` free coders before escalating to paid/metered coders — now `CODING_FREE_ATTEMPT_BUDGET` (the whole free coding pool, ~9) is walked first so the metered floor is genuine last-resort (10+ models before Claude); (c) a capacity limit now cools the **whole vendor for 60 min** on the first strike (new `capacity` `CooldownClass`) instead of the 5-min transient, so a capped key stands down instead of being re-reached/re-billed every run. (The Cloudflare-binding root cause is RESOLVED — see the entry above.) **Residual:** no per-turn telemetry event fires when a cloud run actually bills the direct-Anthropic floor (`claude-sonnet-4-6`/`claude-opus-4-8`) — the metered-floor hit is observable only via usage rows after the fact; a `metered_floor_used` event on the timeline (sibling of `coding_model_degraded`) would make "we spent on the paid Claude key" loud in real time. Unblocks: provable, real-time cost visibility + an alarm before a spend cap is blown.
- **Cloud agents got first-class git tools (get-latest / undo / redo / status / diff / history) — on-prem only ever had a read-only `git_history` that was never migrated** (2026-06-15). Root cause of the task-78 failures: the container agent worked on a stale branch (branched off an old main, never re-synced) so its build broke against old code and its PR would have reverted ~6.7K lines — and it had no tool to pull the latest. Fixed by adding 6 git verbs to the SHARED registry (`packages/agent-tools/src/core-tools.ts`, canonical command text in `buildGitCommand`), gated to the `shell` capability so they reach the Container + on-prem-shell surfaces but NOT the shell-less durable Worker: `git_status`, `git_diff`, `git_history` (migrates the pi-only on-prem tool), `git_sync_latest` (fetch+merge base → never build on stale code), `git_undo`/`git_redo` (reflog pair, dirty-tree-guarded). Container execution is mirrored in `api/container/server.mjs` (`gitTool`) with the surface-specific twist that it persists via Worker-side GitHub-API commits, so each mutating op first fast-forwards the local clone to the remote head, then operates, then pushes (`--force-with-lease` for undo/redo). Covered by `cloudAgentGitTools.test.ts` (10) incl. injection-safety; full api suite green (952). **Container clone is now a FULL clone** (`server.mjs` — dropped `--depth 1`), so `git_sync_latest`, `git diff main`, and `git merge-base` work reliably (a shallow clone had no merge-base with the base branch); `git_sync_latest` is a plain `git fetch`+merge, no `--unshallow` dance. **The cloud system prompt now instructs the agent to call `git_sync_latest` FIRST** (shell-surface line in `prepareCloudRun`), so a stale branch is synced before any edit instead of relying on the tool description alone. **Remaining residuals:** (1) the shell-less durable Worker surface still has NO git sync — a durable run on a stale branch can't self-update (it commits via API, no shell); a base-merge-over-API path would be needed (the Container surface, which is where multi-step coding runs, is covered). (2) On-prem's shared-registry surface (`NODE_FILE_SURFACE_CAPS`) intentionally omits `shell`, so it surfaces git via its NATIVE bash tools, not the shared git tools — the legacy pi `git-history-tool.ts` can be deleted once the pi loop is retired.
- **Cloudflare Workers AI now LEADS every paid pool, but the catalog is only 3 models — expanding it would "use Cloudflare more"** (2026-06-15). Cloudflare bills in neurons with the first ~10K/day FREE, so paid routing should drain that allowance before any metered vendor. Done in `LlmProxyService.ts`: new `PAID_LEAD_VENDOR='cloudflare'` + shared `leadPoolWithVendor()` floats Cloudflare to the head of `PRO_PAID_MODEL_POOL` (general paid) and `CODING_PREMIUM_FALLBACK_MODELS` (coding paid fallback / backstop); the coding-pool default coder is deliberately left as the strong `claude-sonnet-4.6` (cost-first routing must not regress agentic coding quality — Cloudflare leads only the *fallback*, not the primary default). Residual: the Cloudflare catalog (`vendors/cloudflare.ts`) has just `llama-3-8b`, `gemma-4-26b-a4b-it`, `qwen3-30b-a3b-fp8`; adding more enabled Workers AI checkpoints (e.g. larger Llama / Qwen coders) would stretch the free allowance further across request shapes. Blocked on the operator's list of which Workers AI models are enabled on `CLOUDFLARE_ACCOUNT_ID` (a model not enabled returns `success:false` and cooldown-cycles). Unblocks: more paid traffic served on the free neuron allowance instead of metered vendors. Also note: general PRO paid traffic now tries Cloudflare's small general models (8B/26B) first after the free pool — acceptable per the cost directive and adaptively corrected by PRD-13 learned routing (`rankModelsForAction`), but a quality-sensitive Pro tenant may prefer a per-tenant opt-out toggle (not built).
- **On-prem coding-execution repo-prep is now a modular `RepoSyncStrategy` port + skills declare skill-to-skill deps; two follow-ups remain** (2026-06-16). The hard-coded "is this the latest code from the repo?" clone/checkout was duplicated inline in the swimlane dispatch loop ([builderforce-coding-dispatch.ts](agent-runtime/src/infra/builderforce-coding-dispatch.ts)) and the V2 ticket workspace ([builderforce-relay.ts](agent-runtime/src/infra/builderforce-relay.ts) `ensureTaskWorkspace`). Extracted into one injected [repo-sync.ts](agent-runtime/src/infra/repo-sync.ts) `RepoSyncStrategy` (clone-if-missing → WIP-safe refresh-to-latest on reuse → branch mode `new-branch` vs idempotent `ticket-branch`), fixing the latent stale-reuse bug (the ticket workspace previously never re-synced) while preserving accumulated uncommitted WIP. Skills gained a `requires.skills` dependency ([dependencies.ts](agent-runtime/src/agents/skills/dependencies.ts), enforced in `filterSkillEntries`): `coding-agent` now depends on `github`, which is auto-included when active and disables `coding-agent` if `gh` is absent. **Residuals:** (1) `builderforce skills check`/status ([skills-status.ts](agent-runtime/src/agents/skills-status.ts)) and the install flow ([skills-install.ts](agent-runtime/src/agents/skills-install.ts)) do NOT yet surface a skill-dependency unmet reason ("coding-agent disabled: requires github → gh missing") nor auto-install a depended-on skill — the dependency is enforced only for prompt inclusion. (2) This `RepoSyncStrategy` covers the on-prem agent-runtime paths only; the **cloud** durable Worker surface still has no git sync (see the cloud git-tools entry above) — unifying both behind one sync contract is the larger play. Fixing (1) unblocks honest skill diagnostics + one-shot dependency installs; (2) unblocks a single repo-prep policy across on-prem and cloud. Owner: T5 (on-prem runtime).
- **✅ RESOLVED — `surface=container` runs were reaped as "orphaned" mid-build because the 90s liveness ceiling was shorter than a single shell command** (2026-06-15, execution #71 triage + fix). Root cause: the container heartbeated `executions.updated_at` **only on each `op:'llm'` step** (`cloudAgentEngine.ts`). A `run_command` shell step runs up to `COMMAND_TIMEOUT_MS = 10 min` (`api/container/server.mjs`) and made **no callback to the Worker until it finished** (its `op:'event'` is sent only *after* completion). Meanwhile BOTH liveness checks fail any cloud run whose `updated_at` is older than **90s** — `RuntimeService.CLOUD_ORPHAN_MS = 90_000` (read-path) and `staleExecutionReaper.CLOUD_RUNNING_DEADLINE_MS = 90_000` (cron). So the first build/install/test step that exceeded 90s (this repo's `pnpm install && pnpm test` is ~2 min — CI shows 1m58s) let the heartbeat go stale and the reaper killed the run *while the container was still legitimately running the command* → "went silent mid-run past the ~30s wall." The 600s command timeout vs 90s orphan ceiling was a **6.6× mismatch**, and long shell commands are the container surface's entire reason to exist, so it fired on essentially every real build. Compounding: once a file was written the PR existed, so `isSelfHealEligible` (`openPrCount === 0`) was false and the orphan couldn't self-heal onto the durable runner — it just failed (execution #71 had PR #34 open); and `AgentContainerDO.onError` never fired because the container was healthy and busy, it was the Worker-side reaper killing a live run (so the triage's "image is likely unstable" hint was misleading). **Fix:** the container now fires a dedicated `op:'heartbeat'` on a 30s timer for the whole run lifetime (`runLoop`, independent of LLM steps), and the Worker bumps `updated_at` via a shared `heartbeatExecution` helper (DRY — the `llm` op uses it too). The heartbeat response also carries `cancelled`, so a cancel during a multi-minute build SIGKILLs the in-flight child immediately and the loop breaks before spending another LLM call, instead of waiting out the 10-min command timeout. **Residual:** the container surface still has no separate orphan deadline — liveness is correctly measured from the heartbeat now, but if the internal `container-op` endpoint is itself unreachable for >90s the run is still reaped; a container-specific ceiling (≥ a couple beats) would harden against transient Worker-side outages.
- **✅ RESOLVED — container runs (`surface=container`) cloned the BASE branch, never the ticket's HEAD branch, so every pass started blind to prior work** (2026-06-15). Root cause caught in execution #67 triage: prior runs commit their WIP to the ticket's head branch (`builderforce/task-<id>`, `ctx.branch`) via the Worker, but `api/container/server.mjs` cloned `git clone --depth 1 -b <baseBranch>` — and a `--depth 1` clone is single-branch, so the head branch and all earlier passes were silently absent. The container landed on a stale `main` (`git status` → "On branch main", `git log --all` → one commit), and the agent burned its whole budget + multiple LLM steps rediscovering that the file it was asked to fix "doesn't exist on disk." Fixed by carrying `headBranch: repo.ctx.branch` in the container clone spec (`runtimeRoutes.ts`) and having the container clone the head branch first, falling back to the base branch only on run #1 when the head branch doesn't exist on the remote yet. Also emits a `runtime.clone` success event recording the branch actually checked out, so triage never has to reverse-engineer it from `git status` again. Residual: the head-branch clone is still `--depth 1` (shallow) — an agent that needs base-branch history (e.g. `git diff main`, `git merge-base`) won't have it; unblocks full-history container work by deepening selectively (`git fetch --depth=N` / `--unshallow`) when a command needs it.
- **Psychometric persona personality (Pro) shipped, but tenant "My Personas" are localStorage-only so their trait vectors never reach execution** (2026-06-16). New end-to-end personality feature: a persona can carry a `PsychometricProfile` (full framework suite — HEXACO / regulatory-focus / need-for-cognition / decision-style / moral-foundations / Thomas-Kilmann / Schwartz / Enneagram / dispositional) deterministically compiled into BOTH system-prompt directives AND execution levers (think-depth floor, reasoning-on, temperature) by [psychometrics.ts](agent-runtime/src/builderforce/psychometrics.ts) and injected at run time via [buildPersonaSystemBlock](agent-runtime/src/builderforce/personas.ts) + [resolveActivePsychometricParams](agent-runtime/src/agents/assigned-capabilities.ts) in [attempt.ts](agent-runtime/src/agents/embedded-runner/run/attempt.ts). The LIVE path is `platform_personas` (migration `0199` + [adminRoutes.ts](api/src/presentation/routes/adminRoutes.ts) → agent-host sync → [registerPlatformPersonasAsRoles](agent-runtime/src/builderforce/agent-roles.ts)). The editor ([PsychometricEditor.tsx](frontend/src/components/PsychometricEditor.tsx) — sliders/questionnaire/import) is wired into the tenant persona modal ([personas/page.tsx](frontend/src/app/personas/page.tsx)) and Pro-gated via [PlanLimits.psychometricPersona](api/src/domain/tenant/PlanLimits.ts) + [personaRoutes.ts](api/src/presentation/routes/personaRoutes.ts). **Gap:** tenant "My Personas" persist to `localStorage`, not the DB, so a profile a tenant authors there is never synced to an agent host and never executes — only admin-managed platform personas do. **Fixing** (server-back tenant personas in a `tenant_personas` table + sync them down the assignment path the way `platform_personas` flow) unblocks self-serve Pro personality that actually changes how a tenant's agents think. Owner: T1/T2.
- **V2 cloud agents apply psychometric prompt directives but NOT the execution-param half** (2026-06-16). Directives flow into the V2 SDK path via [buildAssignedCapabilityAppend](agent-runtime/src/agents/assigned-capabilities.ts), so a cloud agent reads its personality, but the think-depth/reasoning/temperature overrides from `resolveActivePsychometricParams` are merged only in the embedded (on-prem) runner ([attempt.ts](agent-runtime/src/agents/embedded-runner/run/attempt.ts)); the Claude-Agent-SDK cloud loop manages its own params and ignores them. **Fixing** (thread the merged `PsychometricExecParams` into the V2 cloud run's model/think config) unblocks behavioural personality parity (not just textual) on cloud agents. Owner: T3.
- **Psychometric dimension-id contract is duplicated across packages + admin UI lacks the editor** (2026-06-16). The canonical dimension ids live in `DIM` in BOTH [agent-runtime psychometrics.ts](agent-runtime/src/builderforce/psychometrics.ts) (compiler) and [api psychometricCatalog.ts](api/src/application/persona/psychometricCatalog.ts) (catalog+scoring), hand-synced because the packages share no module — a renamed id on one side would silently drop that dimension. **Fixing** (extract a shared `@builderforce/psychometric-contract` exporting the id constants) unblocks single-source-of-truth safety. Also: the **admin** Personas tab doesn't yet expose `PsychometricEditor` (only the tenant modal does), though admin POST/PATCH already persist the `psychometric` column — so admin platform personas currently need the profile set via API. Owner: T9.

- **Direct-Anthropic coding floor is non-streaming only (`anthropic` vendor has no `callStream`)** (2026-06-14). Added `api/src/application/llm/vendors/anthropic.ts` — a direct `api.anthropic.com/v1/messages` vendor on `CLAUDE_API_KEY` (`claude-sonnet-4-6` → `claude-opus-4-8`), wired as the last-resort tail of `CODING_PREMIUM_FALLBACK_MODELS` so the coding cascade falls back to Claude when every OpenRouter-routed paid coder is down. It implements `call` (non-streaming, with a full OpenAI↔Anthropic-Messages translation) but **not** `callStream`, because the only path that reaches it — the cloud coding tool loop — is non-streaming, so `dispatchVendorStream` cleanly skips it. Residual: a future *streaming* coding/chat request that exhausts into the coding fallback would skip the Anthropic floor (and could surface `cascade_exhausted` where a non-streaming request would have been rescued). Unblocks: streaming reliability-floor parity — implement `callStream` translating Anthropic SSE (`message_start`/`content_block_*`/`message_delta`) → OpenAI chat SSE chunks (incl. `tool_use` → `tool_calls` `input_json_delta` accumulation).

- **✅ RESOLVED — Cloudflare Workers AI now drives the coding tool loop; `@cf/qwen/qwen3-30b-a3b-fp8` is a paid coder ahead of Claude** (2026-06-14). The `cloudflare` vendor now translates tools both ways: OpenAI `[{type:'function',function:{…}}]` → Cloudflare native `[{name,description,parameters}]` on the request (`buildBody`/`toCloudflareTools`; `tool_choice` dropped — native /ai/run has none), and Cloudflare `result.tool_calls` (`{name,arguments}`, no id, object args) → OpenAI `choices[0].message.tool_calls` (synthesized id, JSON-stringified args) on the response (`adaptCloudflareResponse`), so `parseLlmChoice` + the multi-turn coding loop work. `@cf/qwen/qwen3-30b-a3b-fp8` is marked tool-capable, added to `CODING_MODEL_POOL` (paid-coder section → shows in the Pro picker, not Free) and inserted into `CODING_PREMIUM_FALLBACK_MODELS` **before** every Claude entry (vendor-diverse from both OpenRouter and Anthropic; no-key-skips when the Cloudflare token/account aren't bound). `@cf/google/gemma-4-26b-a4b-it` stays a general PRO-pool chat model (not a coder). Covered by new cases in `LlmProxyService.codingPool.test.ts` (api llm suite green).

- **✅ RESOLVED — Learned model routing (PRD 13) implemented end-to-end across all 3 phases (capture → analyze + route → client SSM recall bias)** (2026-06-15). Built on the existing capture substrate (no parallel "model used" store): (1) **Taxonomy** — closed `ACTION_TYPES` enum in `api/src/application/llm/actionTypes.ts` (mirrored to `frontend/src/lib/builderforceApi.ts`), the single source for classifier/router/scorer/analytics/UI; `learnedRoutingEnabled` kill switch (`LEARNED_ROUTING_ENABLED`, default on). (2) **Classifier** — `classifyTask.ts` runs ONCE per task on the FREE pool (strict json_schema) and caches on `tasks.action_type` (+ `action_type_confidence`, migration 0197); `resolveLearnedRoutingInputs` in `cloudAgentEngine` classifies-or-reuses on the first tick, best-effort → `other`. (3) **Outcome scorer** — `scoreRunOutcome.ts` writes one `run_model_outcomes` row (migration 0198, unique `execution_id`) per terminal cloud run via the pure `computeOutcomeScore` (D3: merge 0.5 + green-CI 0.2 + no-degradation 0.15 + efficiency 0.15, approval pins completion, failed/cancelled = 0); wired at every terminal chokepoint (DO `cleanup`, Worker `runCloudExecution` ×3, container `finalize`/`fail`), idempotent + best-effort. (4) **Routing table** — `routingTable.ts`: a derived `routing:<scope>` KV blob (project→tenant→global) maintained by incremental Welford RMW on each outcome (no table scan), read by the router AND the analytics endpoint via `getOrSetCached`; cold miss reconciles from a single grouped SQL. (5) **Router** — pure `rankModelsForAction` reorders `codingModelsForPlan` by avgScore (+ MIN_SAMPLES=8 floor, cost tie-break, optional bias); `pickCloudModel` gains learned opts (free-plan gate + explicit-pin byte-for-byte unchanged; soft seed = `ranked[0]`); `model.select` explains the choice. (6) **Analytics** — `GET /llm/v1/model-analytics` + `ModelRoutingAnalytics` panel (Workforce → LLM tab). (7) **Client SSM bias** — `frontend/src/lib/modelRecallBias.ts` (WebGPU+IndexedDB-gated embed→kNN→bias), seeded via `GET /llm/v1/recall-seed`, threaded interactive-launch-only through `parseRoutingBias` → `pickCloudModel`. Tests: `actionTypes`, `classifyTask`, `routingTable`, `scoreRunOutcome`, extended `codingPool`, `modelRecallBias` (api 940 + frontend 247 green). **Residuals (deferred):** (a) **on-prem/host runs aren't routed** by this (cloud-only phase 1 per PRD §10) — host picks its own model; (b) **no scheduled reconcile cron** — the blob reconciles only on a cold-cache read, so a lost-update race from concurrent same-bucket terminals self-heals only on the next KV eviction, not on a timer (add a cron calling `reconcileRoutingTable` per active scope); (c) **the SSM embedding is a deterministic feature-hash, not a real MambaKit/SSMjs WebGPU SSM embedding** — the `embedTask` seam is in place but the per-codebase `model.bin` weights aren't pushed from builderforce.ai yet (drop-in swap behind the same signature); (d) **recall memory is pull-seeded** (`/recall-seed`), not pushed live over the execution-steering WS as PRD §6.6 envisions (cross-device freshness lags until the next mount); (e) **the container `llm` op doesn't apply learned routing** (only the DO/Worker `runCloudToolLoop` does) — fine while the container falls back to DO, but a parity gap if the long-lived container surface ships. Unblocks: task-aware model routing + per-codebase learned preferences.

- **Superseded (now resolved) — Learned model routing design notes.** (2026-06-14). Every cloud run's **resolved model** is already captured per task/project (`recordCloudUsage` → `llm_usage_log.model` + attribution `{cloudAgentRef, executionId, taskId, projectId}`; plus `model.select`/`coding_model_degraded` timeline events) — so the "which model ran" substrate exists. Missing is the learned-routing loop the operator wants: (1) **action-type labels** — classify each task into an action type (`sql`, `frontend`, `refactor`, `bugfix`, …) so runs group by type; proposed first step is a cheap **first-pass FREE-model classifier** that tags the task before the run (decision: add a per-run classifier call? store the label where — a `task_action_type` column / a `run_labels` table?). (2) **outcome signal** — define "worked best" (PR merged? green CI? human approval? steps-to-done? token cost?) and join it to `(action_type, model)` so analytics can rank models per type ("Google/Gemini best at SQL"). (3) **routing** — feed the ranking back into selection (extend `pickCloudModel`/`codingModelsForPlan` with an action-type→model preference), with **SSM/Samba memory** (MambaKit/SSMjs hippocampus — see the SSM Hippocampus loop) as the per-codebase recall layer that learns which models work best for THIS repo over time. Design-level subsystem spanning api + SSMjs/MambaKit; **not** built this pass to avoid a dead/half-wired routing seam. Blockers needing an explicit decision: the "best" outcome metric, whether to add a first-pass classifier call on every run (cost), and the SSM integration surface. Unblocks: task-aware model routing + per-codebase learned model preferences.

- **✅ RESOLVED — a failing CI build on the agent's PR branch now surfaces WHY on the ticket and feeds the reason back to the agent (pre-merge), not just post-merge** (2026-06-14). An agent could mark a task "complete" while the build on its `builderforce/task-<id>` branch was red, and the failure reason was invisible on the ticket — the pre-merge CI path (`ingestRepoCiEvent.ingestPreMergeEvent`) only recorded a bare `ci.<event>` telemetry ping with the outcome + URL: it never fetched the failing jobs/steps, never persisted a build status/reason on the PR row, and never dispatched an auto-fix (only the POST-merge path did). Fixed by making both phases symmetric through one shared `applyBuildOutcome` helper: on a pre-merge failure it (1) **fetches the failing jobs/steps** via the existing `fetchBuildError`, (2) **persists `build_status` + the reason on the open PR row** (new `build_error` column, migration 0196; new `findOpenPullRequestByTask`; `setPullRequestBuildStatus` extended to write/clear the reason), (3) records a prominent `build.result` timeline event, and (4) **dispatches an auto-fix run** (same per-task attempt cap / loop-guard) carrying a phase-tagged `remediation` block so the cloud agent's prompt is framed as "the CI build on your PR branch FAILED — fix it before merge" (`parseRemediation` + `cloudAgentEngine` prompt are now `phase`-aware). Auto-fix on the PR branch is gated to authoritative `workflow_run` conclusions (a `runId`) so the many per-check events on a branch don't each burn an attempt. UI: `PullRequestPanel` now renders a `BuildStatus` block (status badge + the failing-jobs/steps reason in a scrollable `<pre>` + auto-fix note) for the OPEN PR too, and polls while pre-merge build is pending. Covered by 5 new pre-merge cases in `ingestRepoCiEvent.test.ts` + a pre-merge-phase case in `cloudDispatch.test.ts` (api ci+runtime suites green); frontend `tsc` clean. Sibling to the runtime-crash-reason work above — this is the CI-build-failure counterpart.

- **A failing PR-branch build is surfaced on the Pull Request tab, but not yet as a ticket/execution-chip badge** (2026-06-14). The build status + reason now persist on the PR row and render in `PullRequestPanel` (the ticket's "Pull Request" tab) and the run's Logs/Timeline. What's missing is a higher-altitude signal: the execution chip (`#64 · cancelled`) and the task card don't show a "build failing" badge, so a buyer scanning the executions list still can't tell at a glance that a "completed" run shipped a red build. Deferred: derive a `buildStatus` badge on `AgentExecutionPanel`'s execution chips + the task card from the linked PR row (the data is already there via `getTaskPullRequest`). Unblocks: red-build visibility without opening the PR tab.

- **Task-PRD content — fence-wrap normalized at the render path + on new writes; only the historical backfill remains.** LLM-drafted PRDs sometimes arrive wrapped in a whole-document ` ```markdown ` fence, which `ChatMessageContent` rendered as one raw "MARKDOWN" code box in the task-details PRD tab instead of formatted prose. Closed two ways: (1) **render-time** — `TaskPrdTab` now runs `unwrapMarkdownFence` (the generalized ex-`unwrapLegalMarkdown` util) and adds a `Preview | RAW` `ViewToggle` (panel + fullscreen), so existing rows display correctly; (2) **on WRITE** — `draftTaskPrd` (`api/.../prd/taskPrd.ts`) strips the fence via new `stripPrdMarkdownFence` before persisting, so freshly generated PRDs are stored clean for every consumer (render/export/repo-commit/Copy). **Residual (operator):** a one-off backfill of `specs.prd` rows persisted before this change — until then the render-time unwrap stays the safety net (can't be retired). No code change available for the backfill without live-DB access. Mirrors the legal-doc normalization gap above.

- **✅ RESOLVED — backplanes now report WHY they crashed, and self-heal is unified across every detector** (2026-06-14). Three fixes shipped together: (1) **Crash reasons surfaced** — the container image (`api/container/server.mjs`) reports a caught loop crash on a dedicated `fail` container-op (not `finalize`, which implied an orderly finish), and `AgentContainerDO.onError` (which only `console.error`'d before) now attributes a hard container death (OOM / evict / unbootable image) to its execution and reports the real error; `CloudRunnerDO` already reported its `errorMessage`. New `cloudCrashReason()` carries the actual message to the timeline. (2) **One self-heal** — `api/src/application/runtime/cloudSelfHeal.ts` is the single once-only "re-queue on the durable executor, else fail with the real reason" path, shared by the cron reaper (`staleExecutionReaper`, refactored onto shared `isSelfHealEligible`/`buildDurableStartBody`/`dispatchDurableStart`), the container `fail` op + `onError` (`handleCloudRunCrash`), AND the read-path repair `RuntimeService.reapIfOrphaned` (new `onCloudOrphan` DI callback wired in `index.ts`). This closes the race that bit execution #62: the read path used to permanently fail a crashed run before the cron could retry it; now it self-heals first. (3) **Surface-aware orphan reason** — `cloudOrphanReason` no longer claims a "~30s serverless limit / downgrade to durable" on a container/durable run that ran past the wall. Covered by `cloudSelfHeal.test.ts` (11) + reaper/orphan-reason tests; full api suite green (879).
- **Container hard-death (`onError`) self-heal can't push a LIVE WebSocket event** (2026-06-14). `AgentContainerDO.onError` runs in the container DO's isolate, where the per-run WS subscriber map and the `executionBoardSink` (SESSION_ROOM fan-out) are not registered (they're wired per request isolate). So when a container crash self-heals or fails via `handleCloudRunCrash`, the failure/requeue is persisted + lands a `run.failed`/`runtime.crash` timeline row, but live subscribers only see it on the next read-path reconciliation poll (a few seconds), not instantly — same latency as today's orphan reaps. The container `fail` op path (in the Worker request isolate) DOES push live. Deferred: have `handleCloudRunCrash` emit through a cross-isolate notifier (e.g. always via the SESSION_ROOM DO) so a DO-isolate crash pushes instantly too. Unblocks: real-time crash surfacing regardless of which isolate detected it.
- **✅ RESOLVED — a cloud coding run can no longer fall through to a non-coder backstop; it floors onto paid coders or fails honestly** (2026-06-14). Root cause: a `codingOnly` proxy restricted its *primary* pool to `CODING_MODEL_POOL` but still appended the general non-coder premium-fallback chain (`PREMIUM_FALLBACK_MODELS` → `googleai/gemini-2.5-flash`) inline, and its backstop chain ended in the non-coder `GUARANTEED_BACKSTOP_MODEL` — so an exhausted coding cascade resolved onto a generalist that loops on search and ships no edits (execution #62: ~77s, one orphan file, no wiring). Fixed in `LlmProxyService`: (1) new `CODING_PREMIUM_FALLBACK_MODELS` (paid coders — DeepSeek/Xiaomi/Anthropic, vendor-diverse, cheapest-first) is the appended fallback for `codingOnly` proxies via a new `codingOnly` option on the service + the `premiumFallback` getter; (2) `CODING_BACKSTOP_MODELS` is now coders-only (the gemini last-resort removed) — if every paid coder is also down the run surfaces `cascade_exhausted` (an honest failure beats a weak-model run that fakes progress); (3) `PAID_OVERFLOW_MODELS` metering kept precise — only the cheap `CHEAPEST_PAID_CODER` is flagged by id (the flagship Pro plan coders are metered as overflow only via the explicit backstop `paidOverflow=true` flag, so a Pro tenant's legit plan usage isn't mis-metered). `coding_model_degraded` telemetry stays as a safety net for an explicit non-coder pin. Covered by new/updated tests in `LlmProxyService.backstop.test.ts`, `LlmProxyService.overflow.test.ts`, `cloudAgentEngine.test.ts`, `cloudTelemetry.test.ts` (llm+runtime suites green: 295).
- **Lane agent's host `target` is not threaded into the dispatcher** (2026-06-14). `decideLaneAutoRun` returns the lane agent's `agentRef` + `model`; the dispatcher (`startDispatchedExecution`) resolves the on-prem host from a pin on the *task* (`tasks.assignedAgentHostId`). A swimlane agent that pins its own host `target` (a specific on-prem machine) does not yet propagate that into the run, so a lane can't direct its run to a particular machine — host delivery only happens when the task itself is host-pinned. Unblocks: per-lane choice of which on-prem machine runs the stage. (The V2-on-host engine gate is now removed — host delivery is no longer gated on engine; the on-prem host runtime runs the V2 Agent natively, and the run carries the agent's own model.)
- **✅ RESOLVED — board drag into a staffed lane created the run but never fired the agent** (2026-06-15). Two compounding causes in the autonomous lane trigger (`taskRoutes.ts:maybeAutoRunOnLaneEntry`). (1) The trigger was deferred into `c.executionCtx.waitUntil(...)` and then, from inside that post-response continuation, the dispatcher (`startDispatchedExecution`) re-registered the executor kickoff via *another* `c.executionCtx.waitUntil(orchestrate())` — registering work on an already-closed request context throws ("I/O on behalf of a different request"), which the trigger's `try/catch` swallowed, so `runtimeService.submit` created the `executions` row but `orchestrate()` never ran (run stuck, agent never started). Fixed by having `maybeAutoRunOnLaneEntry` COLLECT the dispatcher's deferred kickoff and `await Promise.allSettled(...)` it inside its own promise (we are already off the response path), so the single outer `waitUntil` registered *during* request handling keeps the whole chain — kickoff included — alive. (2) The idempotency guard used a raw `db.select` over `executions` in live statuses; a cloud run abandoned `RUNNING` by an evicted isolate is only reaped on READ, so a dead row blocked the lane's agent forever on any ticket that had run once before. Now reads through `runtimeService.listByTask` so orphans reap to FAILED first. Also consolidated the create + PATCH wiring into one route helper (`fireLaneAutoRun`) and dropped the per-call `waitUntil` lambda from the signature; the agent-advance path (`buildRuntimeService` `onLaneEntry`) reuses the same function. `tsc` clean.
- **Auto-run execution CREATION is not pushed over the project socket — only poll-surfaced** (2026-06-15). The board/cards/lanes update live via `broadcastProjectChanged` (SESSION_ROOM) on task writes, and the lane drag itself pushes. But when the autonomous trigger submits the auto-run, neither `runtimeService.submit` nor `startDispatchedExecution` broadcasts to the project room — only `notifyExecutionSubscribers` (the per-execution stream). So the freshly-queued run CHIP (e.g. "Bob · pending") surfaces on the board's `useBoardLiveRuns` poll tick, not instantly over WS, despite the run-feed comment treating WS as primary and the poll as a dropped-socket backstop. Distinct from the container-crash WS gap above (that's failure surfacing; this is creation surfacing). Deferred: emit a `broadcastProjectChanged` (or a dedicated run-created event) at dispatch so the chip appears the instant the agent is queued. Unblocks: instant "agent picked it up" feedback on drag without waiting for the reconcile poll.
- **`ide_agents.engine` column + V1 engine values are vestigial post-V1-deletion** (2026-06-14). V1 is deleted in the cloud AND on the on-prem host (the agent-runtime engine registry's sole runner is `builderforce-v2`; any legacy `engine` value falls back to v2). The API dispatch path no longer branches on engine (the `!isV2` gate and the `cloudAgentTypeLabel` V1 branch are gone). The `ide_agents.engine` column is now effectively constant and any rows still holding `'builderforce-v1'` are inert (resolve/behave as v2). Deferred: a migration to normalize/drop the `engine` column. The engine *registry* DI seam is INTENTIONALLY kept (a future V3 registers the same way). Unblocks: schema/code clarity once the column is retired.
- **Autonomous lane runs bypass the execution governance approval gate** (2026-06-14). The manual `/api/runtime/executions` route runs `evaluateExecutionApprovalGate` (governance approval rules — currently gates high/urgent priority tasks) before dispatch; the autonomous lane trigger (via `dispatchCloudRunForTask`) skips it. The lane's own `gate: 'human'` provides board-level human-in-the-loop, but tenant governance approval *rules* are not enforced on autonomously-triggered runs. NOT auto-bundled: applying it would make a high-priority task's autonomous run create an approval instead of running, a product decision (`evaluateExecutionApprovalGate` is currently route-private in `runtimeRoutes.ts` — extract + share when adopted). Unblocks: consistent policy enforcement — every agent run (manual or autonomous) honors the same approval rules.
- **Capability guardrail only enforces an explicitly-configured `required_capabilities`; there is no capability-aware *router*** (2026-06-14). `decideLaneAutoRun` now skips a lane agent whose resolved skills/personas don't cover the lane assignment's `required_capabilities` (`api/src/application/swimlane/laneAutoRun.ts` + the resolve+warn wiring in `taskRoutes.ts:maybeAutoRunOnLaneEntry`), which closes the "BA/PM/PO agent silently runs a coding task" hole **when a lane sets the field**. A lane with no `required_capabilities` configured still runs whatever agent is pinned (the exec #61 lane had none set). Deferred: (a) a real router that *scores* a task's inferred type (coding/docs/review) against each workforce agent's persona/skills and picks the best match rather than the first qualifying one (the AskUserQuestion "full capability-aware router" option), and (b) a sensible default requirement (e.g. infer `coding-agent` for a lane whose template writes code) so the guardrail protects un-configured lanes too. Unblocks: correct-by-default staffing without per-lane manual config.
- **`capability_mismatch` has no pre-execution timeline channel** (2026-06-14). When the guardrail skips a mis-staffed agent it emits a `console.warn` (Worker telemetry sink) only — there is no `execution_id` yet (we are *refusing* to start a run), so it can't ride the existing `recordCloudToolEvent` → Observability timeline path. The mismatch is therefore diagnosable in logs but invisible on the board/timeline. Deferred: a lightweight pre-execution audit channel (e.g. a per-task `auto_run_skipped` audit event) surfaced on the task card so a lane that silently won't auto-run explains itself in-product. Unblocks: operators see *why* a ticket dropped into an auto lane didn't start.
- **`capabilities.load` telemetry conflates agent-pinned vs inherited artifacts** (2026-06-14). The cloud run resolves capabilities via `resolveArtifacts({tenantId, taskId, cloudAgentRef})` — a UNION across tenant + project + task + agent scopes — and the `capabilities.load` timeline event reports that union. So an agent whose own (`scope='agent'`) config is empty still shows personas/skills assigned tenant- or project-wide (this is why exec #61's "Kevin BA/PM/PO" appeared to have `code-creator`/`documentation-agent` it was never directly assigned). The new /workforce **Agent manifest** (`api/src/application/artifact/agentManifest.ts`) deliberately shows the agent-scoped set ONLY, which is the honest "what is pinned to THIS agent" view. Deferred: make `capabilities.load` label each artifact with its source scope (agent vs project vs tenant) so the timeline distinguishes pinned from inherited — and reconsider whether tenant-wide persona assignments should silently apply to every agent at all. Unblocks: an operator can tell, from telemetry alone, what an agent itself carries vs what it merely inherited.
- **Moving a task across boards does not re-point `tasks.segment_id` to the target project's segment** (2026-06-14). `TaskService.moveTask` (now collision-safe re-keying) updates `project_id` + `key` but leaves `segment_id` pointing at the *source* project's segment. The `set_default_segment_id_via_project` trigger only fires `BEFORE INSERT`, and `segment_id` isn't modeled in the `Task` domain entity or written by `TaskRepository.update`, so a moved row keeps its old segment. Harmless for `single`-mode tenants (one shared default segment, so source and target segments are identical), but for a `segmented` tenant whose source/target projects live in different segments this leaves the task's segment stale — a data-isolation drift. Deferred (T7 — segment/isolation): on move, resolve the target project's `segment_id` and update the task to match (or add an `AFTER UPDATE OF project_id` trigger that re-derives it). Unblocks: correct per-segment attribution/erasure (DSR/GDPR cascade) for tasks that change boards in a segmented tenant.
- **A vendor-specific 400 inside the coding cascade can still suppress the paid coding backstop** (2026-06-14). `LlmProxyService.complete()` treats a primary cascade that ends in `outcome === 'request_error'` (every candidate returned 400/422) as "the caller's payload is malformed" and **skips** the guaranteed backstop (so it surfaces the schema diagnostic instead of double-billing a doomed retry). That assumption is wrong when the 400 is *vendor-specific* (e.g. Ollama's `"Value looks like object…"` on a tools payload that Anthropic/DeepSeek accept). The exec #61 trigger is now removed two ways — Ollama is excluded from auto-routed pools and cloud coding runs cascade only within the curated coding pool (`codingOnly`), so a request-error finish is now unlikely — but the short-circuit itself is unchanged. Deferred: fire the *coding* backstop (`CODING_BACKSTOP_MODELS`, a paid coder) even on `request_error`, since a paid coder is the most likely to accept a payload that quirky free vendors rejected. Unblocks: "a coding run always falls over to a paid coder" holds even in the all-400 edge.
- **`PATCH /api/approvals/:id` does not enforce the MANAGER+ role its own contract claims** (2026-06-14). The route's doc header says "tenant JWT, MANAGER+", but the handler (`approvalRoutes.ts`) only runs `authMiddleware` — any authenticated tenant user can approve/reject/answer a request, including the new `task.execution` execution-approval gate (which, as of this pass, now *auto-starts the run* on approve via `dispatchCloudRunForTask`). So a non-manager can both clear the governance gate and trigger the (billable) run. Surfaced while wiring the inline `ApprovalResolveControl`; not fixed here because role-gating writes is a deliberate access-control change (need the canonical role check helper + a decision on which roles may approve which `actionType`s). Deferred (T7 — governance): enforce role on the PATCH (and ideally scope by action type / approval rule). Unblocks: the execution-approval gate is real authorization, not an honor-system label. Note the inline approve UI already degrades safely — a forbidden PATCH surfaces its error in the control — so the only missing piece is the server-side role check.

### ✅ Done / Resolved (53)

_Resolved/closed register items, grouped by the work they came from. Newest dates win; `git log` is the full audit trail._

#### 🧠 Brain conversation rendering (4)

- **Brain agent loop now survives Brain-initiated navigation — FIXED 2026-06-14 (`brain-embedded/src/brainRunStore.ts` (new) + `useBrainConversation.ts` + `frontend/.../PlatformActionsBridge.tsx`, `BrainPanel.tsx`).** When the Brain navigated the user (`navigate_to`/`open_project`) off the full-page `/brainstorm` or the IDE-embedded Brain, the route-scoped panel unmounted mid-run: the loop's state (rich transcript, trace, streaming delta, confirm resolver) lived in that component's refs, so the run was orphaned, the freshly mounted instance lost all grounding, and — worst — it re-answered the trailing user message, spawning a **second concurrent loop** (duplicate writes). Fix: the tool-loop is hoisted into a module-level singleton (`brainRunStore`) keyed by chatId, **single-flight** per chat; any mounted Brain instance subscribes to the same run cell and renders the live run, and a second instance that tries to start the same chat is a no-op. The human-in-the-loop confirm gate also moved into the store, so a navigation that swaps which panel is mounted can still resolve a pending confirmation. `PlatformActionsBridge` force-opens the floating drawer on Brain-initiated nav and `BrainPanel` (page variant) mirrors its active chat into `BrainContext`, so the drawer resumes the exact conversation. Residual (memory eviction) logged above.
- **Brain drawer still closed on navigation paths the 2026-06-14 fix didn't cover — FIXED 2026-06-16 (`brain-embedded/src/BrainContext.tsx` + `frontend/src/components/ChatMessageContent.tsx`).** The above fix kept the Brain open only across its own `navigate_to`/`open_project` tool calls (which `router.push` + `setOpen(true)`). Two other navigation paths still silently closed the drawer: (1) **internal links the model writes in its replies** (e.g. "[the backlog](/projects/11)") rendered as `<a href target="_blank">` — a hard navigation/new-tab that remounts the provider tree and resets `open` to its `useState(false)` default (the system prompt tells the model to prefer `navigate_to`, but it frequently emits markdown links anyway); (2) any hard reload / external deep-link entry, since `open` lived only in volatile React state. Fix: `ChatMessageContent`'s link renderer now routes same-origin paths through the Next router client-side (honouring modifier-clicks for new-tab) so the persistent drawer stays mounted, and `BrainContextProvider` persists `open` + `activeChatId` to **sessionStorage** (per-tab; SSR-safe rehydrate-on-mount to avoid a hydration mismatch) so the drawer reopens on its exact conversation after any remount. Covered by `BrainContext.test.tsx` (persist/rehydrate open, resume active chat, honour a manual close). Together with the 2026-06-14 run-store hoist, the Brain now survives **every** navigation, not just its own tool-driven hops.
- **Brain reused the streaming bubble and erased a turn's narration — FIXED 2026-06-14 (`brain-embedded/brainRunStore.ts` + `useBrainConversation.ts`).** The agent tool-loop streamed every model turn into one shared `streamingText` buffer that the UI rendered as a single trailing bubble; a turn that narrated *and* called a tool showed its text only transiently, then the next iteration cleared the buffer and reused the same bubble — erasing what the user just read (only the final answer was ever persisted). Fix: each turn that produces visible text now persists as its own durable message block, delivered to mounted views as the full run-appended list (merged by id) so React's coalescing of the rapid mid-run emits can't drop the intermediate narration turns. Pure tool-call turns with no text persist nothing. Covered by two new tests in `useBrainConversation.test.tsx`.
- **Brain rendered inline `<tool_call>…</tool_call>` markup as text AND never ran the call — FIXED 2026-06-14 (`brain-embedded/src/xmlToolCalls.ts` (new) + `streamChatCompletion.ts`).** `streamChatCompletion` only parsed native OpenAI-structured `tool_calls` deltas; models that emit calls inline in the content stream as `<tool_call>delete_task<arg_key>id</arg_key><arg_value>75</arg_value></tool_call>` had that markup shown verbatim in the bubble — and, worse, the call **never executed** (the agent loop only runs structured `toolCalls`), so the Brain "said" it deleted #75 but did nothing. Fix: a streaming-safe `XmlToolCallFilter` lifts inline calls into the same `AssembledToolCall` shape (coercing arg types, so `id` → `75` not `"75"`), strips the markup from the visible/persisted text, and is robust to tags split across stream chunks; native deltas still take precedence. Covered by `xmlToolCalls.test.ts` (8 cases) + a streaming integration test in `streamChatCompletion.test.ts`.
- **Brain run-store cells were session-lived in memory with no eviction — FIXED 2026-06-14 (`brain-embedded/src/brainRunStore.ts`).** Hoisting the agent loop out of React (so a run survives navigation) moved each chat's rich transcript + trace + appended-message list from per-instance refs (freed on unmount) into a module-level `Map` keyed by chatId that lived for the whole browser session — so a long session touching many chats grew client memory unbounded. Fix: the `Map` is now an LRU bounded to `MAX_CELLS` (50), evicting least-recently-used **idle** cells (never an in-flight run, a cell with a mounted subscriber, or the cell just created for a mounting view); a re-visited evicted chat rebuilds its cell and reloads visible history from persistence (same grounding loss as a page reload). Per-cell, the trace (`MAX_TRACE_EVENTS` 500) and the live-append buffer (`MAX_APPENDED` 50, via shared `recordAppended`) are also capped so a single marathon chat stays bounded. Covered by `brainRunStore.test.ts` (cap, subscriber-protection, LRU recency).

#### 🏷️ CoderClaw → BuilderForce rebrand (15)

- **Broken image assets from the rename are now FIXED (frontend).** Root cause: the file sweep
  excluded binary extensions, so `.png` *references* got rebranded but the *files* didn't —
  `/claw.png`→`/agentHost.png` (11 refs) and `coderclaw.png`→`/agents.png` (2 refs on `/agents`)
  pointed at non-existent files (404 in prod; the report showed a `522` on `/agentHost.png`, but that
  `522` is Cloudflare-can't-reach-origin — a **deploy/infra** issue, separate from the missing file).
  Fix: renamed `public/claw.png`→`agentHost.png`, restored `coderclaw.png` as `public/agents.png`,
  fixed `public/sw.js` precache + bumped its cache `v1`→`v2`. All `src` asset refs now resolve;
  docs-site + agent-runtime/ui were checked and have no `claw`/`agent*` image-ref breakage. CAUTION
  for future asset sweeps: an image is only "dead" if NO reference (including its *renamed* form)
  resolves to it — I briefly mis-deleted `coderclaw.png` before realising `/agents.png` was its
  orphaned reference, and recovered it from `git show HEAD:`.

- **`frontend/public/install.ps1` crash + stale URLs FIXED; deeper connect-agent flow mismatch LOGGED.**
  Root cause (again): the rename sweep covered `frontend/src` but **not `frontend/public/`**, so
  `install.ps1` still had `worker.coderclaw.ai` (dead) as its default `$ApiUrl` and `coderclaw.ai`
  in docs. Worse, it called `exit` on failure — and the Workforce "Connect a new agent" one-liner
  runs it via `iwr | iex` (in-process), where `exit` **terminates the user's PowerShell session**
  (the reported "crash"). Fixed: URLs → `api.builderforce.ai`/`builderforce.ai`, and every `exit N`
  → `return` so a failure ends the script without killing the host shell.

- **Connect-a-new-agent flow REWRITTEN end-to-end (was: install.ps1 ignored the token).** `install.ps1`
  was a *marketplace-agent registry browser* — it ignored `$env:BUILDERFORCE_TOKEN` /
  `$env:BUILDERFORCE_WORKSPACE` and never registered the machine. Rewrote it to: preflight Node/npm →
  `npm i -g @seanhogg/builderforce-agents` → `builderforce connect` → `builderforce gateway`. Added a
  **new headless `builderforce connect`** command ([builderforce-connect.ts](agent-runtime/src/commands/builderforce-connect.ts),
  [register.connect.ts](agent-runtime/src/cli/program/register.connect.ts)) that reads the token from
  env, `POST`s `/api/agent-hosts`, writes the link key to `~/.builderforce/.env`
  (`BUILDERFORCE_API_KEY`/`URL`) and the host id into project context (which the gateway reads to
  connect). tsgo clean. **Prerequisite to actually run:** `@seanhogg/builderforce-agents` must be
  **published to npm** (still blocked — `npm whoami` 401); until then step 2 of install.ps1 404s
  (handled gracefully).

- **Runtime↔server WIRE CONTRACT was split by the rebrand and is now realigned (the real flow break).**
  The product rename used `claw`→`agentNode` but the API uses `claw`→`agent_host`, so the two halves
  of the SAME wire contract diverged. Fixed in `agent-runtime/src`: **API paths** `/api/agentNodes…`
  → `/api/agent-hosts…` (35 occurrences, 20 files — registration/heartbeat/forward/sync/relay/cron/
  skills/personas all were 404ing); **headers** `X-AgentNode-*` → `X-AgentHost-*` (9, matches the
  server's `X-AgentHost-From/Id/Signature`); **registration response** `res.agentNode` →
  `res.agentHost` (server returns `{agentHost, apiKey}`). tsgo clean. **REMAINING audit (logged):**
  other JSON body fields still carry runtime-side names — `fromAgentNodeId`/`callbackAgentNodeId`
  (forward), assignment-context, etc. in [api-contract.ts](agent-runtime/src/infra/api-contract.ts) —
  each must be verified against its server endpoint's field names; not swept blindly to avoid new
  mismatches. Also `workforce-agent.ts` reads `BUILDERFORCE_AGENTS_LINK_API_KEY` while the rest of the
  runtime uses `BUILDERFORCE_API_KEY` — align to one.

- **The "coderclaw" still visible on `/workforce` was DATA, not code** — the tenant/workgroup row
  (`tenants.id=1`) was literally named/slugged `coderclaw`. `frontend/src` has **0** `coderclaw`
  refs; the page interpolates the workgroup name. Renamed the tenant → `name='BuilderForce'`,
  `slug='builderforce'` (0 `agent_hosts` referenced it, so the slug change was safe) and added a
  `(workspace)` indicator next to the name in `TopBar.tsx`. Remaining `coderclaw` in `api/src` (7)
  are comments + intentional back-compat (GitHub dispatch label, `coderclawllm/` model-id prefix).

- **Two CI failures from the rebrand are now FIXED + verified** (root cause: `tsc`/`tsgo` were used
  as the local gate, but they don't run the checks CI does). (1) **Frontend** — `blogData.ts`
  imported `@/content/blog/agents-and-agent-integration.md` while the renamed file is
  `builderforce-agents-and-agent-integration.md`; `tsc` can't resolve vite's markdown-alias imports
  so it slipped through. Fixed the import; full `vitest run` now green (17 files / 153 tests).
  (2) **API `npm run check:schema`** — `check-schema-drift.mjs` statically parsed only `CREATE TABLE`
  / `ADD COLUMN`, so it couldn't follow migration 0078's dynamic `DO`-block `claw`→`agent_host`
  renames and flagged 21 `agent_host_*` columns/tables as "uncreated". My first instinct (grandfather
  the 21) was WRONG — that masks drift instead of proving schema.ts matches the migrations. **Proper
  fix shipped:** made the checker **rename-aware** — it now follows explicit `ALTER … RENAME TO` /
  `RENAME COLUMN` statements AND declarative `-- @schema-drift-rename-table` /
  `-- @schema-drift-rename-replace` directives (added to 0078, comments only — execution unchanged,
  since the dynamic loop is more complete than any explicit list). The 16 migration-created `claw_id`
  columns + 4 workspace tables now **resolve through the rename (NOT grandfathered)**; only the genuine
  baseline-push (`drizzle-kit push`) items remain grandfathered (93, down from the masking 106). `npm
  test` green (schema check + 350 tests). **Lesson:** the real gates are `npm test` (api),
  `pnpm test`/`vitest run` (frontend), `pnpm build` (agent-runtime) — not just type checks.

- **Migration 0078 is APPLIED + verified live** (`npm run db:migrate`, 2026-06-03): the configured
  Neon DB now has `agent_hosts` (+ all `agent_host_*` tables), `assignment_scope` = `{agent, host,
  project, task, tenant}`, and **0 columns still containing "claw"**. It is metadata-only renames in
  one atomic, idempotent `DO` block (rollback script in `api/scripts/`). NOTE: deploy the renamed
  `api` in lockstep — any still-running pre-rebrand worker against this DB now needs the new code
  (the `/api/claws` alias covers in-flight field agents).

- **Back-compat alias routes `/api/claws` + `/api/managed-claws` were added** ([index.ts](api/src/index.ts))
  so already-deployed field agents (pre-rebrand) keep working. They forward to the new
  `/api/agent-hosts` handlers. Removing them once the deployed agent fleet has upgraded unblocks a
  clean route surface; leaving them indefinitely is harmless but is brand debt.

- **Backwards-compat brand strings intentionally left intact**: the GitHub dispatch label
  `'coderclaw'` ([githubWebhookRoutes.ts](api/src/presentation/routes/githubWebhookRoutes.ts)) and
  the `coderclawllm/workforce-*` model-id prefix ([ideAiRoutes.ts](api/src/presentation/routes/ideAiRoutes.ts))
  still accept the old token for existing integrations. Adding the new `builderforce`/`agent` token
  (keeping both) and later dropping the old one unblocks full brand removal without breaking callers.

- **Frontend (`frontend/src`) is now rebranded + verified** (`tsc` clean): `Claw*`→`AgentHost*`
  components, API client, the marketing route moved `app/coderclaw`→`app/agents` with a
  `/coderclaw`→`/agents` redirect ([next.config.js](frontend/next.config.js)), WS event names
  aligned to the API. The `runtime_support` value `'claw'`→`'host'`. Intentionally preserved: the
  separate **OpenClaw** upstream refs and the external malware IOC `ClawdAuthenticatorTool` in
  `data/agents/threats.yaml`.

- **Docs-site + cross-repo prose are now rebranded** (Phases 5–6): `docs-site` `coderclaw-*.md`
  → `agents-*.md` (609 docs reworded, Astro + `_redirects` slug redirects added, logo + GitHub
  URL updated); root `README.md`, `mambacodejs/README.md`, `SSMjs/README.md`, `ide-architecture`
  reworded. **Follow-up:** the docs-site still has ~90 **code-example identifiers** (`clawId`,
  `ClawRelayDO`, `claw_fleet`, `CLAWHUB_*`, `ClawLink*`) left from before the product rename. They
  now need reconciling with the final code, minding the split: **platform** concepts use the
  `AgentHost` family (e.g. `ClawRelayDO`→`AgentHostRelayDO`, `/api/claws`→`/api/agent-hosts`) while
  **product/runtime** concepts use the `AgentNode`/`AgentHub`/`agent_fleet` family. Left unswept to
  avoid a wrong blind rename across the two namespaces.

- **The CoderClaw product is now fully renamed AND folded into this monorepo at `agent-runtime/`
  (Phase 4 complete).** The whole product (`@seanhogg/builderforce-agents`, CLI `builderforce`,
  binary `builderforce.mjs`) was deep-renamed: `CoderClaw*`→`BuilderForceAgents*`, bare
  `Claw`→`AgentNode`, `ClawLink`→`AgentLink`, `ClawHub`→`AgentHub`, the runtime workspace dir
  `.coderClaw/`→`.builderforce/`, `CODERCLAW_*`→`BUILDERFORCE_AGENTS_*` env, and the 40
  `coderclaw.plugin.json` manifests → `builderforce.plugin.json` (files + discovery code). The
  product's `tsgo` typecheck passed **0 errors**, then it was moved to `agent-runtime/` and
  **`pnpm install` + `tsgo` + `pnpm build` all pass green** (build: 287 bundles, plugin-sdk dts
  compiled, exit 0), and the full **`pnpm test` suite ran (6435 tests)**. The initial run surfaced
  two failure classes, both now resolved: (a) **rename-induced test-data inconsistencies** —
  `CoderClaw`→`BuilderForceAgents` (no space) vs `coderclaw`→`builderforce` made brand strings in 4
  test files diverge (discord slug `friends-of-builderforce` vs normalized `…agents`, an
