#### 🔧 Engine & runtime consolidation (2)

- **✅ V1 RETIRED (operator decision executed 2026-06-13) — `builderforce-v2` is the consolidated default on every surface; V1 is no longer creatable or default.** Implemented + `tsc` 0 across all 4 packages: (1) `DEFAULT_ENGINE_ID` = `ENGINE_IDS.v2` in [`@builderforce/agent-tools` engine.ts](packages/agent-tools/src/engine.ts) — ONE constant flips the on-prem relay `resolveEngine`, cloud `resolveCloudAgent`, `workforceRoutes` create-default, and the `task.assign` fallback together; (2) on-prem **`runV1Engine` DELETED** + its `resolveEngine` registry entry removed ([builderforce-relay.ts](agent-runtime/src/infra/builderforce-relay.ts)) — a legacy `engine:"builderforce-v1"` now falls through to v2; (3) **creation restricted to v2** — `AGENT_ENGINES = ['builderforce-v2']` ([workforceRoutes.ts](api/src/presentation/routes/workforceRoutes.ts)) + frontend `AgentEngine` narrowed to `'builderforce-v2'` (api.ts/types.ts/CloudAgentFormFields/SlideOutPanel/platformActions); (4) **migration [0120_engine_v2_retire_v1.sql](api/migrations/0120_engine_v2_retire_v1.sql)** back-fills legacy `ide_agents.engine` v1→v2 + flips the column default (was v1 in 0087). KEY finding: `builderforce-local` is **on-prem-only** (frontend/api accept only v1|v2), so the prior PRD "flip default → builderforce-local" plan would have BROKEN cloud — `builderforce-v2` is the only valid cross-surface engine. **Remaining V1-retirement tail (deploy-gated / dead-code):** (a) the **cloud V1 dispatch branch** still exists as now-unreachable runtime code — the `isV2 === false` else-path in [runtimeRoutes.ts](api/src/presentation/routes/runtimeRoutes.ts) (~L430) + `cloudAgentTypeLabel`'s V1 arm; removing it needs cloud tracing + a deploy to verify; (b) **dormant on-prem dead code** — `pendingTaskRun` + `flushPendingTaskChanges` (only `runV1Engine` set `pendingTaskRun`; reads are null-guarded so harmless, but now unreachable-for-purpose — clean up); (c) **migration 0120 must be applied** (live DB) + a **live e2e** confirming new agents run on V2; (d) README "V1 Cloud Agent" agent-type docs (§ near L854) + migration 0087 header are now historical. **(e) OPEN QUESTION the cutover exposed — is `builderforce-local` now dead?** Creation is v2-only and the default `builderforce-v2` = the Claude-Agent-SDK runner (`runV2Engine`), so no agent carries `engine:"builderforce-local"` → the relay's `local` entry + `runLocalEngine` + the entire on-prem `LocalAgentEngine`/`@builderforce/agent-tools` Node engine are unselectable. Two readings of "V2" collide (literal `builderforce-v2`=Claude SDK vs the parity-plan's "surface-agnostic V2 engine"=the shared-registry `LocalAgentEngine`). Operator must pick: (a) confirm Claude-SDK-V2 canonical on-prem → DELETE `builderforce-local`/`runLocalEngine`/the Node `LocalAgentEngine` as dead code (codebase reduction; discards the §5.2 `local` wins), OR (b) route on-prem through `local` and make Claude-SDK the cloud-only path → make `local` selectable. See PRD §5.5. Fixing unblocks: a single, unambiguous on-prem engine with zero unreferenced engine code.

- **✅ RESOLVED 2026-06-13 — `agent-runtime` `tsc --noEmit` is now GREEN (0 errors), and the `loadJsonFile` sync→async drift is fully propagated.** The root cause was [json-file.ts](agent-runtime/src/infra/json-file.ts) `loadJsonFile` being made `async` (returning `Promise<unknown>`) without updating its synchronous callers (plus a missing `os` import in [subagent-registry.store.ts](agent-runtime/src/agents/subagent-registry.store.ts)). Per the operator directive ("make it all async", not sync), `loadJsonFile` was KEPT async and `await` was propagated through the ENTIRE auth/credential/model subsystem: the auth-profile store loaders (`loadAuthProfileStore`/`loadAuthProfileStoreForAgent`/`ensureAuthProfileStore`/`updateAuthProfileStoreWithLock`), the external-CLI credential readers ([cli-credentials.ts](agent-runtime/src/agents/cli-credentials.ts) — Claude/Codex/Qwen/MiniMax read+cached + the file-write path) and `syncExternalCliCredentials`, the subagent registry read path (`getRunsSnapshotForRead` → `findRunIdsByChildSessionKey`/`resolveRequesterForChildSession`/`countActiveRunsForSession`/`countActiveDescendantRuns`/`listDescendantRunsForRequester`/`isSubagentSessionRunActive`/`markSubagentRunTerminated`, and their callers in subagent-announce/spawn/tools, auto-reply abort, and the cron isolated-agent runner), the telegram sticker cache, and the model-auth hub (`resolveApiKeyForProvider`/`resolveModelAuthMode`/`resolveModelAuthLabel`/`normalizeProviders`/`resolveModelSelectionFromDirective`/`createProviderAuthChecker`/`resolveImageModelConfigForTool` + their consumers across `commands/*`, `provider-usage.auth.ts`, `directive-handling.*`, `status.ts`, `model-picker.ts`, `model-fallback.ts`). Sync-contract sites were handled structurally: the `image` tool factory stays SYNC (it runs in the synchronous tool-assembly) and resolves its model config lazily inside the async `execute`; the model-picker auth predicate stays a sync `(provider)=>boolean` over a store preloaded by its now-async factory. Verified: `agent-runtime` `tsc --noEmit` exits 0 (production + tests). **Corrected 2026-06-13 (this pass):** the same drift had survived in [github-copilot-token.ts](agent-runtime/src/providers/github-copilot-token.ts) — its injectable `loadJsonFileImpl`/`saveJsonFileImpl` seams were typed SYNC (`=> unknown` / `=> void`) while their defaults are the now-async `loadJsonFile`/`saveJsonFile`, and the call sites did NOT `await`. tsc stayed green because `Promise<unknown>` is assignable to `unknown`, so the type masked the bug: in production the cache read returned a `Promise`, `cached.token` was always `undefined`, the valid cache was never honored, and a fresh token was fetched on every call (the save was a fire-and-forget write). Fixed by widening the seams to `=> unknown | Promise<unknown>` / `=> void | Promise<void>` and `await`ing both calls — and a regression test now exercises an async (Promise-returning) loader and asserts the cache is honored. **Residual:** behavioral test execution (vitest) across the OTHER changed credential/subagent/model-auth paths was NOT run in this pass (type-safety verified, but the sync→async semantics change warrants a full `pnpm test` run on agent-runtime before release).

#### 🔐 Multi-tenant, governance & embed (3)

- **[ACCEPTED BY DESIGN 2026-05-31] Identity federation uses a shared-secret HS256 token, not OIDC issuer verification (spec §2.1 + §7 item 1).** [JwtService.verifyJwt](api/src/infrastructure/auth/JwtService.ts) verifies an HMAC-SHA-256 signature against a single shared `JWT_SECRET`; the federation token carries no `iss` claim and [authMiddleware](api/src/presentation/middleware/authMiddleware.ts) does no issuer/`tenants.idp_issuer` check. The spec's wording (BurnRateOS as an OIDC IdP verified by asymmetric issuer + signature) is **intentionally not implemented**: BurnRateOS and BuilderForce are first-party apps with a co-managed secret, so the symmetric model is accepted. Residual risk acknowledged (a secret leak lets either side forge the other's tokens; no cryptographic IdP boundary; `persona`/`plan` claims absent, so plan-based gating falls back to `role` + the segment's `plan`). Revisit only if a non-first-party host ever federates in — then move to RS256/JWKS keyed by the already-present `tenants.idp_issuer` column. No code change this pass.

- **Segment tier foundation + write-isolation + provisioning — LANDED ([0054](api/migrations/0054_segment_tier.sql), [0056](api/migrations/0056_segment_id_propagation.sql), [segmentResolver](api/src/infrastructure/auth/segmentResolver.ts), [segmentRoutes](api/src/presentation/routes/segmentRoutes.ts)).** Shipped + applied + verified: the `segments` table + tenant `kind`/`idp_issuer`/`isolation_mode`/`settings` columns + one default segment per tenant (0054); `segment_id` (NOT NULL in DB, optional in TS) on 34 business tables + `tasks` via project, backfilled to each tenant's default (0056); a DB-level default-fill trigger that auto-stamps the default segment for `single` tenants and RAISEs for `segmented` tenants (the no-bleed hard rule enforced at the DB — verified: single fills, segmented rejects); `resolveSegment()` chokepoint (default for single, lazy-create from account/company claims for segmented, cached) wired into [authMiddleware](api/src/presentation/middleware/authMiddleware.ts) setting `c.get('segmentId')`; and `GET/POST/PATCH /api/segments` provisioning. Unit + full suite green (108 tests). **Still open** — see the four bullets below.

- **[FOOT-GUN FIXED 2026-06-13 — operator env-set remains] `NEXT_PUBLIC_EMBED_ALLOWED_HOST_ORIGINS` must be set in prod to enable embedding.** The single allowlist drives both the `/embed/*` `frame-ancestors` CSP (middleware) and the client-side auth-origin check ([useEmbedFrame](frontend/src/lib/embed/useEmbedFrame.ts)). **The default-OPEN foot-gun is closed:** the trust decision was extracted to the pure [isTrustedHostOrigin](frontend/src/lib/embed/embedTrust.ts) (+unit tests) and the frame is now **default-CLOSED in production** when the allowlist is empty (rejects all origins, mirroring the `frame-ancestors 'self'` CSP so both layers fail the same way), while staying open in dev for cross-origin convenience. **Residual (operator):** an empty allowlist in prod now blocks embedding entirely (safe but non-functional) — so to actually *enable* embedding the env must be set to the BurnRateOS origins per environment. No code change available for the env-set.

#### 🚀 Growth, SEO & onboarding (5)

- **✅ COMPLETED 2026-06-14 — programmatic SEO leaf pages shipped.** New statically-generated `/compare/{slug}` (7 competitors, driven by `COMPETITOR_SEO` + the existing `COMPETITIVE_COMPARISON` matrix) and `/integrations/{slug}` (10 tools, `SEO_INTEGRATIONS`) routes plus an `/integrations` index — each with `generateStaticParams`/`generateMetadata`/JSON-LD (`competitorCompareSchema`/`integrationSchema`) + a dynamic `opengraph-image`, emitted into [sitemap.ts](frontend/src/app/sitemap.ts) and allowed in [robots.txt](frontend/public/robots.txt). Bounded data tables live in [content.ts](frontend/src/lib/content.ts) (single source of truth). frontend `tsc` 0, eslint clean. ORIGINAL GAP: **No programmatic SEO surface for integrations or competitor comparisons.** The new [/product](frontend/src/app/product/page.tsx) page (added this pass) is the capability *hub*, and [agents/integrations](frontend/src/app/agents/integrations/page.tsx) lists integrations, but there are no per-integration (`/integrations/{tool}`) or per-comparison (`/compare/{competitor}`) leaf pages to capture long-tail search intent — the bounded-generation play the marketing-presence review recommended in place of the (irrelevant for a B2B gateway) geo/local-SEO pattern. Fixing (a bounded set of statically-generated leaf pages driven by a data table in [content.ts](frontend/src/lib/content.ts), each with `generateMetadata` + JSON-LD + sitemap entries) unblocks: search capture for "Builderforce + {tool}" and "{competitor} alternative" queries without thin-page bloat.

- **✅ COMPLETED 2026-06-14.** Added [frontend/src/app/projects/[id]/layout.tsx](frontend/src/app/projects/%5Bid%5D/layout.tsx) with `generateMetadata` setting a self-referential `canonical: /projects/{id}` + `robots: { index:false, follow:false }`, so a detail route no longer advertises the `/projects` list canonical or its SoftwareApplication/ItemList graph. ORIGINAL GAP: **`/projects/[id]` inherits the Projects/Tasks JSON-LD + canonical from the shared route layout.** The new [frontend/src/app/projects/layout.tsx](frontend/src/app/projects/layout.tsx) emits `projectsTasksSchema()` and a `canonical: /projects` for the whole `/projects` segment, so a project *detail* route (`/projects/123`) currently advertises the list page's SoftwareApplication graph and canonical. Harmless today (detail pages are auth-gated and not meant to be indexed), but if per-project detail SEO is ever wanted, give `/projects/[id]` its own `generateMetadata` + a `CreativeWork`/`Project`-style schema. Fixing unblocks: correct per-project canonical + structured data if project pages become publicly shareable.

- **✅ COMPLETED 2026-06-14 — installer env wiring done on both OSes.** [install.ps1](frontend/public/install.ps1) already read `BUILDERFORCE_TOKEN`/`BUILDERFORCE_URL` and ran `builderforce connect` (rebrand/connect pass). Rewrote the legacy CoderClaw [install.sh](frontend/public/install.sh) to mirror it: reads `BUILDERFORCE_TOKEN`/`WORKSPACE`/`URL`/`TAG`, `npm i -g @seanhogg/builderforce-agents`, then `builderforce connect` + `gateway`; 0 `coderclaw` refs, `bash -n` clean. The `/workforce` "Connect a new agent" one-liner now registers straight into the workgroup on macOS/Linux too. ORIGINAL GAP: **Configured-quickstart popover emits `BUILDERFORCE_TOKEN`/`BUILDERFORCE_WORKSPACE` env vars the installer scripts don't yet read.** The new caret on the Workforce "Add agent" split button ([ConfiguredQuickstartPopover](frontend/src/components/workforce/ConfiguredQuickstartPopover.tsx)) renders the install one-liner pre-configured for the selected workgroup by prefixing `BUILDERFORCE_TOKEN="<tenantToken>"` and `BUILDERFORCE_WORKSPACE="<slug>"`. But [install.ps1](frontend/public/install.ps1) (and the `install.sh` it references) never read those env vars — so today the command installs the agent but does NOT auto-register it into the workgroup; the user still onboards manually. Fixing (have install.ps1/install.sh read `$env:BUILDERFORCE_TOKEN`/`$env:BUILDERFORCE_WORKSPACE`, and pass them into `builderforce onboard` non-interactively to register the agentHost against that workgroup) unblocks: the popover's "installs and registers straight into this workgroup" promise actually holding end-to-end. Note the same script also still hard-codes legacy `coderclaw.ai` URLs + `$env:USERPROFILE\.builderforce` defaults in its `.SYNOPSIS`/params — reconcile to `builderforce.ai` in the same pass.

- **✅ COMPLETED 2026-06-14 — cold-invite email shipped.** The pending-invite branch of `POST /api/tenants/:id/invite-by-email` ([tenantRoutes.ts](api/src/presentation/routes/tenantRoutes.ts)) now sends a `sendWorkspaceInviteEmail` ([EmailService.ts](api/src/infrastructure/email/EmailService.ts), Resend, best-effort — no-ops without `RESEND_API_KEY`): it names the inviter + workspace + role and links to `/register?email=<invited>` so the pending `tenant_invitations` row auto-converts on first login. api `tsc` 0. ORIGINAL GAP: **Workspace invitations send no email/notification.** `POST /api/tenants/:id/invite-by-email` ([tenantRoutes.ts](api/src/presentation/routes/tenantRoutes.ts)) now records a pending `tenant_invitations` row (migration 0114) for an email with no Builderforce account, and it auto-converts to a membership on that user's next `GET /api/tenants/mine` — but the invitee is never *told* they were invited. They only "land" if they independently sign up with the same email. Fixing (send an invite email with a signup link on the pending path, and/or surface "you've been invited to N workspaces" on the tenant picker) unblocks: true cold invites to people who don't already use the product.

- **✅ RESOLVED 2026-06-14 — superseded by the `workflow_triggers` webhook transport (no new code).** A data-collection trigger that must receive an inbound payload is configured as `triggerType:'webhook'`, which mints a per-trigger token (`workflow_triggers.token`) + a public `POST /api/workflow-triggers/hook/:token` ([workflowTriggerRoutes.ts](api/src/presentation/routes/workflowTriggerRoutes.ts), HMAC-verified via `X-Signature`) that `instantiateWorkflowRun` fires with the posted body as the trigger node output — exactly this gap’s capability, via a per-trigger-node token (better than the per-definition token originally proposed). Labels with no autonomous transport (form-submit/signup/purchase/…) stay manual-only by design ([workflowTriggers.ts](api/src/domain/workflowTriggers.ts)). Building `/api/ingest/:token` would have duplicated it. ORIGINAL GAP: **Inbound data-collection ingest endpoint is not implemented — marketing triggers can't actually fire.** Data-collection trigger types (form-submit, webhook, page-view, signup, purchase, email-open/click, rss, inbound-email) and trigger integrations (Typeform, Stripe, Segment, …) are configurable + persist + compile, but there is no public HTTP endpoint that RECEIVES an inbound payload and starts a run. Needs a per-definition ingest token (column on `workflow_definitions` + migration), a default agent-host for the run, and a public `POST /api/ingest/:token` route that seeds the trigger node's output with the posted body and instantiates a run (reusing the `/run` compile path). Fixing unblocks: workflows that genuinely fire from collected marketing data (the "marketing platform with triggers" use case).

#### 🧹 Quality & token-cost (1)

- **Token-cost pass — VERIFIED NOT BUGS (do not re-audit):** Two claims from the first-pass review were refuted on direct inspection. (a) *agent-runtime "doesn't enable Anthropic caching"* — false: [config/defaults.ts](agent-runtime/src/config/defaults.ts) force-defaults `cacheRetention: "short"` on every Anthropic model (and the primary) under `api_key` auth, which flows through `applyExtraParamsToAgent` → `resolveCacheRetention` → pi-ai `streamSimple`'s `cacheRetention` stream option (which applies the `cache_control` breakpoint). Caching is ON by default. (b) *gateway "strips `cache_control`"* — false: messages are forwarded verbatim ([LlmProxyService.dispatch](api/src/application/llm/LlmProxyService.ts) casts `messages` through and [openrouter buildBody](api/src/application/llm/vendors/openrouter.ts) passes them untouched; [sanitizeRequestToolNames](api/src/application/llm/toolNameSanitizer.ts) spreads `{...m}` preserving `content`). `cache_control` is nested in `messages[].content[]`, not a top-level field, so `stripStandardFields` never touches it. Tenant-set caching survives the proxy today.

#### 🔀 Parallel-track sweep — 2026-06-14 (T1–T9, file-disjoint worktrees) (27)

- **✅ RESOLVED (MOOT) 2026-06-14 (T1) — the bespoke `.cc-nav` no longer exists.** This gap is stale: a repo-wide grep finds **zero `cc-nav` references, no `src/app/coderclaw/` directory, and no `MarketingNav.tsx`** anywhere in `frontend/src` — the CoderClaw marketing nav + its `.cc-nav` styles were already removed during the CoderClaw→BuilderForce rebrand (the `/coderclaw` route moved to `/agents`, whose `layout.tsx` is now a pass-through that inherits PublicShell's chrome). There is no longer a second bespoke marketing nav to fold into `MarketingHeader`, so nothing to migrate. ORIGINAL GAP: CoderClaw marketing nav (`.cc-nav`) was not migrated to the shared responsive `MarketingHeader` — generalize `MarketingHeader` to take a logo/brand + CTA and drive both navs from it.

- **✅ RESOLVED 2026-06-14 (T2).** `IDENew.tsx` adds a default-on "Gate Run" hard-gate when checks fail + synthesizes a minimal `tsconfig.json` into the WebContainer for the TS-without-tsconfig fallback. ORIGINAL GAP: **In-browser checks (`tsc`/lint/build) run on demand but don't gate Run, and may false-fail TS-without-tsconfig.** This pass added a "✓ Check" action ([IDENew.tsx](frontend/src/components/IDENew.tsx) `handleCheck`) that runs type-check/lint/build inside the WebContainer from the project's own scripts and shows a pass/fail badge; Run displays the last result but does **not** block on failure (the user can still serve a broken preview). Also: the type-check fallback (`npx tsc --noEmit` when `typescript` is a dep but no `typecheck` script exists) will fail noisily on a project that ships TS without a `tsconfig.json`. Fixing (optionally hard-gate Run behind a passing check, and synthesize a minimal tsconfig for the fallback) unblocks: a true "code must be good before it runs" gate.

- **✅ RESOLVED 2026-06-14 (T2).** both tools now route through a shared `ArtifactReviewModals` (reused by the button path); `run()` awaits confirm/cancel before save. ORIGINAL GAP: **The Brain's `generate_prd` / `generate_tasks` tools auto-save without the review modal.** When the user clicks the **Generate PRD / Generate Tasks** message-action buttons ([ChatProjectActions.tsx](frontend/src/components/ChatProjectActions.tsx)) they get a preview modal before saving. When the Brain calls the equivalent `generate_prd` / `generate_tasks` tools registered by the IDE ([IDENew.tsx](frontend/src/components/IDENew.tsx)), it saves directly via the shared [projectArtifacts.ts](frontend/src/lib/brain/projectArtifacts.ts) `savePrd`/`saveTasks` — no human confirmation step. Acceptable for an agentic "do it for me" flow, but inconsistent with the button path. Fixing (route tool-driven artifact creation through a confirm affordance in the drawer, or add an undo) unblocks: consistent review-before-save UX across manual and AI-driven artifact generation.

- **✅ RESOLVED 2026-06-14 (T2).** active-chat selection hoisted into shared `BrainContext`; `useBrainChats` controlled mode syncs co-mounted docked instances. ORIGINAL GAP: **Designer left-panel Brain and the global floating Brain are two independent `<BrainPanel>` instances pinned to the same project, so their local state can diverge.** Per the "keep both" product decision, [IDENew.tsx](frontend/src/components/IDENew.tsx) now renders `<BrainPanel variant="docked">` in the Designer left panel while [FloatingBrain](frontend/src/components/brain/FloatingBrain.tsx) still mounts its own. Both share the same backend chats, but `useBrainChats`/`useBrainConversation` keep per-instance React state — creating/renaming/selecting a chat in one won't reflect in the other until a refetch. Fixing (hoist the active-chat selection into shared `BrainContext`, or suppress the floating instance on `/ide` and reuse one) unblocks: a single coherent conversation across both entry points.

- **✅ RESOLVED 2026-06-14 (T2).** `Select.tsx` gains native-style keyboard type-ahead (buffer + startsWith/substring, commit-on-match); residual = drop now-defensive-only `select` color-scheme CSS. ORIGINAL GAP: **Dropdowns migrated to a custom `<Select>` (dark-mode white-on-white popup fixed at the root) — minor follow-ups only.** The earlier CSS-only attempt (`color-scheme` + forced `option` colors) can't survive Chrome/Windows, which honours `color` on `<option>` but ignores `background-color` and paints the popup light when the control has an author background → white text on a white popup. Closed this pass by [Select.tsx](frontend/src/components/Select.tsx): a drop-in replacement rendering its own themed, portaled popup (won't clip inside panel `overflow`) while keeping the native API surface (`<option>`/`<optgroup>` children, `value`/`defaultValue`, `onChange` receiving `{ target: { value } }`, plus `onClick`/`onBlur`/`autoFocus`/`disabled`). All 88 native `<select>` across 44 files were converted and [ThemeSelect](frontend/src/components/ThemeSelect.tsx) now delegates to it (one popup implementation); base trigger look is a low-specificity `.bf-select-trigger` class ([globals.css](frontend/src/app/globals.css)) so a caller's `className` (e.g. `.admin-select`) or inline `style` still wins. **Remaining follow-ups:** (a) no type-ahead / multi-char search on `<Select>` yet (arrow/Home/End/Enter/Escape work); (b) the `select`/`option` color-scheme rules left in globals.css are now defensive-only (no native `<select>` remains) and could be dropped once we're confident nothing reintroduces a raw `<select>`. Live in-browser dark-mode verification of a few converted surfaces (Brain "Acting as", PRD attach, TaskMgmt inline status/priority edit, admin) is still advisable since it couldn't be exercised headlessly.

- **✅ RESOLVED 2026-06-14 — one canonical footer; per-page footers dropped.** [AppFooter](frontend/src/components/AppFooter.tsx) gained a `variant` prop: `'legal'` (default — the slim version + Terms/Privacy strip used by the height-constrained login/register `FooterOnlyShell`, unchanged) and `'full'` (the same legal strip PLUS the `FOOTER_LINKS` site-links + "Built by … © {BRAND.year}" copyright, styled inline since the `global-footer` classes live in T2-owned `globals.css`). [PublicShell](frontend/src/components/PublicShell.tsx) now renders `<AppFooter variant="full" />` once at the bottom of `.content`, so EVERY marketing/browse route shares it. The bespoke per-page footers + their styled-jsx CSS were deleted from all nine PublicShell-rendered surfaces that carried one — [page.tsx](frontend/src/app/page.tsx) (`.lp-footer`), [product](frontend/src/app/product/page.tsx) (`.pp-footer`), [compare](frontend/src/app/compare/page.tsx) (`.cmp-footer`), [compare/[competitor]](frontend/src/app/compare/%5Bcompetitor%5D/page.tsx) (`.vs-footer`), [integrations](frontend/src/app/integrations/page.tsx) (`.intx-footer`), [integrations/[tool]](frontend/src/app/integrations/%5Btool%5D/page.tsx) (`.intg-footer`), [marketplace/[slug]](frontend/src/app/marketplace/%5Bslug%5D/page.tsx) (`.mps-footer`), [blog](frontend/src/app/blog/BlogPageClient.tsx) (`.blog-footer`), [blog/[slug]](frontend/src/app/blog/%5Bslug%5D/BlogPostClient.tsx) (`.bpost-footer`) — plus their now-orphaned `FOOTER_LINKS`/`BRAND`/`Link` imports (incl. a pre-existing dead `BRAND` import in `compare/[competitor]`). `FOOTER_LINKS` is now consumed only by `AppFooter`. NOTE this corrects the original premise: PublicShell did NOT actually render AppFooter before this pass (only `FooterOnlyShell` did), so marketing pages showed a *single* per-page footer, not two stacked — but the leaf pages WOULD have double-stacked the moment PublicShell adopted the canonical footer, so all nine were swept together. frontend `tsc` 0, eslint clean. ORIGINAL GAP: Landing + product + compare pages render two stacked footers (a rich site-links footer + a legal strip) — fold the site-links into AppFooter via FOOTER_LINKS and drop the per-page footers for one canonical footer.

- **`/llm/v1/messages` plan daily-token cap — RESOLVED (2026-06-14, T3).** The our-models branch (no tenant Anthropic key → served from OUR pool, billing US) previously skipped the `llmUsageLog`-SUM daily-cap gate that `/v1/chat/completions` enforced. Fixed by extracting the inline gate into a shared `enforceDailyTokenCap(c, access)` helper ([llmRoutes.ts](api/src/presentation/routes/llmRoutes.ts)) and calling it on the our-models branch (BYO-key passthrough stays ungated — it bills the tenant's own key). Removed the surface divergence and collapsed a duplicate register entry. tsc 0 + tests.

- **Cache-read tokens charged at full weight in the daily-cap ledger — RESOLVED (2026-06-14, T3).** The plan daily-limit gate summed `total_tokens` at 1×, ignoring the cache-read/creation discount that `computeCostMillicents` already applied to *cost*. The shared `enforceDailyTokenCap` helper now sums a cache-discounted effective total (`SUM(total_tokens − 0.9·cache_read + 0.25·cache_creation)`) via `CACHE_READ_MULTIPLIER`/`CACHE_CREATION_MULTIPLIER` exported from [usageLedger.ts](api/src/application/llm/usageLedger.ts), so tenants get the cached-input discount in their *budget* and the `x-builderforce-daily-tokens-*` headers — not just in the log. tsc 0 + tests.

- **✅ RESOLVED 2026-06-14 (T4).** `POST /tasks/:taskId/pull-request` now honors `tasks.explicit_repo_id` + optional `{repoId,labels}` override and decrypts the repo credential into the dispatch. ORIGINAL GAP: **PR dispatch resolves the repo from task description only (no labels / explicit repoId).** [repoRoutes.ts](api/src/presentation/routes/repoRoutes.ts) `POST /tasks/:taskId/pull-request` calls `resolveRepoForTask` with description text only, because `tasks` has no labels column; the pure resolver already supports labels + `explicitRepoId`. Also the repo `credential_id` is stored but not decrypted/attached to the dispatch message. Fixing (thread an optional `repoId`/labels from the request body, and resolve+decrypt `integration_credentials` into the claw dispatch payload) unblocks: accurate multi-repo targeting + the claw actually receiving git credentials.

- **✅ RESOLVED 2026-06-14 (T4).** route now dual-auths (agentHost API key OR tenant JWT) via shared `resolveHostAuth`; claws report PR status without a user JWT. ORIGINAL GAP: **`POST /pull-requests/:id/result` is tenant-JWT auth only — claws can't call it with an API key.** [repoRoutes.ts](api/src/presentation/routes/repoRoutes.ts) uses `authMiddleware`; a claw posting PR results would need a claw-API-key branch mirroring [specRoutes.ts `verifyClawApiKey`](api/src/presentation/routes/specRoutes.ts). Fixing unblocks: claws reporting PR number/url/status back without a user JWT.

- **✅ RESOLVED 2026-06-14 (T4).** dispatch enforces `runtime_support` (a cloud-only agent is never sent to a pinned host) and defaults to `preferred_runtime`. ORIGINAL GAP: **`runtime_support` / `preferred_runtime` are declared metadata but not enforced at execution dispatch.** An agent can say it supports only `claw`, yet nothing in the runtime/swimlane dispatch path ([runtimeRoutes.ts](api/src/presentation/routes/runtimeRoutes.ts), [SwimlaneCoordinator](api/src/application/swimlane/SwimlaneCoordinator.ts)) reads these fields to route to the right runtime or reject an unsupported one. Fixing (validate the chosen runtime against `runtime_support` and default to `preferred_runtime`) unblocks: honoring an agent's declared best/only experience.

- **✅ RESOLVED 2026-06-14 (T5).** `saveAuthProfileStore`+`ensureAuthStoreFile` made `async` with `await` propagated through all ~10 call sites + 3 test files — durable, ordered credential writes; closes the last json-file sync/async seam. ORIGINAL GAP: **The auth-profile WRITE path still fires the async `saveJsonFile` without `await` (pre-existing — `saveJsonFile` has always been async, so NOT part of the `loadJsonFile` sync→async fix).** [`saveAuthProfileStore`](agent-runtime/src/agents/auth-profiles/store.ts#L336) and [`ensureAuthStoreFile`](agent-runtime/src/agents/auth-profiles/paths.ts#L24) are declared SYNC (`: void`) yet call the async `saveJsonFile`, making every credential/auth-store write a fire-and-forget Promise: a write failure becomes an unhandled rejection (process-level crash risk under `unhandledRejection`), and a caller that reads the store back immediately after can race the not-yet-flushed write. Left sync this pass to avoid a wide cascade — making them async forces `await` through ~10 production call sites (oauth.ts, usage.ts, profiles.ts, store.ts) plus ~6 test files, and re-exports via `auth-profiles.ts`. Fixing (make both functions `async`, `await saveJsonFile`, and propagate `await` to every caller per the operator "make it all async" directive) unblocks: durable, ordered credential writes with no unhandled-rejection surface — closing the last `json-file` sync/async seam.

- **✅ RESOLVED 2026-06-14 (T5).** the 5 remaining lobster-mascot emoji in `agent-runtime` docs/examples reworded; favicon.svg + CONTRIBUTING already swept — no crab anywhere user-facing. ORIGINAL GAP: **The `agent-runtime` sub-app still carries lobster mascot artwork/copy.** The mascot retirement this pass covered the Builderforce.ai frontend; not yet swept: [agent-runtime/ui/public/favicon.svg](agent-runtime/ui/public/favicon.svg) (a hand-drawn lobster with a `lobster-gradient` + "Left/Right Claw" paths) and the "Welcome to the lobster tank! 🦞" line in [agent-runtime/docs/CONTRIBUTING.md](agent-runtime/docs/CONTRIBUTING.md). These are a separate deployable's brand assets and need an actual SVG/logo redraw, so deferred. NOTE: the `lobster` entries in [agent-runtime/extensions/lobster](agent-runtime/extensions/lobster) + CHANGELOG/labeler are the real external **Lobster workflow tool**, NOT the mascot — leave them. Fixing (redraw favicon.svg as the agentHost logo; reword the CONTRIBUTING line) unblocks: consistent brand with no crab anywhere user-facing.

- **✅ RESOLVED (T6, 2026-06-14) — stale; the `/api/studio/weights/*` route now exists.** [studioWeightRoutes.ts](Builderforce.ai/api/src/presentation/routes/studioWeightRoutes.ts) streams from R2 key `studio-weights/<model>/<file>` with `Cache-Control: public, immutable, max-age=31536000` and is mounted at `/api/studio`. Superseded by the upload-tooling entry directly below (also now resolved). - **✅ RESOLVED (T6, 2026-06-14) — upload tooling shipped; remaining work is the one-time operator run.** [studio/scripts/upload-studio-weights.mjs](Builderforce.ai/studio/scripts/upload-studio-weights.mjs) wraps `wrangler r2 object put` for the canonical model files (manifest mirrors `MODEL_REGISTRY` — lcm-tiny-sd / lcm-dreamshaper-v7 / sd-turbo, each with text-encoder/UNet(+data)/VAE(+data)); it downloads from HF or `--from <dir>`, supports `--model`/`--remote`/`--dry-run`, and the operator workflow is documented in [studio/README.md](Builderforce.ai/studio/README.md). Dry-run smoke-tested. **Operator action remaining (deploy-gated, needs authed `wrangler`):** actually run it against the prod `builderforce-uploads` bucket so the proxy serves first-party weights; until then the engine stays on the HF fallback (functional, just slower cold loads). ORIGINAL GAP: route mounted but no weights uploaded and no upload script existed.

- **✅ RESOLVED (T6, 2026-06-14) — the noise-level-scaled bias formula shipped; latent-residual coherence now composes with img2img.** The binary skip-gate `shouldApplyLatentResidualBias` was replaced by [`latentResidualBiasScale`](Builderforce.ai/studio/src/engine/mamba-coherence.ts), which returns the multiplier `applyToLatent` (now takes a `noiseScale` param) applies to its per-channel offset: `1` on the fresh-noise path, `sqrt(1-ᾱ_t)` under img2img — so the bias perturbs only the noise component and leaves the carried-forward signal intact. The schedule's noise fraction comes from the new `DiffusionEngine.noiseScaleForTimestep` (single source of truth, also now backing `addNoiseToLatent`); `video-engine.ts` `produceClip` wires it. Unit-tested in [mamba-coherence.test.ts](Builderforce.ai/studio/src/engine/mamba-coherence.test.ts) (bias-scale gate + proportional-offset + no-op). ORIGINAL GAP follows. [studio/src/engine/mamba-coherence.ts `shouldApplyLatentResidualBias`](studio/src/engine/mamba-coherence.ts) gates the bias and returns `false` whenever `useImg2Img` is on (the bug it fixes: `applyToLatent` adds a per-channel broadcast constant designed for unit-variance noise, which catastrophically disfigures partially-denoised img2img latents and compounds frame-to-frame). The conservative fix means a user picking `latent-residual` + `imgToImgStrength > 0` gets the same temporal coherence behaviour as `prompt-bias` + img2img (i.e. zero latent-side Mamba bias). A proper fix would scale the bias by the schedule noise level — at timestep `t` the latent is `sqrt(α)·clean + sqrt(1-α)·noise`, so scaling the broadcast bias by `sqrt(1-α)` would perturb only the noise portion and leave the signal intact, letting both mechanisms compose. Fixing (one parameter on `applyToLatent`, one call site, one test) unblocks: stacking trained-state coherence on top of img2img for the longer-clip "scene-aware walking" use case.

- **✅ RESOLVED (T6, 2026-06-14) — the silent contradiction is gone.** The scattered `showAdvanced ? model : tier.primary` ternaries were unified into one source of truth, [`resolveEffectiveChain`](Builderforce.ai/studio-embedded/src/components/QualityTierPicker.tsx) (used by the engine factory, saved-version params, the debug snapshot, and the badge). A self-contained [`EffectiveChainBadge`](Builderforce.ai/studio-embedded/src/components/QualityTierPicker.tsx) renders the authoritative effective chain and flags when Advanced has overridden the tier; the Quality picker is now `disabled` while an Advanced override is active, so both surfaces can no longer claim to be in effect at once. ORIGINAL GAP follows. When the user opens Advanced and picks a specific model, the engine uses *that* model and skips the refinement pass even if Quality is set to "Refined" ([StudioPanel.tsx](studio-embedded/src/components/StudioPanel.tsx) — the `showAdvanced ? model : tier.primary` ternary). The current Quality picker doesn't visually indicate it was overridden, so a user with Advanced open + Refined selected sees both controls active and the tier description (lying about "two-pass chain") while only single-pass runs. Fixing (either grey out the Quality picker when Advanced model is set, or grey out the Advanced model picker when Quality !== "fast/balanced/refined", with a single resolved-state badge showing the effective model chain) unblocks: no silent contradiction between the two control surfaces.

- **✅ RESOLVED (T6, 2026-06-14) — the snapshot now reports the effective chain.** [DebugCopyButton](Builderforce.ai/studio-embedded/src/components/DebugCopyButton.tsx) takes `quality`, the RESOLVED `model`/`refinementModel` (from [`resolveEffectiveChain`](Builderforce.ai/studio-embedded/src/components/QualityTierPicker.tsx)), `interpolationFactor`, and `anchorRefreshInterval`, and renders them in both the markdown ("Quality tier", "Model chain: a → b (two-pass)", "Keyframe interpolation") and JSON snapshots. A two-pass "Refined" capture now states the full chain instead of a stale `lcm-tiny-sd`. ORIGINAL GAP follows. [DebugCopyButton](studio-embedded/src/components/DebugCopyButton.tsx) receives `model={model}` (the Advanced picker state, default `lcm-tiny-sd`) from [StudioPanel](studio-embedded/src/components/StudioPanel.tsx), not the resolved `(tier.primary, tier.refinement)` pair, nor `quality`, nor `interpolationFactor`. A two-pass "Refined" capture therefore reads `Model: lcm-tiny-sd` with no sign a refinement model ran — which made the two-pass distortion above harder to triage. Fixing (pass `quality`, the resolved `model`/`refinementModel`, and `interpolationFactor` through to the snapshot and render them under Configuration) unblocks: a debug paste that unambiguously states the model chain + temporal density that produced the frames.

- **✅ RESOLVED 2026-06-14 (T7).** `emitWebhookEvent` persists the signed body; non-2xx/network failures retry via capped backoff (5→10→20→40→80m, max 6 then dead-letter) in a `scheduled()` sweep re-signing under the original delivery-id nonce (idempotent). Migration 0160. ORIGINAL GAP: **Failed webhook deliveries are best-effort with no retry/backoff.** [emitWebhookEvent](api/src/application/seams/webhookService.ts) attempts each delivery once and records `failed`/`pending` rows in `webhook_deliveries`, but nothing redelivers them. A transient receiver outage drops the event permanently. Fixing (a `scheduled()` cron — mirroring the vendor-health cron in [index.ts](api/src/index.ts) — that re-signs and retries `failed`/`pending` deliveries with capped exponential backoff) unblocks: at-least-once delivery semantics.

- **✅ RESOLVED 2026-06-14 (T8).** new `awaiting_workflow` lifecycle + `ticket_runs.awaiting_workflow_id` (migration 0171) parks the ticket; a poll sweep (`resumeParkedWorkflows`) advances on settle / routes to `needs_attention` on fail/missing-definition. ORIGINAL GAP: **`run_workflow` lane action fires the workflow but does not block ticket advancement on its completion.** When a lane's action is `run_workflow`, [SwimlaneCoordinator.onStageComplete](api/src/application/swimlane/SwimlaneCoordinator.ts) calls [DrizzleStageWorkflowRunner](api/src/application/swimlane/stageWorkflowRunner.ts) → [instantiateWorkflowRun](api/src/application/workflow/instantiateRun.ts) as a fire-and-forget side-effect, then advances the ticket immediately — it does not wait for the spawned workflow to reach `completed`/`failed` before moving the ticket on (nor surface that workflow's failure back onto the ticket). A definition deleted since assignment is also silently skipped. Fixing (a back-edge that parks the ticket until the spawned workflow settles and maps its status onto the ticket lifecycle, plus surfacing a missing-definition error instead of a silent no-op) unblocks: lane actions that genuinely gate on a downstream workflow's outcome.

- **✅ RESOLVED 2026-06-14 (T8).** `runBoardSyncSweep` (wired into `scheduled()`) honors each active connection’s `poll_interval_sec` and runs `syncConnection`+`drainOutbox` with per-connection failure isolation. ORIGINAL GAP: **No scheduled poller drives external board sync; outbox writeback is not triggered.** [SyncEngine.syncConnection](api/src/application/boardsync/SyncEngine.ts) + `drainOutbox` are implemented and unit-tested but only run via `POST /api/board-connections/:id/sync`. No `scheduled()` cron/queue iterates active `board_connections` to poll on their `poll_interval_sec`, and nothing periodically drains `board_sync_outbox`. Fixing (a Cloudflare `scheduled()` handler in [index.ts](api/src/index.ts) — mirroring `runVendorHealthCron` — that calls `syncConnection` + `drainOutbox` per active connection using `drizzleStore` + `createBoardProvider`) unblocks: hands-off inbound polling + reliable reverse-sync.

- **✅ RESOLVED 2026-06-14 (T8).** closed by the same `runBoardSyncSweep` scheduled poller — configured poll intervals are now honored automatically. ORIGINAL GAP: **Recurring external-board sync still has no scheduled poller — only the on-create + "Sync now" manual triggers fire.** The new `BoardConnectionsManager` calls `POST /api/board-connections/:id/sync` once on create and on demand, but nothing drains `board_sync_outbox` / re-polls on `poll_interval_sec` (already logged under the Cloud Agent Boards section — "No scheduled poller drives external board sync"). The new UI makes the gap user-visible: a user sets a poll interval that is never honored automatically. Fixing (the `scheduled()` handler from that entry) unblocks: hands-off inbound sync matching the configured interval.

- **✅ RESOLVED 2026-06-14 (T8).** JSONB `fields` column (migration 0170); `upsertLink` writes it and `getLink` reads it back — unblocks field-level three-way merge. ORIGINAL GAP: **`external_ticket_links` does not persist the normalized field bag.** [drizzleStore.ts](api/src/application/boardsync/drizzleStore.ts) `getLink` returns `fields:null`; reconciliation still works (it keys on `content_hash`/`external_version`), but field-level three-way merge is impossible. Fixing (add a JSON `fields` column to `external_ticket_links` or derive fields from the linked task) unblocks: field-level conflict merge instead of whole-record LWW.

- **✅ RESOLVED 2026-06-14 (T9).** 4 recent prefix collisions renumbered into T9’s band (0109→0190, 0114→0191, 0120→0192, 0121→0193); 8 historical ones grandfathered in `.migration-collisions-allowlist.txt`; `check-migrations.mjs` fails CI on any new duplicate prefix. ORIGINAL GAP: **Duplicate migration numbers: `0109` (`0109_execution_cloud_agent_ref.sql` + `0109_execution_messages.sql`) AND `0111` (`0111_boards_project_unique.sql` + `0111_agent_feedback_and_perf.sql`).** The migrations dir keys ordering off the numeric prefix, so a runner that sorts by prefix-then-name applies each pair in filename order (`agent_feedback…` before `boards…` for 0111; `cloud_agent_ref` before `messages` for 0109) but a runner that dedupes/keys on the bare prefix token could skip one. Both `0111` files are independent CREATE-only DDL with no ordering dependency between them, so the practical risk is the same latent skip, not a broken sequence. The `0111_agent_feedback_and_perf.sql` number was assigned by task spec (gap [1247]) before noticing `0111_boards_project_unique.sql` already held it. Fixing (renumber one file of each colliding pair to the next free slot and update any applied-migrations ledger that already recorded the old name) unblocks: an unambiguous, gap-free migration sequence.

- **✅ RESOLVED 2026-06-14 (T9).** `migrate.mjs` now applies each file + its ledger INSERT in one `sql.transaction([...])` so a mid-file failure rolls the whole file back — no half-applied schema. ORIGINAL GAP: **The migration runner is not transactional per file — a mid-file failure leaves a partial apply.** [scripts/migrate.mjs](api/scripts/migrate.mjs) executes statements one-by-one and only records the migration in `_migrations` after all succeed; a failure midway (e.g. 0056's first attempt hit a missing table after 15 tables were already altered) leaves the DB half-migrated with the file un-recorded. 0056 was made idempotent + guarded so re-running converges, but not every migration is written that way. Fixing (wrap each migration file's statements in a single `BEGIN/COMMIT` so a failure rolls the whole file back) unblocks: no half-applied schema states, safe to author non-idempotent migrations.

- **✅ RESOLVED 2026-06-14 (T9).** `ci.yml` now builds brain-embedded in the link-dep prerequisites step alongside sdk/studio/studio-embedded. ORIGINAL GAP: **`brain-embedded` is a `link:` dep but is NOT built in CI's "link: dep prerequisites" step like its siblings (`sdk`/`studio`/`studio-embedded`).** [ci.yml](.github/workflows/ci.yml) only runs `npm install` (→ `prepare` build) for those three before `pnpm install`. The Vitest `react` resolution failure was fixed in this pass via [vitest.config.ts](frontend/vitest.config.ts) `resolve.dedupe: ['react','react-dom','react/jsx-runtime']` (forces the frontend's single React copy instead of reaching into `brain-embedded/node_modules`, which the frontend-only CI job never installs). This works today **only because `brain-embedded/dist` is committed to git** (unlike `sdk/dist`/`studio/dist`/`worker/dist`, which are gitignored). If brain-embedded's `dist` is ever added to `.gitignore` to match the sibling convention, CI will break again because no build step regenerates it. Fixing (add `(cd brain-embedded && npm install --no-audit --no-fund)` to the prerequisite step so the package is built+installed consistently with its siblings, then `dist` can be safely gitignored) unblocks: a uniform link-dep build story with no committed build artifacts.

- **✅ RESOLVED 2026-06-14 (T9).** `.github/isolation-tracks.json` manifest + `check-track-scope.mjs` (CI job `track-scope.yml` + pre-commit hook) reject out-of-scope files and out-of-band migrations per `track/<id>` branch — isolation is now enforced, not honor-system. ORIGINAL GAP: **Isolation-track boundaries are convention-only — no CI/pre-commit guard enforces a branch’s declared track.** The README’s 🧵 Isolation Tracks table assigns each agent a set of _Owns_ paths + a reserved migration band, but nothing rejects a commit/branch that edits files outside its track or grabs a migration number from another band. A sloppy or confused agent can silently cross tracks, reintroducing the merge/parallel-safety problem the tracks exist to prevent. Fixing (a pre-commit hook + CI job that maps a `track/<id>` branch name → the track’s path globs and migration band, failing on any out-of-scope file or out-of-band migration) unblocks: **enforceable** parallel-agent isolation instead of honor-system isolation. Prereq + DRY: extract the table into a machine-readable manifest (e.g. `.github/isolation-tracks.json`) that BOTH the guard and the README render from, so the two never drift.

### 💰 Open — Direct revenue / monetization (15)

_Billing, plan tiers (Free/Pro), marketplace purchase/payout, pricing & entitlement gates, metering, cost attribution._

- **Per-user sub-ledger from `metadata.userId` is not implemented.** The gateway debits the tenant's daily plan budget; if the SDK's `metadata.userId` is set, the gateway could maintain a per-user sub-ledger and enforce per-user caps. Tenant apps continue to enforce per-user budgets locally. Needs a product decision (per-user cap UX in the portal) plus a `tenant_user_token_caps` table and a query in the chat route. Fixing unblocks deletion of tenant-side `tokenLedger.charge` plumbing.

- **Pending invitations don't reserve a plan seat.** The seat-limit guard (`buildPlanLimitsGuard.checkSeatLimit`) counts only active `tenant_members`, so a manager can queue many pending invites under the cap and have them *all* auto-accept on signup, pushing the workspace past its seat limit (the accept path in `acceptPendingInvitations` swallows the per-tenant add error and leaves the row pending, but never tells anyone). Fixing (count `status='pending'` invitations toward the seat tally at invite time, or re-check + surface the limit at accept time) unblocks: seat limits that can't be bypassed via the invite queue.

- **Cost attribution (ticket → project → workspace → account) covers only the cloud-agent execution loop — web/SDK and on-prem host spend isn't attributed.** Cost now stamps the full rollup chain on `llm_usage_log`: `task_id` (ticket, the finest grain — migration 0104), `project_id` (0103), and `tenant_id` (account). **Workspace (segment) is intentionally NOT a column here** — 0056 keeps `llm_usage_log` tenant-level (platform/infra ledger; its segment trigger RAISEs for segmented tenants), so workspace-level cost is derived by joining `project → segment` (projects.segment_id), not denormalized. Stamped from the run's task in [recordCloudUsage](api/src/presentation/routes/runtimeRoutes.ts); surfaced as ticket spend on the execution panel (`GET /tasks/:id/cost`) and the "By Project" card ([LlmUsageContent.tsx](frontend/src/components/LlmUsageContent.tsx)) rolling up to the account total. STILL UNATTRIBUTED (task_id/project_id null → account-level only): (a) gateway chat/image calls via `logUsage` ([llmRoutes.ts](api/src/presentation/routes/llmRoutes.ts)) — no ticket/project context on a raw LLM call; (b) self-hosted **on-prem host** runs, which meter via the gateway path not `recordCloudUsage`, so a host executing a ticket records cost with no task/project; (c) the future CloudRunnerDO must pass `taskId`+`projectId` to `recordCloudUsage` or its spend regresses to unattributed. Also missing: a **workspace (segment) rollup** surface (the join exists; no endpoint/card yet) and a **project-page** spend widget (only the execution panel + LLM-usage dashboard show it). Fixing (thread a ticket/project hint through the gateway `_builderforce` metadata for agent-attributed calls; resolve execution→task→project on the host-run usage write; add segment + project-page rollups) unblocks: complete spend at every level of the hierarchy. (Backfill for past cloud rows handled in 0103/0104 via execution→task→project.)

- **hired.video's tailor worker runs its own client-side 6-model cascade against the gateway, using a deprecated model id.** The 2026-06-07 trace (`handleTailor`, `worker.js`) shows hired.video looping its *own* model list — `qwen3-next:free`, `qwen3-coder:free`, `gemma-4-31b:free`, `hermes-3-405b:free`, `cerebras/llama3.1-8b`, and `anthropic/claude-3-haiku` (retired on the first-party Anthropic API) — one builderforce call each, duplicating the gateway's failover and pinning models that no longer exist. The tailor's plan (free vs pro) is also unconfirmed; with the backstop added this pass, builderforce now *funds* the paid fallback for free-plan calls (~$0.0001/call by design). The hired.video repo is not in this workspace. Fixing (in hired.video: drop the client-side cascade — send one request with no `model` hint and let the gateway route; remove the `claude-3-haiku` pin) and confirming the intended billing posture for tailor unblocks: no wasted duplicate attempts, no doomed deprecated-model pins, and clarity on who pays for the free-tier backstop.

- **Gateway + agent-runtime prompt-cache TTL is fixed at 5-minute ephemeral — no 1-hour opt-in.** This pass wired Anthropic prompt-cache breakpoints into the gateway request path ([promptCaching.ts](api/src/application/llm/promptCaching.ts) → injected in [openrouter.ts `buildBody`](api/src/application/llm/vendors/openrouter.ts)) and into agent-runtime's OpenRouter/Anthropic system prompt ([extra-params.ts `addAnthropicSystemCacheControl`](agent-runtime/src/agents/pi-embedded-runner/extra-params.ts)), completing the caching+metering pair the gateway already read via [`pickUsage`](api/src/application/llm/vendors/types.ts) (`cache_read_tokens`/`cache_creation_tokens`). Both always emit `cache_control: { type: 'ephemeral' }` (5-min TTL). For bursty tenants with a large stable prefix and gaps >5 min between calls, a 1-hour TTL (`{ type: 'ephemeral', ttl: '1h' }`, ~2x write cost) would keep the prefix warm across idle gaps — pi-ai already supports this for *direct* Anthropic via `cacheRetention: 'long'`, but the gateway/OpenRouter path doesn't expose it. Fixing (a per-request `_builderforce: { cacheTtl: '1h' }` hint / per-`useCase` profile that flips the marker, in both surfaces) unblocks: cache hits across multi-minute idle gaps for high-prefix tenants. **UPDATE 2026-06-14 (T3) — gateway side shipped.** `_builderforce.cacheTtl:'1h'` is now honoured end-to-end on the gateway: [promptCaching.ts](api/src/application/llm/promptCaching.ts) `applyPromptCaching(messages, model, ttl)` emits `{ type:'ephemeral', ttl:'1h' }` on every breakpoint when requested; the hint is read by `resolveCacheTtl` in [LlmProxyService.ts](api/src/application/llm/LlmProxyService.ts), threaded through `dispatch` → `VendorCallParams.cacheTtl` → [openrouter.ts `buildBody`](api/src/application/llm/vendors/openrouter.ts) (the only vendor that needs the marker). The `_builderforce` envelope is still stripped before vendor dispatch, so the hint never reaches the upstream as a body field. tsc 0 + new TTL unit tests. **Still open:** the agent-runtime surface (T5) — wiring `cacheTtl:'1h'` / `cacheRetention:'long'` through pi-ai's direct-Anthropic path — and an optional per-`useCase` profile that auto-selects 1h.

- **No per-tenant cap on the always-on premium fallback chain.** [LlmProxyService.PREMIUM_FALLBACK_MODELS](api/src/application/llm/LlmProxyService.ts) is appended to every non-strict candidate chain (Free plan included) — when the (now 2-attempt-capped) free section is exhausted, the proxy falls through to `googleai/gemini-2.5-flash` → `googleai/gemini-2.5-flash-lite` → OpenRouter `google/gemini-2.5-flash-lite` so callers never see a cascade-exhausted 429. The residual risk: a Free-plan tenant in a tight retry loop can drive arbitrary spend against the Builderforce `GOOGLE_API_KEY` / `OPENROUTER_API_KEY` because there's no per-tenant overflow cap or daily budget on the premium-fallback path, and the new 2-free-cap means the cascade reaches paid endpoints *faster* than the previous design. Fixing (track premium-fallback hits in `llm_usage_log` against a per-tenant `paid_overflow_daily_cap`, default ~$0.50/day, and surface the cap in the superadmin tenants page) unblocks: hard ceiling on overflow cost while preserving the "zero `LLM_UNAVAILABLE` escapes" guarantee. **UPDATE 2026-06-14 (T3) — backend shipped (migration 0130, not yet applied to any live DB).** [Migration 0130](api/migrations/0130_paid_overflow_cap.sql) adds `tenants.paid_overflow_daily_cap` (millicents; NULL → plan default = $0.50/day free, unlimited pro/teams; -1 = unlimited) and `llm_usage_log.paid_overflow` (+ partial index). The proxy now classifies a funded-overflow resolution via `isPaidOverflowModel` (premium-fallback ∪ backstop models) and stamps `ProxyResult.paidOverflow`, which both gateway surfaces write to the usage row. A new `disablePaidOverflow` option on `LlmProxyService`/`llmProxyForPlan` drops the premium-fallback chain AND skips the backstop; the route helper `isPaidOverflowExhausted` ([llmRoutes.ts](api/src/presentation/routes/llmRoutes.ts)) sums today's overflow `cost_usd_millicents` and flips it once the cap is hit — so the tenant's PRIMARY pool keeps serving while the funded path is closed (preserving the guarantee for tenants under cap). `resolvePaidOverflowCapMillicents` ([usageLedger.ts](api/src/application/llm/usageLedger.ts)) is the single cap-resolution source. tsc 0 + new overflow tests. **Still open:** (1) apply migration 0130 to the live DB; (2) surface/edit the cap in the superadmin tenants page (frontend — T2/T7); (3) image-gen overflow (FluxAPI premium fallback) is not yet classified (separate from the chat path).

- **Pro plan's free-tier section is now also capped at 2 attempts.** [LlmProxyService.FREE_ATTEMPT_BUDGET](api/src/application/llm/LlmProxyService.ts) (= 2) is applied universally in `buildCandidateChain`, so Pro tenants' cascade is `[2 free, ...PRO_PAID_MODEL_POOL, ...PREMIUM_FALLBACK_MODELS]` instead of the previous "walk all free + all paid + cross-vendor" chain. Net effect is positive (Pro tenants reach their paid premium models faster) but the design is uniform with Free plan — there is no Pro-specific carve-out that, say, lets Pro tenants try 5 free models before paying. If Pro customers report missing free-tier breadth, the fix is to take `FREE_ATTEMPT_BUDGET` from a plan-aware lookup instead of a single constant. Fixing unblocks: plan-tier-differentiated cascade depth.

- **Image gen shares the chat per-tenant daily token budget at a flat 1000-tok/image rate.** [llmRoutes.ts POST /v1/images/generations](api/src/presentation/routes/llmRoutes.ts) charges `images_returned * 1000` against `llm_usage_log.total_tokens`, so heavy image usage can exhaust the chat-text budget and vice versa. Two-budget separation (chat tokens vs image credits) would let tenants buy/cap each independently. Fixing (add `image_credits_daily_limit` column to `tenants`, log image rows with a new `llm_product` value and check them against the new cap instead of the token cap) unblocks: independent image-only quotas and pricing.

- **Gateway keys, usage metering, and rate limiting are tenant-only — no segment dimension.** `tenantApiKeys` and claw keys map to a tenant; `llm_usage_log` and `TenantRateLimiterDO` meter/limit per tenant. An integrator calling the gateway/SDK can't say which end-client a call is for. Fixing (add `segment_id` to keys + usage log + a segment header on `/v1/*`, namespace the rate-limiter DO by `tenant:segment`) unblocks: per-segment metering, quotas, and chargeback for integrators reselling the platform.

- **Spec assumes a per-Segment credit ledger + `viewer` projection + `AI_USE_CASES`/`callAiAndCharge` facade that does not exist in BuilderForce.** Doc 01 §8 / doc 05 §6 lean on BurnRateOS's AI facade; the BuilderForce gateway meters per *tenant* via `llm_usage_log` + plan token limits with no `AI_USE_CASES` registry, no `viewer`, no segment dimension (grep: no `AI_USE_CASES`/`callAiAndCharge`). Extends the per-segment-metering gap above. Fixing (port the use-case registry + per-segment credit ledger + viewer-projection into BuilderForce, or map them onto the existing gateway primitives with a `segment_id` added to usage) unblocks: the `dev.*` + `pm.*`/`agile.*` use cases billing per end-client as the spec requires.

- **Project modality entitlement gate is partial — the `comingSoon` flag gates the LLM modality, but the Pro+ paid gate for Video can't be enforced client-side because the frontend `Tenant` type carries no plan/tier field.** [frontend/src/components/IDENew.tsx](frontend/src/components/IDENew.tsx) disables `comingSoon` modalities in the switcher (config-driven from [frontend/src/lib/modality.ts](frontend/src/lib/modality.ts)), so the mechanism exists. But [frontend/src/lib/types.ts](frontend/src/lib/types.ts) `Tenant` exposes only `{ id, name, slug, role }` — no plan — so the agreed Pro+ gate on the heavy Video modality has no data source to read. Fixing (surface the tenant plan/tier on the `Tenant` object via the auth/tenant token claim or a `/api/tenants/:id` fetch, add a `requiresPaidPlan` flag to the Video `ModalityDef`, and gate the switcher on it) unblocks: revenue protection on the 6GB-VRAM modality.

- **Free tier is capped to diagnostic + recommendation by design; Pro multi-repo/large-repo evidence trimming is still coarse.** `planConfig` in [AnalysisRunnerDO.ts](api/src/infrastructure/relay/AnalysisRunnerDO.ts) gives Free 2 artifacts / ~9k tokens and Pro all 6 / ~120k, with `selectEvidence` sized per-repo. Very large or many-repo Pro projects can still overflow a single artifact's prompt budget (no cross-repo prioritization, no per-artifact evidence subsetting). Fixing (rank repos by relevance, subset evidence per artifact kind, summarize-then-analyze for huge trees) unblocks: reliable full analysis on monorepos / large estates.

- **Publishing an agent sets `published`+price but agents are NOT yet a marketplace artifact type, so there is no purchase/payout path.** The marketplace artifact enum is `skill | persona | content` ([schema.ts](api/src/infrastructure/database/schema.ts)); `marketplace_purchases` + the Stripe-intent purchase route ([marketplaceRoutes.ts](api/src/presentation/routes/marketplaceRoutes.ts)) don't know about agents. So a published agent's price is stored + displayed but cannot actually be transacted, and "revenue" isn't collected/paid out. Fixing (add `'agent'` to `artifactTypeEnum`, surface published agents in the marketplace listing/detail, and wire the purchase + payout path for agents) unblocks: real agent monetization end-to-end.

- **"Hire" is still only a counter — it does not provision/deploy the agent.** [POST /api/ide/agents/:id/hire](api/src/presentation/routes/ideRoutes.ts) increments `hire_count`; there's no instantiation of the hired agent into the hirer's workspace (no claw bind / cloud-runtime registration). Fixing (on hire, create a tenant-scoped agent instance or bind to a runtime per the agent's `runtime_support`) unblocks: hiring that actually puts an agent to work.

- **The new IDE dashboard exposes a "New Video project" create path with no Pro+ entitlement gate.** [/ide/dashboard](frontend/src/app/ide/dashboard/page.tsx) renders a project-type chooser (Designer / Video / LLM) driven by [modality.ts](frontend/src/lib/modality.ts) and calls `createProject({ modality })` directly — so a free-plan tenant can now create a `video` project and open the heavy (6 GB-VRAM) Video modality from the launcher, not just via the in-IDE switcher. This is the same root gap already logged above ("Project modality entitlement gate is partial … the frontend `Tenant` type carries no plan/tier field"): the chooser only honors `comingSoon`, and Video isn't `comingSoon`. Fixing (surface tenant plan/tier on the `Tenant` object, add a `requiresPaidPlan` flag to the Video `ModalityDef`, and gate both the dashboard chooser card AND the IDE switcher on it — one shared check) unblocks: revenue protection on the Video modality across every create surface. Bundle with the existing partial-gate entry — same fix closes both.

### 🚀 Open — Growth / acquisition & retention (10)

_SEO, marketing surfaces, onboarding / connect flow, public & embed presence, funnel capture, notifications._

- **`builderforce.ai/docs/*` proxy — needs deploy + one post-deploy verification.** Live symptom was `404` on *every* `/docs/*` path. **Corrected root cause** (the earlier "stale artifact built before `base:/docs`" theory was wrong — disproven by `https://builderforce-docs.pages.dev/agents-overview` serving real content while `.../docs/agents-overview` 404s): Astro `base: '/docs'` only prefixes the emitted *links/assets*, it does **not** nest the build *output* — content is written to `dist/` root and served at the pages.dev **root** (`pages.dev/agents`, `pages.dev/_astro/*`). The apex proxy in [frontend/next.config.js](frontend/next.config.js) was forwarding `/docs/* → pages.dev/docs/*` (a path that doesn't exist), so all paths 404'd. **Fixed this pass** by making the proxy **strip** the `/docs` prefix (`/docs/:path* → pages.dev/:path*`), and by relocating the rebrand redirect stubs to `dist` root (dropped `/docs` from the `redirects` *source* keys in [docs-site/astro.config.mjs](docs-site/astro.config.mjs), kept it in destinations). Both ship on the next push to `main` (frontend `build-and-deploy` + `deploy-docs`); the content fix only needs the frontend redeploy. **Remaining follow-up:** verify post-deploy that `@cloudflare/next-on-pages` actually *proxies* the external rewrite via `fetch` rather than 301-redirecting to `builderforce-docs.pages.dev` — some versions mishandle absolute-URL `dest`. If the URL bar changes / goes cross-origin, fall back to a Cloudflare Workers Route `builderforce.ai/docs/*` → tiny proxy worker, or bind the docs project to `docs.builderforce.ai`. Fixing unblocks: every `/docs/*` link across the marketing site resolving same-origin.

- **Marketing / public-shell pages still center on `.page-inner`; not migrated to the new `PageContainer`.** This pass introduced [PageContainer](frontend/src/components/PageContainer.tsx) (`full` / `readable` / `narrow` width tiers, all left-aligned to kill the sidebar-gutter gap) and migrated every authenticated AppShell route plus `/prompts`, `/admin/llm-traces`, and `.admin-page` onto it. Deliberately left on their existing centered layout: `/marketplace` + `/models` (shared `.page-inner` = `max-width:1100px; margin:0 auto` in [globals.css](frontend/src/app/globals.css)) and the pure-marketing routes (`/pricing`, `/blog`, `/product`, `/`), because their hero-style centered design is intentional. They render in the same `PublicShell` `Sidebar`+`.content`, so when signed in they show the same left gutter the user flagged. Fixing (decide per-page whether marketing centering should yield to left-aligned `PageContainer`, then migrate `.page-inner` consumers and retire the class) unblocks: one consistent page-width primitive across the whole app, no parallel `.page-inner` / `PageContainer` width systems.

- **Marketplace / prompt detail views are client-side overlays with no per-entity route — individual agents, skills, personas, and prompts are unindexable and have no rich link previews.** Both [marketplace/page.tsx](frontend/src/app/marketplace/page.tsx) and [prompts/page.tsx](frontend/src/app/prompts/page.tsx) open detail in an in-page modal/drawer, so there is no `/marketplace/{slug}` or `/prompts/{slug}` URL. The listing pages now have per-page metadata + a dynamic OG image (added this pass via [seo.ts](frontend/src/lib/seo.ts) + [og.tsx](frontend/src/lib/og.tsx)), but an individual published agent/skill/prompt has no crawlable page, no per-entity `<title>`/description/JSON-LD, and no per-entity OG card. Fixing (add server `…/[slug]/page.tsx` routes with `generateMetadata` driven by a shared `buildEntitySeo(kind, record)` adapter + a per-entity `opengraph-image.tsx`, and emit them into [sitemap.ts](frontend/src/app/sitemap.ts) from the live API — cached read-through, verified/public-only, thin-entity gated) unblocks: indexable long-tail marketplace/prompt pages and correct Slack/LinkedIn/X previews when a specific agent or prompt is shared. This is the SPA-style "UGC detail" surface the marketing-presence review flagged. **UPDATE 2026-06-14 — skills detail surface shipped (the registry’s public face).** New SSR `/marketplace/[slug]` route (+ dynamic `opengraph-image`) over a cached, increment-free public read (`GET /marketplace/skills/:slug?seo=1` via `getOrSetCached`, invalidated on PUT) with `generateMetadata` + a `marketplaceSkillSchema` JSON-LD graph, emitted into [sitemap.ts](frontend/src/app/sitemap.ts) from the live published-skills list (best-effort). api + frontend `tsc` 0. **Still open:** per-entity public routes for prompts, personas, and published *agents* need their own public read endpoints + slug surfaces.

- **`/skills/[slug]` and `/personas/[slug]` carry edge-runtime + OG-image scaffolding yet are crawler-blocked and absent from the sitemap.** Both routes ([skills/[slug]/page.tsx](frontend/src/app/skills/%5Bslug%5D/page.tsx), [personas/[slug]/page.tsx](frontend/src/app/personas/%5Bslug%5D/page.tsx)) run on the edge and look intended for public sharing, but `/skills` and `/personas` are `Disallow`-ed in [robots.txt](frontend/public/robots.txt) (they double as authenticated app surfaces) and neither appears in [sitemap.ts](frontend/src/app/sitemap.ts). So if these detail pages are meant to be the public, shareable face of a published skill/persona, they are currently invisible to search + AI crawlers; if they are purely in-app, the per-route edge runtime is dead ceremony. Fixing (decide public-vs-app: either split a public `/workforce/skills/{slug}` surface with metadata + sitemap + a robots `Allow`, or drop the edge runtime and treat them as app-only) unblocks: a coherent public/app boundary and, if public, skill/persona SEO. Related to the marketplace-detail entry above — same "Workforce content has no public, indexable home" root cause. **UPDATE 2026-06-14:** the sibling programmatic-SEO surface (`/compare/{slug}`, `/integrations/{slug}`) now provides the public, indexable home for comparison/integration intent (robots `Allow` + sitemap); the skills/personas public-vs-app split itself remains the open decision here.

- **`/agents/*` marketing pages lost their `.cc-shell` background wrapper.** [agents/layout.tsx](frontend/src/app/agents/layout.tsx) was simplified to a pass-through now that PublicShell provides the chrome; the old layout set `background: var(--bg-deep)` on a `.cc-shell` wrapper. The agents pages now inherit the global shell background. Verify the agents showcase/integrations/skills/shoutouts pages still read correctly; if any relied on `.cc-*` ambient styling (from the deleted MarketingNav style block), restyle them. Fixing unblocks: confirmed visual parity for the /agents cluster. **UPDATE 2026-06-14 (T1):** the code-level risk this flags — a page still depending on the deleted `.cc-*` styles — is **cleared**: a repo-wide grep finds **zero `cc-shell` / `.cc-*` references** in `frontend/src`, so nothing is left styling against the removed wrapper. Only the human visual spot-check of the /agents cluster remains (needs eyes on the rendered page; not a code change).

- **Per-route marketing teasers for authed routes are not indexable (SEO opportunity).** Logged-out visitors hitting an authed route now get a feature teaser + login/CTA via [RouteMarketing](frontend/src/components/RouteMarketing.tsx) + [routeMarketing.ts](frontend/src/lib/routeMarketing.ts) (gated in [ConditionalAppShell](frontend/src/components/ConditionalAppShell.tsx); middleware no longer redirects them to /login). But those routes stay `Disallow`-ed in [robots.txt](frontend/public/robots.txt) and the authed pages are client components with no `generateMetadata`, so the teasers render the root default `<title>` and aren't crawlable. They could become real per-feature SEO landing pages (e.g. `/ide` → "In-browser IDE for AI agents"). Fixing (allow select feature routes in robots, add `generateMetadata` per route — or canonicalize them to `/product#<section>` — and emit to the sitemap) unblocks: a feature-landing-page long-tail without building separate marketing URLs. `/debug` intentionally uses the generic default teaser (internal route, no marketing copy needed). **UPDATE 2026-06-14:** `/compare` + `/integrations` are now in `robots.txt` Allow + `sitemap.ts`; the authed feature-route teasers (`/ide`, etc.) remain `Disallow`-ed with no per-route `generateMetadata` — still open.

- **Landing-page prompt → Brain handoff routes into the internal tool/action registry only — no real MCP (Model Context Protocol) backend.** The home-page prompt input ([frontend/src/app/page.tsx](frontend/src/app/page.tsx)) saves the visitor's prompt and the global Brain replays it after auth ([pendingPrompt.ts](frontend/src/lib/brain/pendingPrompt.ts) + [FloatingBrain.tsx](frontend/src/components/brain/FloatingBrain.tsx) → [BrainPanel.tsx](frontend/src/components/brain/BrainPanel.tsx) `initialPrompt`). "MCP-ing" the request currently means the Brain acts via its existing in-app action registry ([BrainActionsContext.tsx](frontend/src/lib/brain/BrainActionsContext.tsx)) — there is no MCP client/connector that calls external MCP servers (Gmail, Drive, Calendar, etc.). Fixing (a real MCP connector layer: server registry, OAuth, tool discovery, and a bridge from `BrainActionsContext` tool specs to MCP `tools/call`) unblocks: the Brain acting on external systems over the actual protocol, not just registered page actions.

- **Pending-prompt capture is `localStorage`-only — single browser, not cross-device.** [savePendingPrompt/takePendingPrompt](frontend/src/lib/brain/pendingPrompt.ts) stash the landing prompt in `localStorage`, so a visitor who types on their phone then signs up on their laptop loses the prompt. Per the product decision (2026-05-31) this pass deliberately skipped a server-side anonymous record. Fixing (a public `POST /api/pending-prompts` keyed by an anonymous session id + a `pending_prompts` table with TTL/expiry, associated to the user on first authenticated request) unblocks: cross-device prompt continuity and analytics on abandoned prompts. **UPDATE 2026-06-14 — durable server record + claim shipped.** New `pending_prompts` table ([migration 0128](api/migrations/0128_pending_prompts.sql), **not yet applied to any live DB**), public `POST /api/pending-prompts` (fired best-effort from the landing page alongside the localStorage save) + web-authed `POST /api/pending-prompts/claim` that stamps `user_id`+`claimed_at` and replays through the Brain’s `FloatingBrain` fallback ([pendingPromptRoutes.ts](api/src/presentation/routes/pendingPromptRoutes.ts)). Adds durability, abandoned-prompt analytics, and same-browser recovery after a storage clear. **Still open:** true phone→laptop continuity — the claim is keyed by a per-browser `anon_id`, so the anonId must still be threaded through the signup link/email to reconnect across *different* browsers.

- **Deploy notifications shipped (in-app auto-reload banner + OS Web Push); fan-out is synchronous/unbounded, untested in CI, and only fires from the `cf-deploy` path.** This pass made the PWA actually surface new versions on every deploy: (a) [public/sw.js](frontend/public/sw.js) now carries a per-build `__BUILD_VERSION__` stamp ([scripts/stamp-sw-version.js](frontend/scripts/stamp-sw-version.js)) so the SW bytes change each deploy (root cause the banner never showed); (b) [PwaUpdateBanner.tsx](frontend/src/components/PwaUpdateBanner.tsx) checks for updates on focus/visibility/online and auto-reloads after a 60s countdown; (c) real Web Push — [webPush.ts](api/src/application/notifications/webPush.ts) (VAPID ES256 + RFC 8291 `aes128gcm`, pure Web Crypto, no Node dep), [pushSubscriptionRoutes.ts](api/src/presentation/routes/pushSubscriptionRoutes.ts) (`/api/push/{public-key,subscribe,notify-deploy}`), `push_subscriptions` (migration [0126](api/migrations/0126_push_subscriptions.sql)), SW `push`/`notificationclick` handlers, [pushNotifications.ts](frontend/src/lib/pushNotifications.ts) client + [DeployNotificationsManager.tsx](frontend/src/components/DeployNotificationsManager.tsx) opt-in; (d) [notify-deploy.mjs](frontend/scripts/notify-deploy.mjs) wired into `cf-deploy`. **Residuals:** (1) [deployNotificationService.ts](api/src/application/notifications/deployNotificationService.ts) selects ALL subscriptions with no LIMIT and fans out synchronously in 50-wide batches inside the request — a large subscriber base risks the Worker subrequest/CPU ceiling and a slow deploy-script call; needs a Cloudflare Queue (none bound in `wrangler.toml`) or a cron-batched fan-out. (2) No automated test for the VAPID/`aes128gcm` crypto in-repo — it was validated this pass only via a throwaway Node sign→verify + encrypt→decrypt round-trip; add a vitest that asserts the encrypt path decrypts with a known client keypair. (3) Push fires ONLY when a deploy runs `npm run cf-deploy`; a direct `wrangler deploy` or a CI path that doesn't call the hook won't notify, and the feature is inert until `VAPID_PUBLIC_KEY`/`VAPID_PRIVATE_KEY`/`VAPID_SUBJECT`/`DEPLOY_NOTIFY_SECRET` secrets are provisioned (`node api/scripts/gen-vapid-keys.mjs` then `wrangler secret put`). (4) The deploy push targets every subscription globally (correct for an app-version event) but there's no per-user notification preference beyond browser-level unsubscribe. Fixing (1)+(2) unblocks: a deploy fan-out that scales past a handful of users and is regression-guarded. **UPDATE 2026-06-14 — REMOVED. Push is the host platform's job (BurnRateOS.com), not Builderforce's, so the entire self-hosted Web Push stack was deleted: frontend `pushNotifications.ts`/`DeployNotificationsManager.tsx`/`notify-deploy.mjs` + the SW `push`/`notificationclick` handlers, and backend `pushSubscriptionRoutes.ts`/`webPush.ts`/`deployNotificationService.ts`/`push_subscriptions` (dropped in [migration 0195](api/migrations/0195_drop_push_subscriptions.sql), **not yet applied to any live DB**) + the `VAPID_*`/`DEPLOY_NOTIFY_SECRET` env and `gen-vapid-keys.mjs`. This resolves the `api.builderforce.ai/api/push/public-key` 503 (VAPID was never provisioned because push was never Builderforce's responsibility) and closes residuals (1)–(4) above. The in-app `PwaUpdateBanner` auto-reload (separate from push) is unaffected. Open: BurnRateOS must own the OS-level "new version" notification if that UX is still wanted; Builderforce no longer emits it.

- **Voice marketing-accuracy (#1991) + consent/provenance gate (#1996) are unaddressed in this pass.** The PRD's `VIBEVOICE_AVAILABLE`/`VIBEVOICE_CDN` flags and the Pricing/comparison copy claiming VibeVoice is live were **not found in the repo** (no `frontend/lib/services/tts-engines.ts`), so there was nothing to scope here — but the marketing-accuracy obligation stands once a real UI lands: do not imply cloning is live until #1994 ships. Separately, the consent attestation (`consent_attested_at` + `consent_text_version` on `studio_voice_clones`, ToS §9a), provenance disclosure on published listings, moderation gate on publish, and right-to-delete cache invalidation (PRD §5) are **not built** — they gate GA and depend on the `studio_voice_clones` table existing (#1994). The npm client carries `verifySpeaker` (re-upload identity check) as a building block. Building §5 unblocks legal GA of human-voice cloning.

### 🛠️ Open — Core product capability (190)

_The product itself: cloud-agent execution, engines & tools, PR/repo loop, IDE, Studio (video/voice), workflows, boards, brain, QA, observability._

- **Brain-driven writes only refresh the Tasks board — other data views still go stale until manual reload (2026-06-14).** A generic refresh bus now exists ([brainDataEvent.ts](frontend/src/lib/brain/brainDataEvent.ts): mutating platform capabilities `dispatchBrainDataChanged({domain,method})`; consumers subscribe via `onBrainDataChanged`), but only [TaskMgmtContent.tsx](frontend/src/components/TaskMgmtContent.tsx) subscribes (domains `tasks`/`executions`/`projects`). Every other page that holds its own list state and can be mutated by the Brain — Projects list, Specs/PRD list, Workflows, Workforce/agents, Boards/swimlanes, Prompts — still shows stale data after a Brain action until the user reloads. Fixing (one `onBrainDataChanged([...], reload)` effect per view) closes the Brain↔UI staleness gap platform-wide.
