- **Remove `@mariozechner/pi-*` entirely — ONLY `pi-tui` remains; the blocker is the atomic `src/tui`→`ink` flip.** `pi-agent-core`, `pi-ai`, and `pi-coding-agent` are at **0 imports and removed from `agent-runtime/package.json`** (the loop, model client, tools, OAuth/Codex, and embedded runner are all native/pi-free). `@mariozechner/pi-tui` is the **last** dep: ~6,500 LOC of interactive CLI (`agent-runtime/src/tui/*`, 17 component sites — `Container`/`Markdown`/`Editor`/`SelectList`/`SettingsList`/`Component`/`TUI`/…). **✅ Built 2026-06-14 — the ink replacement is real, not a skeleton:** `@builderforce/tui`'s [ink-renderer.ts](packages/tui/src/adapters/ink-renderer.ts) now mounts a live `ink`(^7)+`react`(^19) render tree (chat scrollback, status footer, history-aware input editor, focus-trapping `select`/`settings`/`confirm` overlays) behind the `TuiRenderer` port; `TextMetrics` is `string-width`/`cli-truncate`-backed; the two `pi-tui` text-metric sites (`tui-overlays`, `searchable-select-list`) already moved to a native `truncateToWidth` in `terminal/ansi.ts` (`ansi.test.ts`). `@builderforce/tui` `tsc` 0. **✅ Wired into `agent-runtime` 2026-06-14:** [renderer-registry.ts](agent-runtime/src/tui/renderer-registry.ts) (composition root: `headless`+`ink` registry, default ink, `resolveTuiRenderer`) + [ink-session.ts](agent-runtime/src/tui/ink-session.ts) `runInkSession` — a complete runnable ink chat loop through the port (input→`chat.send`; gateway `chat`/`agent` events→chat surface via the renderer-agnostic `TuiStreamAssembler`), reachable today via `BUILDERFORCE_AGENTS_INK_TUI=1 builderforce tui`; the `wireInkSession` core is DI'd + headlessly unit-tested (`ink-session.test.ts`, 6 tests). `tsgo` 0, 138 `src/tui` tests green. **Remaining (TTY-verified):** bring `runInkSession` to parity with the legacy pi-tui `runTui` (slash-command autocomplete, bash mode, session switching, verbose stats), flip the default, then delete the legacy pi-tui `src/tui` components and drop `@mariozechner/pi-tui` from [package.json](agent-runtime/package.json). Fixing unblocks the last third-party agent-framework dependency leaving the runtime.

- **TUI render seam built (`@builderforce/tui`) — the 18-site `pi-tui` migration + live `ink` render tree are the deferred tail (terminal-verified).** The framework-agnostic `TuiRenderer` contract + DI `RendererRegistry` + headless renderer + `ink` adapter skeleton landed ([packages/tui/](packages/tui/), `tsc` 0); see the pi-cutover entry's pass-14 update + [specs/builderforce/11-prd-engine-consolidation.md](specs/builderforce/11-prd-engine-consolidation.md) §5.1 Stage 4. **Remaining:** (a) migrate the 18 `@mariozechner/pi-tui` import-sites in `agent-runtime/src/tui/*` onto the port (they extend pi's `Component`/`Container`/`Editor`/`SelectList` classes directly — reexpress as view-intent); (b) build the live `ink` render tree in [ink-renderer.ts](packages/tui/src/adapters/ink-renderer.ts) (`start()` currently throws; add `ink`/`react`, swap placeholder width metrics for `string-width`/`cli-truncate`); (c) drop `pi-tui` from `agent-runtime/package.json` + `pnpm install`; (d) the On-Prem default-engine decision. Fixing unblocks: the last `@mariozechner/pi-*` dependency removal + a swappable terminal framework.

- **Cloud agents are wired but only happy-path validated — 50 gaps catalogued, none yet closed.** A new PRD ([specs/builderforce/09-prd-cloud-agent-validation.md](specs/builderforce/09-prd-cloud-agent-validation.md)) summarizes the three cloud execution paths (V1 pi loop, V2 Claude Agent SDK, cloud-Worker fallback) and enumerates 50 falsifiable gaps across dispatch, workspace/PR lifecycle, engine parity, steering/cancel, telemetry integrity, billing/BYO-key, and security/isolation. P0 highlights: cloud V2 runs `bypassPermissions` + Bash on shared infra with no documented sandbox (GAP-G1); cloud-Worker fallback has no steering/cancel honoring (GAP-S5/S6); no test reconstructs a run from `tool_audit_events`+`usage_snapshots`+`llm_usage_log` by `execution_id` (GAP-O1) nor asserts ledger==snapshot (GAP-O2); errored/cancelled runs leak the task workspace (GAP-W2); BYO-key-missing may silently fall to platform-billed key (GAP-B2). Fixing (execute PRD 09 phases 9a→9d, starting with telemetry/billing integrity then isolation, plus a `pnpm qa:cloud-agents` golden-path E2E) unblocks: cloud agents shippable as a GA runtime alongside self-hosted hosts.

- **Shared tool-catalogue status: 12 cross-runtime core tools + 21 Node-native tools are now under the shared `@builderforce/agent-tools` contract (33 total); ~6 remaining (`github_issue_workflow` + media `message`/`tts`/`canvas`/`image`/`browser`) need porting — media first needs a `ToolResult.content` block extension (text-only `data` can't carry images/audio/MEDIA tokens) (updated 2026-06-13).** **Cross-runtime core (12), defined directly in [core-tools.ts](packages/agent-tools/src/core-tools.ts)** and capability-gated/backed per surface: list_files, search_code, read_file, write_file, **edit_file** (cap `repo.edit`; cloud [read+commit] + Node [disk], NOT the container — its image only commits whole files), delete_file, run_checks, run_command, **web_fetch** (cap `web`; Node-backed via global `fetch`+HTML→text), **web_search** (cap `web.search`; defined, no backend advertised yet), ask_human, finish. **Node-native (21), 2026-06-13:** code-intelligence (5) in [node-code-tools.ts](agent-runtime/src/builderforce/shared-tools/node-code-tools.ts) — `git_history` (cap `shell`), `code_analysis`/`project_knowledge`/`codebase_search`/`codebase_semantic_search` (cap `repo.read`), read the working tree via `ctx.workspaceRoot`; orchestration/session (4) in [node-orchestration-tools.ts](agent-runtime/src/builderforce/shared-tools/node-orchestration-tools.ts) — `orchestrate`/`agent_fleet`/`workflow_status` (cap `orchestrate`), `save_session_handoff` (cap `memory`); service/session (12) built by the **`buildNodeServiceTools(deps)` factory** (DI seam over a `NodeServiceToolDeps` bag) in [node-service-tools.ts](agent-runtime/src/builderforce/shared-tools/node-service-tools.ts) + co-located `build*ToolDef` exports in their `agents/tools/*` files — `agents_list`/`sessions_list`/`sessions_history`/`sessions_spawn`/`session_status`/`subagents` (cap `orchestrate`), `sessions_send` (cap `message`), `gateway` (cap `process`), `nodes` (cap `orchestrate`), `cron` (cap `orchestrate`), `memory_search`/`memory_get` (cap `memory`, emitted only when config resolves). These reuse the existing TypeBox schema verbatim (TypeBox *is* JSON Schema) and share ONE body via an exported `run*()` that the pi wrapper also calls; `detailsData`/`nativeToolData` ([common.ts](agent-runtime/src/agents/tools/common.ts)) bridge the legacy `AgentToolResult` to the native `ToolResult.data` (throw-safe). `NODE_SURFACE_CAPS` advertises `orchestrate`/`memory`/`message`. `buildNodeToolRegistry(deps?)` assembles core + code + orchestration + service; the `builderforce-local` engine wires it + threads `workspaceRoot`. Tested in [node-code-tools.test.ts](agent-runtime/src/builderforce/shared-tools/node-code-tools.test.ts) + [node-registry.test.ts](agent-runtime/src/builderforce/shared-tools/node-registry.test.ts). The legacy pi files still hold the `AgentTool` shape ONLY because the still-default pi loop consumes it — deleted in cutover stage 3 (above). **Remaining (~6): `github_issue_workflow` (JSON, portable now); media `message`/`tts`/`canvas`/`image`/`browser`** — these return content blocks (images/audio/MEDIA tokens) the text-only `ToolResult.data` can't carry, so they need a `ToolResult.content` extension to the shared contract + engine handling before porting (logged below).

- **Shared `ToolResult` is text/JSON-only (`data`) — it cannot carry media (image/audio) content blocks, blocking native ports of `tts`/`canvas`/`image`/`browser`/`message`** ([tool.ts](packages/agent-tools/src/tool.ts) `ToolResult` has `data` + `control` but no `content`). The legacy pi tools return `{content:[...]}` (image blocks, `MEDIA:` tokens, `[[audio_as_voice]]`) the on-prem channel layer delivers. Fixing = add an optional `content?: ToolContentBlock[]` to `ToolResult`, have the engines (LocalAgentEngine sinks + cloud loop) surface it, then port the 5 media/channel tools via `buildNodeServiceTools(deps)`. Unblocks the final tool-layer (cutover stage 1) tools + true media parity on the native engine.

- **On-prem `ask_human` is NOT offered through the shared Node registry — the Node `CapabilityProvider` does not advertise the `human` capability** ([node-capability-provider.ts](agent-runtime/src/builderforce/shared-tools/node-capability-provider.ts) `NODE_SURFACE_CAPS` omits `human`; the legacy on-prem loop wires its own ask-human). So an agent on the `builderforce-local` engine cannot pause for a human via the shared `ask_human` tool. Fixing = add a `HumanCapability` concretion to the Node provider (CLI prompt / relay human-requests queue) and add `human` to `NODE_SURFACE_CAPS`, unblocking on-prem human-in-the-loop parity with cloud.

- **Newly added catalog model ids (openrouter free + paid + Cloudflare `@cf/...`) are unverified.** This pass added ~15 new entries to [api/src/application/llm/vendors/openrouter.ts](api/src/application/llm/vendors/openrouter.ts) (`openrouter/owl-alpha`, `deepseek/deepseek-v4-flash:free`, `arcee-ai/trinity-large-thinking:free`, `openai/gpt-oss-20b:free`, `meta-llama/llama-3-8b-instruct`, `google/gemma-3-4b-it`, `microsoft/phi-4`, `qwen/qwen3.5-9b`, `z-ai/glm-4-32b`, `openai/gpt-5-nano`, `openai/o4-mini`, `alibaba/qwen3.5-397b-a17b`) and one entry to [api/src/application/llm/vendors/cloudflare.ts](api/src/application/llm/vendors/cloudflare.ts) (`@cf/meta/llama-3-8b-instruct`). Operator gave the ids by hand without an `/v1/models` cross-check; wrong ids will surface as `404` from the upstream and the cascade will skip them (vendor cooldown drops them after 3 misses in 60s). Same drift risk as the existing NVIDIA NIM entry below. Fixing (curl `https://openrouter.ai/api/v1/models` with the OpenRouter key and `https://api.cloudflare.com/client/v4/accounts/<id>/ai/models/search` with the Cloudflare token, reconcile each vendor's catalog against live ids — remove or correct any 404'ing entries) unblocks: clean cascade ordering with no wasted attempts on phantom models.

- **NVIDIA NIM catalog model ids are wrong in production — 404s observed live.** Re-confirms the existing entry below: in the 2026-05-23 `llm-b9a3db1b-...` trace, both `mistralai/mistral-large-3-675b-instruct-2512` (returned `408` after our timeout) and `nvidia/mistral-nemotron` (`404`) appeared in the cascade for a caller-pinned `anthropic/claude-3-haiku` request — burning two attempts on doomed model ids. Compounds the "paid failover" bug closed in this pass because NVIDIA is the only non-OpenRouter vendor in the paid pool, so when the cascade falls through, it lands on the broken ids. Fixing (curl `https://integrate.api.nvidia.com/v1/models` with the API key, reconcile against [api/src/application/llm/vendors/nvidia.ts](api/src/application/llm/vendors/nvidia.ts) — verified-id allowlist only, drop the inferred org-prefix entries) unblocks: paid cascade tail actually reaches working models when OpenRouter is saturated.

- **The standardized cloud coding default `minimaxai/minimax-m2.7` is operator-supplied and unverified against the live NIM catalog.** `CODING_DEFAULT_MODEL` resolves to `minimaxai/minimax-m2.7` ([api/src/application/llm/vendors/nvidia.ts](api/src/application/llm/vendors/nvidia.ts) → lead of `CODING_MODEL_POOL` in [LlmProxyService.ts](api/src/application/llm/LlmProxyService.ts)) because M2.7 is FREE on NVIDIA NIM but PAID on OpenRouter. Reachability is **confirmed** — `NVIDIA_API_KEY` is bound on the api worker (`wrangler secret list`, 2026-06-12), so the NIM default dispatches rather than no-key-skipping; `minimax/minimax-m2.5:free` (OpenRouter) sits immediately after as failover. **Still open:** the exact id strings for the NIM coding entries added by hand — `minimaxai/minimax-m2.7` (the default) and `z-ai/glm-5.1` (a free coding-pool member) — are not cross-checked against live `https://integrate.api.nvidia.com/v1/models` (the key value isn't retrievable via `wrangler secret list` and there's no local NVIDIA key to curl with) — same drift risk as the NVIDIA NIM entry above; a wrong slug 404s and the cascade skips it (the default silently degrades to M2.5). Fixing (curl the NIM models endpoint with the bound key and confirm/correct each slug — vendors may ship these under a different org prefix or version) unblocks: M2.7/GLM-5.1 actually serving instead of the cascade burning a doomed attempt.

- **Gateway-side strict-mode validation only fires when consumers send `response_format: { type: 'json_schema', strict: true }`.** Today consumers like hired.video do their own client-side Zod validation after the fact and never set `response_format` on the outbound request, so the gateway can't help them retry the chain on schema mismatches — even though [jsonSchemaValidator.ts](api/src/application/llm/jsonSchemaValidator.ts) now supports it fully. Fixing (consumer-side migration: send `response_format: { type: 'json_schema', json_schema: { strict: true, schema } }` instead of post-call Zod) unblocks: cross-vendor retry on strict-schema failures, deletion of tenant-side retry loops, less wasted budget burning models that can't conform.

- **Epic decomposition foundation shipped; the agent reasoning step + board tree UI + fan-out routing are the residuals.** This pass built the task *type/hierarchy* data-model + API: migration [0112](api/migrations/0112_task_type_and_parent.sql) adds `task_type` (`task`|`epic` enum) + a nullable self-FK `parent_task_id` (ON DELETE SET NULL → deleting an Epic orphans, not cascade-deletes, its children) to [tasks](api/src/infrastructure/database/schema.ts), with a matching `TaskType` enum + `taskType`/`parentTaskId`/`isEpic`/`isAssignedToAgent` on the [Task entity](api/src/domain/task/Task.ts) and a `reclassifyAsEpic()` behaviour (flips type + sheds the agent assignee, since an Epic is a planning container). [TaskService](api/src/application/task/TaskService.ts) now has an **on-assign hook** (`onAssignedToAgent`, fired from create *and* update whenever a plain task newly transitions into AGENT ownership) that runs an injectable [EpicDecomposer](api/src/application/task/EpicDecomposer.ts) and, when the verdict is "Epic", calls the public `decomposeEpic` server action to reclassify→fan-out child tasks (each `parent_task_id`-linked, sequentially re-keyed, fanned out to the planned human/agent assignee). [TaskRepository](api/src/infrastructure/repositories/TaskRepository.ts) persists both columns + has `findChildren`; the board read path surfaces the tree via `taskType`/`parentTaskId` on every `GET /api/tasks` row plus new `GET /api/tasks/:id/tree` and `POST /api/tasks/:id/decompose` ([taskRoutes](api/src/presentation/routes/taskRoutes.ts)). Fan-out + reclassify is unit-tested ([epicDecomposition.test.ts](api/src/application/task/epicDecomposition.test.ts), 9 cases). **Residuals (deliberately scoped out):** (1) the `EpicDecomposer` is a **deterministic checklist-parsing heuristic** (`heuristicEpicDecomposer` — markdown `- [ ]`/`-`/`1.` lines → children), a clearly-marked stand-in for the real BA-agent reasoning step; swap an LLM-backed `assess()` (e.g. an `ideProxy(env)` structured completion returning the same `DecompositionPlan` shape) in via the already-wired constructor injection. (2) **No board UI** renders the parent/child tree yet — [TaskMgmtContent.tsx](frontend/src/components/TaskMgmtContent.tsx) still draws a flat status grid; children appear as standalone cards (data is there via the new fields, the nesting/expand UI is not). (3) Fan-out **assignee routing is pass-through** — `decomposeEpic` writes whatever assignee the plan specifies but does NOT resolve a *role* ("give the QA subtask to the QA agent") nor dispatch the children through [SwimlaneCoordinator](api/src/application/swimlane/SwimlaneCoordinator.ts); newly-created children just land in the backlog. Fixing all three unblocks: agents acting as real planners/BAs end-to-end. Builds on the human+agent assignee foundation.

- **Routing pools are hand-maintained from a hardcoded vendor catalog that drifts from the live OpenRouter `/models` API.** The FREE/PRO/CODING pools derive from static `VendorModule.catalog` arrays ([vendors/*.ts](api/src/application/llm/vendors/)), edited by hand. This pass caught real drift by calling the live API: invented ids (`qwen/qwen3-coder-480b-a35b-instruct` as an OpenRouter id, a `deepseek/deepseek-v4-flash:free` that doesn't exist), AND missing current best coders (`qwen/qwen3.7-plus`, `xiaomi/mimo-v2.5` = Programming #1, `nex-agi/nex-n2-pro:free`, `nvidia/nemotron-3-ultra-550b-a55b:free`) — now added/corrected. But the gateway ALREADY fetches the live catalog via [getCatalogCached](api/src/application/llm/modelCatalog.ts) for `/v1/catalog` (display only); routing ignores it. Fixing (derive the coding/free/paid pools — or at least validate them — from the cached live `/models` payload, filtering by `supported_parameters: tools` + a coding/programming tag, so a stale hardcoded id can never silently route to a 404 backstop again) unblocks: model selection that tracks OpenRouter's fast-moving free tier automatically instead of by manual catalog edits. Discovered when a cloud run fell to `gemini-2.5-flash-lite` because the hardcoded free coders were saturated/stale.

- **Drag-to-lane autonomous trigger uses the simple runtime executor, not the SwimlaneCoordinator — so multi-agent stages / success policies / lane actions don't fire.** Fixed this pass: dropping a ticket into a lane now passes the lane's configured cloud agent (`decideLaneAutoRun`, gated by the lane's `auto`/`human` gate — NOT the legacy `boards.autonomous` flag, which is always false → would have blocked every run) → `submitExecution` payload `cloudAgentRef`+`model`, so a "Coder Agent (V2)" lane actually runs AS that agent instead of the V1 gateway-default. BUT the path still goes `patchStatus → runtimeApi.submitExecution` (single cloud run), bypassing [SwimlaneCoordinator](api/src/application/swimlane/SwimlaneCoordinator.ts): only the FIRST cloud lane agent runs; a lane's `executionMode: 'parallel'` multi-agent fan-out, `successPolicy`/`successThreshold`, and `actionType` (advance/move_ticket/run_workflow) are ignored on a manual drag. Fixing (route lane-entry through the board coordinator's ticket-run start when the lane has >1 agent or a non-advance action) unblocks: full board automation semantics on drag, not just single-agent autorun. Discovered tracing why a dragged ticket ran as "BuilderForce Cloud (default)".

- **Lane agents with `runtime` host/local/remote aren't dispatched by the drag trigger — only `runtime: 'cloud'`.** [decideLaneAutoRun](frontend/src/lib/laneAutoRun.ts) picks the first cloud agent; a lane configured only with a self-hosted/remote agent falls back to the legacy status auto-run (no agent pinned), so that host-run agent never executes on drag. Fixing (resolve a host/remote lane agent to an `agentHostId` or coordinator dispatch) unblocks: self-hosted lane agents triggering on drag, parity with cloud lane agents.

- **IDE file storage diverges between the worker and api backends (different buckets AND key layouts).** The frontend routes file reads/writes to the worker (`builderforce-storage`, key `{projectId}/…`, [worker/src/routes/files.ts](worker/src/routes/files.ts)) when `NEXT_PUBLIC_WORKER_URL` is set, else to the api (`builderforce-uploads`, key `ide/projects/{projectId}/…`, [ideRoutes.ts](api/src/presentation/routes/ideRoutes.ts)). The two never share data. Server-side template seeding ([projectTemplate.ts](api/src/application/project/projectTemplate.ts)) writes only to the api bucket, so when the worker is the active backend a freshly-created project's seeded scaffold never appears (Run silently falls back to its in-memory defaults). The new repo-import sidesteps this by persisting through the same `saveFile` path the IDE reads from, but the underlying split remains a latent correctness hazard for any server-side write to project files. Fixing (one bucket + one key layout, or have the worker proxy the api's storage) unblocks: server-side seeding/writes that the IDE actually sees regardless of backend.

- **Cloud PRD generation + V1 workflow executor still dispatch on the fixed FREE pool.** Closing the cloud-coding-agent plan-routing gap routed the durable/container *tool loops* through `llmProxyForPlan(env, effectivePlan, premiumOverride)`, but the one-shot PRD generator ([taskPrd.ts](api/src/application/prd/taskPrd.ts) `ideProxy(env)`) and the V1 workflow executor ([workflow/cloudExecutor.ts](api/src/application/workflow/cloudExecutor.ts) `ideProxy(env)`) still use the free pool. Low impact (PRD gen is a cheap structured-doc completion free models handle fine; V1 workflows are the legacy engine), so deliberately left on free. Fixing (thread the run's `effectivePlan`/`premiumOverride` — already resolved once per run — into these two callers via `llmProxyForPlan`) unblocks: a Pro tenant's PRD/V1-workflow steps also running on premium models, fully consistent with the coding loop.

- **The core app component classes (`.btn` family, `.input`, `.label`, `.page-header`, `.card-header`, `.card-title`, `.modal-title`, base `.badge`, base `.empty-state`) were referenced in 145+ call-sites across 26 files but were never defined in any loaded stylesheet — now fixed, so spot-check the wider app.** Tailwind ships `@tailwind components` with an empty `plugins: []` ([frontend/tailwind.config.js](frontend/tailwind.config.js)) and the only stylesheet ([frontend/src/app/globals.css](frontend/src/app/globals.css)) defined only the *variant* leaves (`.page-title`, `.card`, `.badge-green`, `.empty-state-title`, …) — so every page using bare `.btn`/`.input`/`.page-header` fell back to native chrome or stacked layout, which is why only `/prompts` (self-contained inline styles) looked finished. This pass added the missing base classes to globals.css matched to the `/prompts` aesthetic. **Deferred:** the fix lights up chrome on many pages beyond the four normalized here (admin, marketplace, models, settings, workforce sub-views, ArtifactAssigner, …) that were silently relying on the same undefined classes; they should be visually spot-checked for any page that had hand-tuned around the missing styles. Fixing (a quick visual sweep of `.btn`/`.input`/`.empty-state` consumers) unblocks: confidence the design-system completion didn't regress a page that compensated for the gap.

- **Marketplace pages aren't fully converged: Prompts keeps a local `card` style const and a different create-UX pattern from Skills/Personas/Content.** This pass unified headers, tab bars, search/filter placement, badges, and buttons across `/content-manager`, `/skills`, `/personas`, `/prompts` onto the shared classes, but two residuals remain: (1) [prompts/page.tsx](frontend/src/app/prompts/page.tsx) still renders cards + detail-drawer surfaces via a local `card` CSSProperties const (padding 16 / `--bg-base`) instead of the shared `.card` class (padding 20 / `--card`), so prompt cards sit slightly tighter on a different surface token; (2) Prompts uses an inline expanding `CreatePromptForm` while the other three use a centered `.modal-overlay` create dialog. Both deferred to avoid restyling the prompts grid/detail and to keep a product decision (inline vs modal create) explicit. Fixing unblocks: pixel-identical card chrome and one canonical create pattern across all four library pages.

- **Brain "capture execution" trace is in-memory per session — it doesn't persist across reload.** This pass added a Brain-side triage capture (the `⧉` button beside `+ New` in both BrainPanel headers): [useBrainConversation.ts](brain-embedded/src/useBrainConversation.ts) records a per-chat `BrainTraceEvent[]` (LLM steps, full tool chain with args/results/timing, intermediate assistant messages, and errors — thrown tool errors are now fed back as `{ok:false}` AND traced) and `buildTriageReport()` ([brainTriage.ts](brain-embedded/src/brainTriage.ts)) assembles the same errors-first → trace → logs → transcript report the host/cloud Logs view emits. **Residual (deliberate, mirrors `transcriptRef`):** the trace lives only in a `useRef` Map for the session, so a page reload (or capturing a chat from a prior session) yields only the steps that ran since mount — the persisted chat tables have no tool columns. Fixing (persist trace events to a `brain_chat_trace` table written alongside the final-assistant message, and rehydrate on chat load) unblocks: capturing a complete report for any historical Brain run, not just the live session.

- **A cloud coding run that floors onto a non-coder backstop now SAYS so on the timeline, but is not aborted/escalated — and the rationale event is durable-loop-only.** This pass made model selection legible in the execution triage (the #1 unanswered question on exec #59: dispatched `gateway-default`, silently floored onto the `gemini-2.5-flash-lite` backstop, spun 7 steps, shipped nothing): `runCloudToolLoop` now emits a run-start `model.select` event (requested model, strict-pin vs soft-seed, the seed + whether it's a curated coder, the plan's reachable coders) and the existing `coding_model_degraded` event ([cloudAgentEngine.ts](api/src/application/runtime/cloudAgentEngine.ts) `emitModelSelection`/`emitCodingModelDegraded`) now spells out cause (curated coders unreachable: vendor key unbound / cooled down / outage) AND consequence (backstop generalist loops on search, finishes with no edits). **Residuals (deliberately scoped out):** (1) **Observability only — no policy change.** A degraded run still proceeds and burns its full step budget producing nothing; it is flagged, not stopped. A Coder Agent that resolves to a non-coder backstop arguably should hard-fail fast (or retry on a different reachable coder) rather than spin — needs a product decision on abort-vs-warn. (2) The `model.select` rationale fires from the durable loop only; the long-lived **Container** executor ([handleContainerOp](api/src/application/runtime/cloudAgentEngine.ts)) picks per-op with no run-start hook, so a container-surface run gets the `coding_model_degraded` *outcome* event but not the up-front selection rationale. (3) The dispatch event ([runtimeRoutes.ts](api/src/presentation/routes/runtimeRoutes.ts)) still logs the opaque `gateway-default` label — now superseded by `model.select` but left in place. Fixing all three unblocks: degraded coding runs that fail fast instead of wasting budget, and uniform selection telemetry across both cloud executors. Builds directly on entry [1247] (stale/saturated hardcoded coders → fell to gemini-2.5-flash-lite).

- **Subdomain hosting ships static-only and behind the path form — the wildcard DNS/route + container web-serving are unprovisioned.** This pass added Designer→subdomain publishing: migration [0121](api/migrations/0121_project_sites.sql) (`project_sites`), an in-browser build-capture (`handlePublishBuild` mounts→`npm run build`→`readDirRecursive('dist')` in [IDENew.tsx](frontend/src/components/IDENew.tsx) via [useWebContainer](frontend/src/hooks/useWebContainer.ts)), a multipart publish endpoint + cached subdomain→site lookup ([ideRoutes.ts](api/src/presentation/routes/ideRoutes.ts) `POST /projects/:id/publish`, [siteHosting.ts](api/src/application/ide/siteHosting.ts)), a public R2 server ([sitesRoutes.ts](api/src/presentation/routes/sitesRoutes.ts)), and the [SitePublishPanel](frontend/src/components/SitePublishPanel.tsx). **Residuals (deliberately scoped out):** (1) **Wildcard hosting is wired but needs the DNS record + a deploy.** The Worker route `*.apps.builderforce.ai/*` is now in [api/wrangler.toml](api/wrangler.toml) and a Host-serving middleware in [index.ts](api/src/index.ts) (`tryServeHostedSite`) serves any path on a hosting subdomain from R2; `AUTH_CACHE_KV` is already bound. **Still required:** (a) a proxied wildcard DNS record `*.apps → AAAA 100:: (proxied)` — the local wrangler token has only `zone:read`, not `dns_records:edit`, so create it via the dashboard or a DNS-scoped token (`curl -X POST https://api.cloudflare.com/client/v4/zones/<ZONE_ID>/dns_records -H "Authorization: Bearer <DNS_EDIT_TOKEN>" -H 'Content-Type: application/json' --data '{"type":"AAAA","name":"*.apps","content":"100::","proxied":true}'`); (b) `wrangler deploy` (currently blocked locally only because the `[[containers]]` image build needs Docker running). Until both land, sites are reachable via the path form `/api/sites/<sub>/...` (wired + working, surfaced as "preview" in the panel). (2) **Container mode is schema-only** — `project_sites.mode='container'` exists but the V2 Cloudflare Container serves no HTTP; long-lived web-serving (SSR/APIs) is a later phase. (3) **Build-default parity** — `handlePublishBuild` only injects a default `package.json`; unlike `handleRun` it doesn't backfill index.html/main.jsx/index.css/vite.config, so a project missing those (and never Run) can fail the build. (4) **Orphaned R2 on project delete** — `project_sites` cascades on `projects` delete (FK) but the `sites/<sub>/...` R2 objects are not swept, leaking storage; add an on-delete R2 prefix purge. Fixing all four unblocks: real `<sub>.apps.builderforce.ai` hosting (static now, container later) with no orphaned assets.

- **Vision image input ships inline-data-URL-first; the signed-URL fallback needs `JWT_SECRET` and the gateway picks the vision model by shape, not a hard pin.** This pass wired uploaded/pasted/dropped images into OpenAI `image_url` content parts so the model actually sees them (was previously flattened to a markdown link): [ChatInput.tsx](frontend/src/components/ChatInput.tsx) paste/drop → [useBrainConversation](brain-embedded/src/useBrainConversation.ts) builds `ContentPart[]` from a downscaled data URL ([imagePrep.ts](brain-embedded/src/imagePrep.ts)), falling back to a signed public URL ([brainFilesRoutes.ts](api/src/presentation/routes/brainFilesRoutes.ts) + [uploadSign.ts](api/src/infrastructure/auth/uploadSign.ts)) for oversize images. The gateway already routes `image_url` requests to a vision model via `reorderPoolByShape`. **Residuals:** (1) the signed-URL path no-ops to the text link when `JWT_SECRET` is unbound (graceful, but silent); (2) downscaling targets ~1568px/3.5MB so it covers ~all real images, but a pathological one still degrades to text; (3) the Brain sends no explicit vision-model hint — it relies on the gateway's shape reorder + cross-vendor recovery, so a non-vision caller-pinned model would burn one attempt before failover. Fixing unblocks: guaranteed vision routing + a louder signal when signing is unconfigured.

- **Cloud human-in-the-loop SHIPPED for the durable/Worker surfaces — residuals are the container surface, the chip-resume glyph, and unanswered-question lifecycle.** A blocked cloud agent can now ask instead of failing silently: new `ask_human` tool ([cloudAgentTools.ts](api/src/application/runtime/cloudAgentTools.ts)) → records a `question` approval scoped to the run (`execution_id`/`cloud_agent_ref`, migration 0120) into the SAME human-requests queue + `HumanRequestsView` self-hosted agents use, fans out Slack+email via the shared [approvalNotifier.ts](api/src/application/approval/approvalNotifier.ts) (extracted from the approval route, now used by both), parks the run in the new `paused` execution state (amber "needs attention" chip on the board), and resumes when a human answers: `PATCH /api/approvals/:id` → [executionResume.ts](api/src/application/runtime/executionResume.ts) delivers the answer as a steer and wakes the durable runner via a new `CloudRunnerDO` `/resume` (the loop drains the answer on its next tick). **Residuals (deliberately scoped out):** (1) **Container surface** ([handleContainerOp](api/src/application/runtime/cloudAgentEngine.ts)) is NOT wired — it picks per-op with no run-start/pause hook, so `ask_human` is intentionally absent from `CONTAINER_AGENT_TOOLS` (asserted in [cloudAgentHumanInLoop.test.ts](api/src/application/runtime/cloudAgentHumanInLoop.test.ts)); since the container falls back to the DO today this is latent, but a true long-lived container needs its own pause/resume op. (2) The board/chip **`resume` play-glyph re-runs a fresh execution** rather than calling a dedicated resume-execution endpoint — true resume is the answer path; the glyph is a secondary nudge. (3) The **Output "Send" box on a `paused` run** doesn't resume (it follows the terminal/steer branch); the canonical answer channel is the human-requests queue. (4) **No timeout/auto-fail for an unanswered cloud question** — a `paused` run waits indefinitely (intended for HITL, but a cancel-while-paused leaves the DO cursor + a `pending` approval dangling, since cloud questions set no `expiresAt`). (5) **Task isn't routed to a `needs_attention` lane on pause** — only the amber chip signals it; wiring `paused`→lane move would close the exec #69 ask fully. Fixing these unblocks: HITL parity across all cloud surfaces + a self-cleaning paused-run lifecycle. Builds on the model-selection observability entry above (same "silent no-output run" failure class, exec #59/#69).

- **NVIDIA NIM catalog model ids are partially unverified.** [api/src/application/llm/vendors/nvidia.ts](api/src/application/llm/vendors/nvidia.ts) registers 11 free models against `https://integrate.api.nvidia.com/v1/chat/completions`. Confidently mapped: `mistralai/mistral-large-3-675b-instruct-2512`, `nvidia/mistral-nemotron`, `nvidia/nemotron-mini-4b-instruct`, `qwen/qwen3-coder-480b-a35b-instruct`, `google/gemma-2-2b-it`, `google/gemma-3n-e4b-it`, `microsoft/phi-4-multimodal-instruct`. Inferred org prefixes (need verification against NIM's `/v1/models` listing): `minimax/minimax-m2.7`, `stepfun-ai/step-3.5-flash`, `bytedance/seed-oss-36b-instruct`, `abacusai/dracarys-llama-3_1-70b-instruct`. Wrong ids will surface as 404s and the cascade will skip them, but they pollute the pool until corrected. Fixing (curl `https://integrate.api.nvidia.com/v1/models` with the API key, reconcile against the catalog) unblocks: clean cascade ordering, no wasted 404 attempts.

- **Cloud Done-finalize doesn't emit a `pr_opened` tool-audit event, and the no-existing-PR guard is a read-time check (narrow double-PR race).** This pass closed the host/cloud finalize-parity gap: [dispatchTaskFinalize](api/src/presentation/routes/taskRoutes.ts) now opens a PR server-side via [openTaskPullRequest](api/src/application/repos/openTaskPullRequest.ts) when a *cloud*-assigned task hits Done with a pushed `gitBranch` and no `githubPrUrl` yet. Two residuals: (1) unlike the inline run-end finalize in [runCloudToolLoop](api/src/presentation/routes/runtimeRoutes.ts) (which calls `recordCloudToolEvent` with a `pr_opened`/`merge_to_main` event), the Done-transition path records only the `pull_requests` row + task `githubPrUrl` — so the Observability timeline shows no `pr_opened` event for a manually-completed cloud ticket. (2) The `!githubPrUrl` guard reads task state at Done-time; if an execution's inline finalize is opening a PR at the same instant a human drags the card to Done, both can fire before either writes `githubPrUrl` → a duplicate PR. Both are narrow (the common path is execution-opens-PR-then-auto-Done). **Investigated 2026-06-13 — needs two prerequisites, not a drop-in:** (1) the uniform-emit can't just call [recordCloudToolEvent](api/src/application/runtime/cloudAgentEngine.ts) from `openTaskPullRequest` because that helper requires a non-optional `executionId` and writes an *execution-scoped* row (`sessionKey: exec:<id>`); the Done-finalize path is *task-scoped* with no execution, so a uniform `pr_opened` needs a task-scoped audit channel (nullable `executionId` + `sessionKey: task:<id>`) AND a check that the Observability timeline read path renders execution-less events (else the event is written but invisible). (2) The race-free guard needs an atomic claim *before* the external PR-create call (the URL isn't known until after, so a conditional update on `githubPrUrl` can't claim pre-creation) — i.e. a new nullable `tasks.pr_opening_at` claim column set via `UPDATE … WHERE id=? AND pr_opening_at IS NULL AND github_pr_url IS NULL` (a migration, hence live-DB-apply gated), rolled back on PR-create failure. Fixing both unblocks: uniform cloud PR observability + race-free single-PR finalize.

- **Changes-tab Monaco diff viewer reads only the cloud ticket branch `builderforce/task-<id>`; on-prem custom-branch runs show "No content found."** This pass added a [FileChangeViewer](frontend/src/components/agent/FileChangeViewer.tsx) that fetches a changed file's current+base contents via the new `GET /api/runtime/tasks/:taskId/file-content` route ([runtimeRoutes.ts](api/src/presentation/routes/runtimeRoutes.ts)) and renders the diff in Monaco (the same editor the IDE uses). The route resolves the branch via [resolveTicketRepoContext](api/src/application/repos/commitFileAsPendingChange.ts), which hardcodes `builderforce/task-<taskId>` — correct for cloud V2 runs (same resolver the cloud `commitAgentFile`/`write_file` path commits through), but on-prem runs and any task with an explicit [tasks.branchName](api/src/infrastructure/database/schema.ts) (migration 0091; [prDispatch.buildBranchName](api/src/application/repos/prDispatch.ts) emits `task/<slug>` or the explicit name) commit to a *different* branch, so the viewer reads the wrong ref and degrades to "No content found." Fixing (thread `tasks.branchName` into `resolveTicketRepoContext` and have both the read path and `commitAgentFile` honor it, so cloud + on-prem + custom-branch all converge on one branch source of truth) unblocks: the diff viewer working for every execution path, not just default-branch cloud runs. Same hardcoded-branch root cause as the cloud commit path, so fix them together.

- **Workforce Teams drive assignee scoping; lane-agent picker scoping is the remaining edge.** Teams shipped end-to-end: migration [0114](api/migrations/0114_workforce_teams.sql) (`teams` + polymorphic `team_members` [`human`|`cloud_agent`|`host_agent`, mirroring the task-assignee identity] + `team_projects` M:N), [teamRoutes.ts](api/src/presentation/routes/teamRoutes.ts) CRUD/members/projects + cached `GET /by-project/:projectId` and `GET /by-project/:projectId/workforce` (MANAGER+), [lib/teams.ts](frontend/src/lib/teams.ts), the [TeamsView](frontend/src/components/teams/TeamsView.tsx) Workforce tab, and the Teams tab in the [Board-config panel](frontend/src/components/board/BoardConfigPanel.tsx) (assigns teams to a board's project). **Now wired into assignee resolution:** the manual task assignee picker ([TaskMgmtContent.tsx](frontend/src/components/TaskMgmtContent.tsx) — create dialog + drawer) filters its human/cloud-agent/host options to the project's assigned-team members when any team is assigned (falls back to the full tenant roster otherwise); the auto-assign recommender ([assigneeRecommender.ts](api/src/application/metrics/assigneeRecommender.ts) `loadProjectTeamMembers`, shared with the picker endpoint) already scopes the same way. **Residuals:** (1) the **board lane-agent picker** ([BoardConfigPanel.tsx](frontend/src/components/board/BoardConfigPanel.tsx) `AgentList` → `loadAgentPool`) is NOT team-scoped — it uses the tenant-wide pool whose identity space (`workforce`/`registered` agents from `/api/agents`) doesn't line up 1:1 with `team_members` (`cloud_agent`=ide_agents.id / `host_agent`=agent_hosts.id), so a clean filter needs the pool reconciled to the team-member id spaces first; `SwimlaneCoordinator` dispatch stays correctly agnostic (it runs the explicitly-configured lane agent). (2) The **all-projects board view** (`TaskMgmtContent` with no `projectId`) can't scope the per-task picker to each task's own project — it stays tenant-wide there; only the single-project board scopes. (3) `team_members.member_name` is denormalized and only refreshed on (re-)add, so renaming a user/agent/host drifts the team's stored label until re-added (the picker dodges this by filtering live lists, but the TeamsView roster still shows the stale name). (4) The member picker's agent pool is owned cloud agents (`/api/workforce/agents/mine`) + remote hosts only; marketplace-*hired* agents (`/agents/purchased`) are not offered.

- **"V2 Cloud Agent (Node/Container)" real Cloudflare Container is BUILT — needs deploy + Containers-enabled account, and has two known bounds.** The `container` surface now runs on a real long-lived Cloudflare Container ([AgentContainerDO](api/src/infrastructure/relay/AgentContainerDO.ts) via the `[[containers]]` block in [wrangler.toml](api/wrangler.toml), image [api/container/](api/container/server.mjs)). The container clones the repo to disk, runs the agent loop in one persistent process with a REAL shell (`run_command` for build/type-check/lint/test), and delegates every LLM step / commit / PR finalize back to the Worker's `/internal/container-op` endpoint (authenticated by a per-run HMAC token, [containerRunToken.ts](api/src/application/runtime/containerRunToken.ts)) so metering/commit/finalize stay single-impl (the finalize block was extracted to the shared `finalizeCloudRun`). Dispatch routes `container`-surface V2 runs to it and degrades to the durable DO only when the binding is absent or the container can't start. **Remaining:** (1) **deploy** — needs a Workers Paid plan with Containers enabled and a `wrangler deploy` that builds `api/container/Dockerfile`; not yet built/pushed from this environment (no Docker/CF here), so end-to-end is unverified. (2) **inactivity bound** — `sleepAfter` is 20m and the loop's outbound calls don't renew the Container activity timer, so a single run that exceeds ~20m of wall-clock could be stopped mid-flight; raise `sleepAfter` or add a keep-alive ping for very-long tasks. (3) **clone token in run spec** — the Worker passes a tokened `x-access-token` git URL to the container so its shell can clone; it's short-lived and internal, but is a wider exposure than the DO loop (which commits via the GitHub API and never hands out a token) — consider a scoped git-proxy for the container instead. (4) **non-GitHub providers** — the tokened clone URL is built only for `provider.startsWith('github')`; GitLab/others run reasoning+commit-only (no local clone, so `run_command` returns "no repo"). Also: the agent picker ([RunAgentControl.tsx](frontend/src/components/task/RunAgentControl.tsx)) doesn't label which of the three cloud types (V1 / V2-Durable / V2-Container) an agent is, so users can't tell the surface at selection time (user opted to defer the picker chip).

- **V2 cloud agents run fully in the cloud (all Cloudflare); the `durable` (CloudRunnerDO) executor is built — needs deploy verification.** A V2 cloud agent picks a `runtime_surface` at creation (migration 0105 on `ide_agents`; selector in [CloudAgentFormFields](frontend/src/components/workforce/CloudAgentFormFields.tsx); resolved in `resolveCloudAgent`; routed via [cloudDispatch.resolveCloudSurface](api/src/application/runtime/cloudDispatch.ts)). Both surfaces execute **in the cloud, on Cloudflare** (no local/hybrid/Fly.io): **`durable`** = [CloudRunnerDO](api/src/infrastructure/relay/CloudRunnerDO.ts), a Durable Object running the cloud agent loop ONE LLM step per `alarm()` tick with conversation state persisted in DO storage — fresh CPU/subrequest budget per tick, so it survives the ~30s `waitUntil` wall and runs to completion (mirrors [AnalysisRunnerDO](api/src/infrastructure/relay/AnalysisRunnerDO.ts)). Built this pass: `CLOUD_RUNNER` binding (env.ts + wrangler.toml) + `new_sqlite_classes=["CloudRunnerDO"]` migration (tag v5) + export in index.ts; `dispatchAndQueue` kicks off the DO (interim `runCloudExecution` Worker loop is the fallback when the binding is absent); `runCloudToolLoop` parameterized for per-tick resume (Worker path behavior preserved by defaults); orphan ceiling is now a **heartbeat** — cloud runs measured from `updated_at` (bumped each tick) in both [RuntimeService.isOrphaned](api/src/application/runtime/RuntimeService.ts) and the [reaper](api/src/application/runtime/staleExecutionReaper.ts). **`container`** = a long-lived **Cloudflare Container** runtime (for very long/continuous tasks) — dispatched to an online runtime via the relay, and **gracefully falls back to the durable DO** (recorded as a `runtime.fallback` event) when none is online, so it never dies. The Fly.io `agent-runtime/fly.toml` was an unused orphan (wired into no CI/deploy) and was deleted — the stack is Cloudflare-only. REMAINING: cannot verify DO/alarm behavior locally — verify on deploy that a durable V2 run ticks to completion + PR/merge; the actual **Cloudflare Container** executor for the `container` surface is a future build (today it falls back to the DO); CloudRunnerDO notifications are skipped (UI polls) so live streaming is poll-only for durable runs.

- **Workforce member metrics + DORA + planner consumption + Calendar sync shipped end-to-end (backend + frontend, migrations live on Neon); only operator-config remains.** The metrics keystone: member capability/availability **profiles** (migration [0116](api/migrations/0116_member_profiles.sql) `member_profiles`), an append-only **task_status_transitions** log + `tasks.completed_at`/`last_worked_at`/`redo_count`/`reopen_count` (migration [0117](api/migrations/0117_task_status_transitions.sql)), and **member_metrics_period + deployment_events** (migration [0118](api/migrations/0118_member_metrics_dora.sql)) feeding [workforceMetrics.ts](api/src/application/metrics/workforceMetrics.ts) behind `GET/PUT /api/members/*` ([memberRoutes.ts](api/src/presentation/routes/memberRoutes.ts)). Transition recording fires from the agent-execution path ([RuntimeService](api/src/application/runtime/RuntimeService.ts) `onTaskStatusSync` → [syncExecutionTaskLifecycle](api/src/application/task/taskLifecycle.ts)) + the dequeue claim + the human PATCH, and a terminal run stamps the true work-stopped signal `tasks.last_worked_at`; **DORA deployment_events auto-produced** at the merge chokepoint ([recordPullRequestRow.ts](api/src/application/repos/recordPullRequestRow.ts) — every PR merge writes a `success` deploy; post-merge CI `failure` flips `is_failure`, a later `success` stamps `restored_at` for MTTR); **planner consumption** is live via [assigneeRecommender.ts](api/src/application/metrics/assigneeRecommender.ts) (ranks by availability + spare WIP + skill match + ramp) behind `GET /api/members/recommend`, injected into the Epic fan-out; **frontend** ships the Performance tab ([WorkforceMetricsContent.tsx](frontend/src/components/workforce/WorkforceMetricsContent.tsx)) + capability/availability editor ([MemberProfileEditor.tsx](frontend/src/components/workforce/MemberProfileEditor.tsx)). **Google Calendar sync built** (migration [0122](api/migrations/0122_google_calendar_provider.sql) adds the `google_calendar` provider; [googleCalendarSync.ts](api/src/application/integrations/googleCalendarSync.ts) overlays busy→availability + events→PTO onto profiles via the existing integration-credentials framework; `POST /api/members/:kind/:ref/calendar-sync` + a "Sync from Google Calendar" button; AES-GCM credential crypto extracted to the shared [credentialCrypto.ts](api/src/application/integrations/credentialCrypto.ts)). **Migrations 0116–0118 + 0122 applied to the live Neon DB and verified idempotent.** **Operator-config remaining (not code gaps):** (1) to *use* Calendar sync a tenant must connect a `google_calendar` integration credential and (for token refresh) set `GOOGLE_OAUTH_CLIENT_ID`/`GOOGLE_OAUTH_CLIENT_SECRET`; the per-member calendar id defaults to the user's email, so reading other users' calendars needs Workspace domain-wide read or per-user consent. **Minor code follow-ups:** the merge-path deployment write has no `env` to bump the workforce-metrics cache version (a fresh DORA read can lag up to the token TTL / next status write); the Epic fan-out recommender ranks on capacity/availability only (no per-child skill hint passed yet).

- **No pause/resume execution lifecycle — the chip's `resume` (play) affordance is unreachable.** The execution chip ([ExecutionChip.tsx](frontend/src/components/agent/ExecutionChip.tsx)) re-runs failed/cancelled executions and is wired to show a play/resume glyph for a `paused` status via the shared [rerunAffordance](frontend/src/components/board/AgentChip.tsx), but the backend `execution_status` enum ([schema.ts](api/src/infrastructure/database/schema.ts)) has only `pending|submitted|running|completed|failed|cancelled` — there is no `paused` state, nor a pause/resume endpoint or a way to checkpoint+resume a cloud run mid-loop. So the `resume` branch never renders today. Also note: "re-run" creates a *new* execution that re-submits the task (it does not continue the old run's context/partial work — for cloud runs it re-plans from the PRD and operates on the same ticket branch). Fixing (add a `paused` status + `POST /executions/:id/pause|resume`, persist enough run state to continue, and surface it through the existing chip affordance) unblocks: pausing a long/expensive run and continuing it instead of restarting from scratch.

- **Host-run terminal failures show on the Timeline but not the Log view.** This pass made every terminal failure (orphan-reap, FAILED transition, stale-run reaper) emit a `run.failed` tool-audit event ([recordRunFailureEvent.ts](api/src/application/runtime/recordRunFailureEvent.ts)), so for **cloud** runs the error now appears in both the Logs and Timeline tabs (both derive from `tool_audit_events`). For **self-hosted host** runs the Timeline picks it up (it reads host `tool_audit_events` via `eventsByHost`), but the **Log view** is sourced only from the host's live WebSocket relay stream + cloud-derived lines ([ObservabilityContent.tsx](frontend/src/components/ObservabilityContent.tsx) `cloudLogLines`), so a host that crashed/disconnected before the failure was reaped will not show the `run.failed` line in its Log tab (the host is offline → no WS). Fixing (fold `eventsByHost` error events into the derived log lines, or backfill the host log pane from `tool_audit_events` when the WS is disconnected) unblocks: parity so host failures surface in the Log tab too, not just the Timeline.

- **[PR CREATE + MERGE + CORE DETAIL now multi-provider 2026-06-13 — needs live-provider validation + rich-detail parity] In-product PR lifecycle.** The full non-GitHub PR loop now works for **GitHub, GitLab, and Bitbucket Cloud**: [createPullRequest.ts](api/src/application/repos/createPullRequest.ts) (pure `buildCreatePrRequest`: GitHub `POST /pulls` head/base; GitLab `POST /merge_requests` source/target_branch; Bitbucket `POST /pullrequests` nested branch refs) → [mergePullRequest.ts](api/src/application/repos/mergePullRequest.ts) (pure `buildMergeRequest`: GitHub `PUT /pulls/:n/merge`+merge_method; GitLab `PUT /merge_requests/:iid/merge`+squash; Bitbucket `POST /pullrequests/:id/merge`+merge_strategy) → [getPullRequestDetail.ts](api/src/application/repos/getPullRequestDetail.ts) (core `state`/`merged` all three; GitLab adds mergeable + head-pipeline CI). `buildGitApiBaseUrl` maps GitLab `/api/v4` + Bitbucket Cloud `/2.0`; all request construction is unit-tested. Routes are reachable (no provider gate); `unsupported`→501 only for unknown providers / Bitbucket **Server**. **Residual:** (a) **live-provider validation** — request shapes are doc-derived + unit-tested but not yet run against real GitLab/Bitbucket creds; auth is `Bearer <token>` (modern GitLab PATs + Bitbucket Cloud access tokens — confirm vs an app-password if used). PR create is now idempotent on all three (a conflict resolves to the existing open PR/MR via `buildFindOpenPrUrl`, +unit-tested). (b) **rich-detail parity** — Bitbucket detail is state/merged only (no diffstat/build-statuses); GitLab lacks per-file additions/deletions (needs `/changes`). Fixing unblocks: verified non-GitHub PR create→merge + full diff/CI detail parity.

- **All three providers now cover the cloud-agent repo loop; only Bitbucket code-search + live-validation remain.** As of 2026-06-13 GitHub, GitLab, AND Bitbucket Cloud have read (`readRepoFile`/`listRepoFiles`/`listBranchDiff`), write (`commitFileToRepo`/`deleteFileFromRepo`), and PR lifecycle (`createPullRequest`/`mergePullRequest`/`getPullRequestDetail`) — all additive + unit-tested (Bitbucket write via the form-encoded `/src` API: branch forked off the base commit `hash`, deletion via the `files` field; branch diff via `/diffstat`). **Residual:** (a) **Bitbucket code search** — only GitHub + GitLab implement `searchRepoCode`; Bitbucket's is workspace-scoped (`/workspaces/:ws/search/code`, not repo-scoped) and Premium-gated, so it's deferred. (b) **live-provider validation** — the GitLab/Bitbucket request construction is doc-derived + unit-tested but not yet exercised against real GitLab/Bitbucket creds (auth `Bearer <token>`; confirm Bitbucket app-password vs access-token). (c) minor: GitLab/Bitbucket `commitUrl` is returned `null` (their write responses carry no html_url; a follow-up commit lookup would populate it). Fixing unblocks: Bitbucket code search + verified non-GitHub repo operations.

- **The agentHost PR-dispatch path still inserts a placeholder `pull_requests` row (null number) before the host calls back — minor residual.** The user-facing bug (a stale numberless placeholder surfacing over a real PR in `GET /tasks/:taskId/pull-request`) is FIXED [1280]: the GET now orders `number IS NOT NULL DESC, createdAt DESC`, and the merge route already 409s a null number. Residual cleanliness only: [RepoService.dispatchPrCreation](api/src/application/repos/RepoService.ts) could upsert on `(task, branch)` instead of insert so a never-arriving callback leaves no orphan row at all (cosmetic — nothing surfaces it now).

- **Post-merge build validation + auto-fix is GitHub-Actions-only and reuses the merged ticket branch.** This pass added: record `merge_sha` on the PR at every merge site; correlate the deploy-branch CI build back to the task by that SHA ([ingestRepoCiEvent.ts](api/src/application/ci/ingestRepoCiEvent.ts)); on failure, fetch the failed jobs/steps ([fetchBuildError.ts](api/src/application/ci/fetchBuildError.ts)) and auto-dispatch a fix run (capped at `MAX_AUTOFIX_ATTEMPTS=2` per task via `autofix.dispatch` telemetry count) through the new context-free `dispatchCloudRunForTask`. Remaining gaps: (a) the step-level error fetch only works for **GitHub Actions** (`workflow_run` → jobs API); Cloudflare Pages / `deployment_status` / `check_suite` events record the pass/fail status + run URL but no failed-step detail, so a fix run on those gets a URL-only error summary. (b) The fix run reuses the SAME `builderforce/task-<id>` branch (already merged) rather than a fresh `-fix-<n>` branch — the new PR shows only the post-merge diff (works), but the branch history is a bit unclean and the CI-correlation regex assumes one branch per task. (c) `build_status` only populates for PRs whose merge we recorded a `merge_sha` for — PRs merged before this pass (or merged directly on the provider) won't validate. (d) Full step LOGS (the actual error text) are a zip we don't unpack in the Worker — the agent gets job/step names, not the stack trace; piping a trimmed log tail would improve fix quality. Fixing unblocks: build validation for non-GitHub-Actions CI, cleaner fix branches, and richer fix prompts.

- **No pre-`finish` completeness/self-review loop for cloud agents — the prompt is the only guard against premature finish.** Execution #20 had the V2 cloud agent write a single stub file then call `finish`. This pass tightened the system prompt + `finish` tool description ([runtimeRoutes.ts](api/src/presentation/routes/runtimeRoutes.ts)) to forbid finishing with stubs/unimplemented requirements, and removed the auto-merge so an incomplete run now lands in an OPEN PR for human review instead of on `main` (the real safety net). But there is no programmatic check that the deliverables are complete before `finish` is honored (e.g. a reviewer pass, a "no TODO/placeholder" lint, or PRD-requirement coverage). Fixing (a self-review step that re-prompts the agent to verify each PRD requirement is met before accepting `finish`, or a cheap static placeholder scan that rejects `finish` and continues the loop) unblocks: cloud runs that reliably produce complete changes, not scaffolds. Deferred as a larger per-run-token investment.

- **The serverless durable executor has no real V2 (Claude Agent SDK) engine — a V2 agent with no live runtime now FAILS LOUDLY instead of silently running gemini.** Root cause of the reported "I kicked off Coder Agent V2 and the logs show BuilderForce Cloud (default)" (execution #26): the durable Worker loop ([runCloudToolLoop](api/src/presentation/routes/runtimeRoutes.ts)) only ever calls `ideProxy().complete()` with the gateway-default model + a 4-tool set and never branches on `engine`, while `dispatchAndQueue`/`startDispatchedExecution` forwarded `agent.engine` only to the *host* dispatch message, never to `CloudRunnerDO`/the Worker fallback. So any V2 agent that landed on the durable surface (its `container` runtime offline, or `runtime_surface:'durable'`) ran the V1 gemini tool-loop and — when no `cloudAgentRef` reached the API — was attributed to the `__default__` bucket. **Fixed this pass:** (a) frontend [RunAgentControl](frontend/src/components/task/RunAgentControl.tsx) now takes `cloudAgentRef` straight from the selected target string, not only from the loaded pool, so a selected agent's identity is never lost; (b) `startDispatchedExecution` now refuses the durable fallback for any `engine !== 'builderforce-v1'`, recording an attributed `runtime.unavailable` event + FAILED status ([failCloudEngineUnavailable](api/src/presentation/routes/runtimeRoutes.ts)) telling the user to bring an agent-runtime host / Container online. **Still missing:** an actual serverless V2 executor — i.e. drive the Claude Agent SDK loop from the durable surface via the gateway `/llm/v1/messages` bridge (with the V2 toolset), so a V2 agent can run cloud-only without a self-hosted runtime. Until then V2 strictly requires a long-lived runtime. Fixing unblocks: V2 agents runnable on the serverless surface instead of only failing when no runtime is online. Ties to PRD 09 engine-parity gaps.

- **Cloud loop has no code execution, so verification is CI-only — now made honest, not fabricated.** Execution #26 also exposed that the agent invented a `run_code` tool (got `unknown tool 'run_code'`), then declared *"I am confident the typecheck will now pass"* and opened a PR without running anything. The Worker executor has no shell and cannot run builds/tests. **Mitigated this pass:** a defined `run_checks` tool that honestly states checks run in CI on the PR; a system-prompt clause forbidding any claim that a check passed; an [assertsUnrunVerification](api/src/presentation/routes/runtimeRoutes.ts) honesty gate that blocks a `finish` summary asserting a check passed (once) to force an honest restatement; and an always-on "⚠ Not verified in-agent" annotation on both the opened PR body and the run output. **Still heuristic:** the gate is a narrow regex (clear fabrications only); borderline "should resolve the errors" phrasing isn't blocked (the annotation covers it). A structured `finish({ verified: false })` contract + the green-gate (`CLOUD_AUTOMERGE_REQUIRE_GREEN`) are the durable fixes. Fixing unblocks: cloud PRs that never present unrun checks as passing.

- **Execution #26 likely opened an INVALID fix (PR #12 on Fix-Faster-LLC/hired.video) — repo-state cleanup, not code.** The gemini fallback added `.ts` extensions to relative imports in `api/src/db/schema/localizations.ts`. TypeScript NodeNext/ESM requires `.js` specifiers even for `.ts` sources (`allowImportingTsExtensions` is editor-only), so the change probably does not compile — and nothing verified it (see above). The PR should be closed or corrected; this is operator repo state outside this workspace. Fixing unblocks: not shipping a non-compiling change merged on the agent's unverified word.

- **[ANALYZED 2026-06-13 — likely-correct failover, not drift; needs exec-#26 trace to close] Gateway model-id prefix `googleai/gemini-2.5-flash-lite` (step 0) vs `google/gemini-2.5-flash-lite` (steps 1+) within one run.** Re-analysis: `googleai/*` (direct Google AI, [vendors/googleai.ts](api/src/application/llm/vendors/googleai.ts), in `PREMIUM_FALLBACK_MODELS` [LlmProxyService.ts](api/src/application/llm/LlmProxyService.ts)) and `google/*` (Google **via OpenRouter**) are TWO DISTINCT upstream vendors. `vendorForModel()` ([vendors/registry.ts](api/src/application/llm/vendors/registry.ts)) already keys cooldown + cost to the correct separate vendor for each prefix, so the "split accounting" is *correct* (two real upstreams), and force-normalizing the prefix would WRONGLY merge them. The per-step prefix change is the cascade failing over between the two Google routes — expected behavior — UNLESS the run had a strict model pin that a later step violated. Closing requires the execution-#26 `llm.complete` trace (operator/data-gated) to confirm pin-vs-failover; no code change is warranted under the failover reading. Fixing the pin path (if confirmed) unblocks: strict-pinned runs never silently swapping Google upstreams mid-run.

- **Card/List `ViewToggle` rollout skipped a few non-tabular / delegated surfaces.** This pass added the shared [ViewToggle](frontend/src/components/ViewToggle.tsx) + [dataTableStyles](frontend/src/components/dataTableStyles.ts) to all primary data-list pages (projects, dashboard, content-manager, prompts, workforce, members, api-keys, logs, approvals, admin users/tenants, llm-traces, marketplace, skills, personas, contributors, shoutouts, showcase, integrations, agent skills). **Not converted:** (a) [chats/page.tsx](frontend/src/app/chats/page.tsx) — the conversation sidebar is a messaging UI, not a tabular record set, so a List view was judged inapplicable; (b) [settings/page.tsx](frontend/src/app/settings/page.tsx) Connected Accounts / Active Sessions / Admin Access sections — still card-only with no toggle; (c) the **assigned** tab on skills/personas, which delegates to `SkillAssignmentsContent` / `PersonaAssignmentsContent` — the `ViewToggle` is hidden there and those child components have no table view; (d) [TaskMgmtContent](frontend/src/components/TaskMgmtContent.tsx) keeps its own **Board/List** switch (not relabeled to Card/List) since it already offers dual views. Fixing (decide whether settings sections + the assigned tabs warrant a list view, and whether TaskMgmt's Board/List should be unified under the shared `ViewToggle` vocabulary) unblocks: fully uniform view-switching vocabulary across every surface.

- **Agent card/badge/price/skill rendering was consolidated; the non-agent marketplace listings and the table chrome were not.** This pass extracted shared agent primitives — [AgentCard](frontend/src/components/workforce/AgentCard.tsx) (owned/purchased/marketplace variants), [AgentOwnerActions](frontend/src/components/workforce/AgentOwnerActions.tsx), [AgentTypePill](frontend/src/components/AgentTypePill.tsx), [StatusBadge](frontend/src/components/StatusBadge.tsx) (+ `.badge-muted` in [globals.css](frontend/src/app/globals.css)), [SkillTags](frontend/src/components/SkillTags.tsx), [formatAgentPrice](frontend/src/lib/agentPresentation.ts) — and rewired [WorkforceAgents](frontend/src/components/workforce/WorkforceAgents.tsx) (card + list) and the marketplace workforce section onto them. **Still duplicated:** (a) the marketplace **main listings** (personas/skills/content) in [marketplace/page.tsx](frontend/src/app/marketplace/page.tsx) re-inline their own price formatting, type badges, and tag-pill slicing — `formatAgentPrice`/`SkillTags` are agent-typed but the same rules apply to artifacts; (b) there is still no shared `<DataTable columns rows />` — every list view (marketplace ×2, showcase, integrations, skills, WorkforceAgents) hand-writes its own `<thead>/<tbody>` against [dataTableStyles](frontend/src/components/dataTableStyles.ts). Fixing (generalize the price/tag helpers to an artifact-agnostic shape and introduce a `DataTable` that owns thead/tbody) unblocks: one row-rendering path for every collection page, not just agents.

- **No `GOOGLE_API_KEY` (nor `NVIDIA`/`CEREBRAS`/`OLLAMA`/`CLOUDFLARE` keys) bound in production — the cascade is OpenRouter-only.** [wrangler.toml](api/wrangler.toml) documents only `OPENROUTER_API_KEY` + `_PRO` as secrets. Consequence: the two `googleai/*` entries in [`PREMIUM_FALLBACK_MODELS`](api/src/application/llm/LlmProxyService.ts) are always skipped (key-unbound), every non-OpenRouter free model in the pool is dead weight, and the *only* paid safety net is OpenRouter-routed Gemini — a single upstream with no vendor diversity. The new guaranteed backstop (`GUARANTEED_BACKSTOP_MODEL`, this pass) leans entirely on `OPENROUTER_API_KEY_PRO` having credit; if that key lacks paid balance the backstop 402s and the request still hard-fails. Fixing (`wrangler secret put GOOGLE_API_KEY` so direct Gemini becomes a vendor-diverse backstop, confirm `OPENROUTER_API_KEY_PRO` is a credited key, and document the optional free-vendor keys) unblocks: real multi-vendor failover instead of a single-upstream dependency, and a backstop that can't 402.

- **LLM trace capture is wired for the gateway chat route and IDE chat, but not brain / dataset-gen / agent-inference callers.** [traceLogger.logTrace](api/src/application/llm/traceLogger.ts) is invoked from [llmRoutes.ts](api/src/presentation/routes/llmRoutes.ts) (`/v1/chat/completions`) and [ideAiRoutes.ts](api/src/presentation/routes/ideAiRoutes.ts) (`/api/ai/chat`). Other internal `ideProxy(...).complete()` callers — [BrainService](api/src/application/brain/BrainService.ts), the workforce agent inference endpoint, dataset generation, and `/v1/images/generations` in [llmRoutes.ts](api/src/presentation/routes/llmRoutes.ts) — still pass through the proxy (so a `traceId` is minted and the cooldown/failover path runs) but never call `logTrace`, so those calls are invisible in the superadmin trace view. Fixing (thread `newTraceId()` + `logTrace` through each remaining caller with the right `surface` label — `brain` / `agent` / `dataset-gen` / `image`) unblocks: full-surface diagnostic coverage, not just the public gateway.

- **A cloud run still targets exactly ONE repo — no multi-repo *spanning* for a task whose change crosses repositories.** Run-time repo *selection* shipped (a task pins `tasks.explicit_repo_id` via [migration 0110](api/migrations/0110_task_explicit_repo.sql); [resolveDefaultRepoForTask](api/src/application/repos/resolveDefaultRepo.ts) now delegates to the pure [resolveRepoForTask](api/src/application/repos/resolveRepo.ts) — explicit pin → inferred-by-matchHints → single default, falling back to the legacy default/most-recent pick so nothing regresses; the [RunAgentControl](frontend/src/components/task/RunAgentControl.tsx) picker, shown when a project has >1 repo, sends `repoId` in the run payload, validated + stamped at dispatch so the run/finalize/CI/PRD all use the same repo). The picker's repo list is served through the read-through cache (`project-repos:<tenant>:<project>`, invalidated on every repo CRUD route). **Still open:** a single run cannot edit MULTIPLE repos at once — the ticket model is one branch (`builderforce/task-<id>`) → one PR → one repo, so a task that legitimately spans repos (e.g. shared types in repo A + consumer in repo B) needs N branches/PRs and a loop that resolves a repo per file/sub-task. Fixing (a per-task repo *set* with a branch+PR per repo, and a loop that routes each write to the right repo via matchHints/pathGlobs) unblocks: cross-repo changes in one run. Lower priority — the common case (wrong single repo bound) is now fixed by selection. Related to the "happy-path validated" (PRD 09) entry above.

- **CI/deploy auto-merge: the safety follow-ups remaining after this pass.** The build/deploy feedback loop now exists — [githubWebhookRoutes.ts](api/src/presentation/routes/githubWebhookRoutes.ts) ingests `check_suite`/`check_run`/`workflow_run`/`deployment_status`/`status` and [ingestRepoCiEvent](api/src/application/ci/ingestRepoCiEvent.ts) correlates them to the task's latest execution and records a `ci.*`/`deploy.status` `tool_audit_event` (visible on the run's Logs/Timeline). An opt-in **merge-only-on-green** gate (`CLOUD_AUTOMERGE_REQUIRE_GREEN`, [cloudAutoMergeRequiresGreen](api/src/application/repos/mergeBranchToBase.ts)) defers the immediate merge to a green CI/deploy webhook. **Still open:** (a) requires the *target* repo to have a webhook → `/api/webhooks/github` with those events + `GITHUB_WEBHOOK_SECRET` set (no auto-provisioning); (b) a **failed** deploy is recorded but only surfaces in Logs/Timeline — there's no task-card badge or `needs_attention` flag (would need a status column on the task/execution); (c) when the gate is on and no CI ever runs, the ticket branch is left open and never merges (no timeout/fallback). Fixing unblocks: a hard failure signal on the board, not just in the timeline. Ties to PRD 09 GAP-W6.

- **V1 cloud loop still auto-merges UNVERIFIED code when the green-gate is off (the operator default).** With `CLOUD_AUTOMERGE_REQUIRE_GREEN` unset, the shell-less V1 loop merges best-effort edits straight to the deploy branch without compiling/testing. The opt-in gate (above) is the mitigation; routing test-gated tasks to V2 (which has Bash) is the other. Fixing (make the green-gate the default once the webhook is provisioned everywhere, or add a provider-side "trigger CI + poll" pre-merge check) unblocks: no unverified code reaching `main` by default.

- **Host-scoped Logs/Timeline aren't execution-filtered, so a V2/host run's panel shows ALL the host's events, not just the selected run.** V2 telemetry now persists with `execution_id` (the cloud `/agents/:ref/tool-audit?executionId=` path filters precisely), but the host path `GET /api/agent-hosts/:id/tool-audit` ([agentHostRoutes.ts](api/src/presentation/routes/agentHostRoutes.ts)) only filters by `runId`/`sessionKey`, and the panel uses host scope (not the executionId-filtered cloud path) when `execution.agentHostId` is set. So a V2 run's Logs/Timeline include the host's other runs. Fixing (add an `executionId` filter to the host tool-audit GET + have the panel use it for host scope, or route the panel's per-execution Logs/Timeline through the execution-scoped cloud endpoint regardless of host vs cloud) unblocks: per-execution precision for V2/host runs to match V1.

- **[TOKENS FIXED 2026-06-13] Streaming traces — response-body capture is the remaining half.** Token back-fill DONE [1298]: the gateway chat stream's `onUsage` callback now calls `backfillTraceUsage` ([traceLogger.ts](api/src/application/llm/traceLogger.ts)) → `UPDATE llm_traces SET prompt/completion/total_tokens WHERE trace_id`, so a streamed trace shows real token counts instead of 0 (was logged up-front at 0). **Residual:** the completion `response_body` is still null for streams — capturing it needs tee-ing the stream into a buffer (the higher-risk half; tokens were the higher-value one). Also `ideAiRoutes.ts` streams aren't back-filled yet (only the gateway chat path). Fixing the body-tee unblocks: full streamed-call diagnostics.

- **Project Calendar/Gantt views are read-only and derive deadlines from tasks — no in-view editing and no project-level date column.** This pass added Calendar + Gantt view modes to the projects page ([ProjectCalendar](frontend/src/components/ProjectCalendar.tsx), [ProjectGantt](frontend/src/components/ProjectGantt.tsx), shared [projectSchedule.ts](frontend/src/lib/projectSchedule.ts)/[ScheduleLegend](frontend/src/components/ScheduleLegend.tsx)), wired through the now-generic [ViewToggle](frontend/src/components/ViewToggle.tsx). A project has no date column of its own, so [GET /api/projects](api/src/presentation/routes/projectRoutes.ts) derives `startDate` (min task start, falling back to min due) and `dueDate` (max task due) by aggregating non-archived `tasks` rows. **Scope cuts:** (a) the views are display-only — there's no drag-to-reschedule or click-to-set-deadline, so changing a timeline still means editing individual task dates in the task UI; (b) the derived range recomputes on every list fetch with a `min/max ... group by project_id` aggregate that is NOT run through the read-through cache (`getOrSetCached`) the perf rule mandates — at high project/task counts this is an uncached fan-over-tasks scan on the hot `/api/projects` path; (c) the Calendar plots only the deadline (`dueDate`) as a single-day pill and does not render multi-day spans across the grid the way the Gantt does. Fixing (cache the per-project date aggregate keyed by a tenant task-version token invalidated on task write; add an editable mode that PATCHes task dates from the timeline; optionally a true project-level milestone/deadline column) unblocks: cached timeline reads, in-place rescheduling, and a project-owned deadline independent of task data. The View-Toggle vocabulary note (TaskMgmt's Board/List) in the rollout entry above also now applies to these two new modes.

- **Agent-host liveness depends on the 5-min heartbeat; the relay DO / WS path does not refresh `lastSeenAt` on its own.** The online-status fix ([onlineStatus.ts](api/src/domain/agentHost/onlineStatus.ts)) treats a host with a stale `lastSeenAt` (>15 min) as OFFLINE even while its socket is up, so liveness now hinges entirely on the periodic HTTP heartbeat landing. This pass found the agent-runtime relay ([builderforce-relay.ts](agent-runtime/src/infra/builderforce-relay.ts)) targets `/api/agentNodes/:id/{upstream,heartbeat,assignment-context}`, a path the worker never mounted (only `/api/agent-hosts` + the `/api/claws` alias) — so the heartbeat was 404ing and `lastSeenAt` only moved on (re)connect. Mitigated this pass by adding an `/api/agentNodes` back-compat route mount in [index.ts](api/src/index.ts) so heartbeats now land. **Still open:** (a) the runtime/worker naming is now triplicated (`claws`/`agent-hosts`/`agentNodes`) and should converge on one — repoint the runtime to `/api/agent-hosts` and drop both aliases; (b) the WS `/upstream` handler ([agentHostRoutes.ts](api/src/presentation/routes/agentHostRoutes.ts)) sets `lastSeenAt` only at connect, and the [AgentHostRelayDO](api/src/infrastructure/relay/AgentHostRelayDO.ts) never bumps it — add a periodic `lastSeenAt` touch on the live socket as defense-in-depth so a host stays ONLINE even if the HTTP heartbeat is blocked. Fixing unblocks: liveness that doesn't silently depend on one easily-misrouted heartbeat call.

- **Gateway prompt caching covers the Anthropic family only — Gemini relies on implicit caching, no explicit breakpoints.** [promptCaching.ts `modelSupportsExplicitCaching`](api/src/application/llm/promptCaching.ts) deliberately gates to `anthropic/*` / `claude` ids (the only OpenRouter upstreams that *require* an explicit marker and are known to honour it without a 400). `google/*` (via OpenRouter) and the direct `googleai` vendor cache implicitly above the model minimum, so they get *some* caching for free — but explicit breakpoints would give tunable placement and a higher hit rate on long stable prefixes. Held back to avoid 400s on providers that reject the unknown `cache_control` field. Fixing (extend the gate + a per-vendor allowlist once Gemini-via-OpenRouter explicit-cache behaviour is confirmed against a live call) unblocks: tunable Gemini prompt caching, not just whatever the provider caches implicitly.

- **Cloud Worker agent toolset is minimal (write_file/finish) and V1 self-hosted (pi) tool events may still be relay-only.** This pass made both cloud engines genuinely *execute tools*: [runCloudExecution](api/src/presentation/routes/runtimeRoutes.ts) now runs a real tool loop ([runCloudToolLoop](api/src/presentation/routes/runtimeRoutes.ts), up to 6 steps) where the model calls provider-API-backed tools — `write_file` commits to the ticket branch as a pending change ([commitFileAsPendingChange.ts](api/src/application/repos/commitFileAsPendingChange.ts) → opens a PR) and `finish` ends the run — emitting an `llm.complete` + per-tool event each step (migration 0092 columns). V2's agent-runtime SDK loop now *persists* its tool calls too: [builderforce-relay.ts `persistToolAudit`](agent-runtime/src/infra/builderforce-relay.ts) POSTs each `onToolUse` to the agent-host tool-audit ingest (Bearer agent-host key) instead of live-relay-only. **Residual:** (a) the Worker toolset has only `write_file`/`finish` — no `read_file`/`search`/`run_tests`/`apply_patch`, so the cloud Worker agent can write but not inspect the repo or self-verify; richer tools need a read path through the provider contents API. (b) The V1 self-hosted **pi** coding loop's tool calls are not confirmed to flow through `persistToolAudit`/the ingest — only V2's `onToolUse` was wired this pass; verify whether pi emits `tool.audit` only over the relay (live, non-durable) and wire it the same way if so. Fixing unblocks: cloud agents that can read+verify their own work, and durable timelines for V1 self-hosted runs.

- **Cloud log view is polled, not streamed.** Cloud agents have no live relay socket, so the unified Log view derives cloud log lines from polled tool-audit telemetry with a manual "Refresh cloud" button ([ObservabilityContent.tsx](frontend/src/components/ObservabilityContent.tsx)) rather than a live tail. Self-hosted hosts still stream live over the relay WS. Fixing (a per-execution cloud log stream — the cloud equivalent of `logs.subscribe`, e.g. an SSE/WS tail of the execution's events) unblocks: live cloud logs without a refresh button. (Note: `/timeline` now renders the D3 [ExecutionTimelineChart](frontend/src/components/ExecutionTimelineChart.tsx) via `ObservabilityContent` and is the intended timeline visual; the sidebar links `/observability`, which holds the same chart behind the Log/Timeline toggle.)

- **builderforce-memory's `CachingBridge`/`ResponseCache` (response-level cache) is still unused by the gateway and agent-runtime — separate mechanism from this pass's prompt caching.** This pass added Anthropic *prompt* caching (provider-side prefix reuse, billed at ~0.1x). It does **not** touch [builderforce-memory's CachingBridge / ResponseCache](../builderforce-memory/packages/memory/src/bridges/CachingBridge.ts) (an SSM-embedding-keyed response cache that returns a stored completion without an upstream call at all). The two are complementary: prompt caching discounts the input of calls that still happen; response caching elides the call entirely on a semantic hit. Fixing (wire `CachingBridge`/`ResponseCache` into the gateway read path for idempotent/low-temperature `useCase`s, with the same version-token invalidation the project's read-through cache uses) unblocks: zero-cost responses on repeated/near-duplicate prompts, on top of the per-call prompt-cache discount.
